21A	ncRNA 21A	Characteristics	~300 nucleotide, nonpolyadenylated, RNAP III transcript. . SINE (short interspersed nucleotide element - AluJb). 21A lacks the Alu-specific intragenic consensus elements needed to promote its pol III transcription such as the blocks A and B, which points to transcription driven by an extragenic type 3 pol III promoter.. Very low free energy (deltaG) value (deltaG < -100) indicating strong secondary structure.
21A	ncRNA 21A	Expression	Nuclear localisation. Detected in tested cultured cells such as HeLa and skin fibroblast cells.. The level of 21A transcription was very low in three immortalized, fully proliferating cell lines (HeLa, 293T, and LAN5) compared to unproliferating/resting PBL (peripheral blood lymphocyte) cells. Similarly, the 21A RNA level in primary skin fibroblasts was higher than in 293T cells, reinforcing an inverse correlation between endogenous 21A expression and cell proliferation. 
21A	ncRNA 21A	Function	21AS is one of a number of RNAP III-transcribed short ncRNAs that have sequence complementarity to protein-coding genes, possibly acting as as a natural trans-chromosomal antisense RNA. Aligned to the human genome, it shows several homology hits, among which the most highly significant were associated to multiple intronic regions of centromeric protein F gene (CENP-F). In vitro over-expression of 21AS transcripts inhibits CENP-F protein accumulation and decreased levels of CENP-F mRNA, indicating that 21AS regulates CENP-F expression in trans.. 21A RNAs has a role in the control of the proliferation of human tumor cell lines, possibly via regulation of CENP-F expression. This effect was not observed in a mouse cell line.
21A	ncRNA 21A	Conservation	Similarly to all of the 7SL/Alu-derived elements, 21A is primate-specific.
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Characteristics	~330 nt in vertebrates*. Transcribed by RNAP III, GC-rich sequence forming conserved secondary structures  (especially 3' and 5' stem-loop motifs).. 7SK RNA is capped at its 5' end by BCDIN3, a specific methylase methylphosphate capping enzyme (MePCE) (Jeronimo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643375). . RNAP II was recently found to bind near 7SK promoter, as well as many other known Pol III genes, suggesting that RNAP II may also play a role in regulating their transcription (Raha (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20139302).. *In invertebrates, 7SK homologs may have different sizes (such as >400 nt and ~130 nt in drosophilids and nematodes, respectively). (Gruber (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18566019) (Marz (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19734296)
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Expression	Nuclear, highly abundant (one of the most abundant small RNAs in vertebrate cells), first isolated from HeLa nuclear extracts, but ubiquitously expressed.. RNA sequencing from 11 humans tissues confirmed ubiquitous high expression of 7SK with expression in some tissues being higher than any mRNA (Castle (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20668672). 
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Function	Controls RNAP II activity by inhibiting P-TEFb elongation factor, which is a cdk-cyclin kinase that functions as both a general and an HIV-1 Tat-specific transcription factor (Nguyen (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11713533) (Yang (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11713532), with an impact on cell growth and differentiation.. 7SK snRNA is a central scaffold that coordinates protein-protein interactions and, by inhibiting P-TEFb kinase-mediated CTD phosphorylation, regulates RNAP II elongation (Nguyen (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11713533). 7SK snRNP (composed of 7SK snRNA, Hexim1, Larp7/Pip7S, and the P-TEFb subunits CycT1 and Cdk9) is not only critical for controlling transcription, but also for regulating alternative splicing coupled to transcription elongation (Barboric (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19416841). It is also essential for vertebrate development (Barboric (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19416841). The 3' end of HIC mRNA has full activity and contains a predicted structure resembling the 3'-terminal hairpin of 7SK that is critical for P-TEFb binding (Barboric (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19416841).. 7SK has been found highly enriched in isolated chromatin fractions, which may be related to its role in transcriptional regulation (Mondal (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20404130).. At an early stage of the HIV transcription cycle, elongation is prevented as P-TEFb is recruited to the HIV-1 promoter in a catalytically inactive state bound to the 7SK snRNP and also the Tat trans-activator of transcription protein. The inhibitory 7SK snRNP may be displaced by the nascent TAR HIV RNA that also binds Tat protein, activating P-TEFb kinase and transcriptional elongation (D'Orso (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20562857). Displacement of 7SK may also be performed by cellular RNAs, as indicated by the 3'-untranslated region (~300-nt) of HIC mRNA, which forms complexes with P-TEFb and is necessary and sufficient for stimulation of P-TEFb-dependent transcription of the HIV promoter (Young (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17925858).. 7SK RNA also inhibits APOBEC3C deaminase activity and sequesters it to the nucleolus, suggesting broader role for 7SK RNA in regulating key nuclear functions (He (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17381310).
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Conservation	Highly conserved throughout jawed vertebrates (but in lamprey it differs in 32% of its sequence from the mammalian 7SK (GÃ¼rsoy (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10824089)), and has a few conserved sequence and structure motifs over longer evolutionary distances. Homologs have been identified in deuterostome invertebrates and in two protostome phyla (mollusks and annelids) (Gruber (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18193315). More recently, it has also been detected in arthropods, showing that two highly structured conserved domains (5'- and 3'-stem regions) were present in the bilaterian ancestor (Gruber (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18566019), and even in nematode Caenorhabditis species (Marz (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19734296).
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Misc	The 7SK family contains a number of pseudogenes and derived repeats.. May be implicated in the transformation-dependent activation of oncogenes SV40 T-antigen and c-myc gene promoters (Krause (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9018369).
7SK	7-3 RNA, K-RNA, 7SK-RNA, 7SK snRNA, RN7SK	Name	RN7SK: RNA, 7SK small nuclear
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Characteristics	~300 nt, transcribed by RNAPIII. . The eukaryotic small cytoplasmic 7SL is an RNA component of the SRP (signal recognition particle), which associates with the ribosome and targets nascent proteins to the endoplasmic reticulum for secretion or membrane insertion (Walter (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6181418) (Zwieb (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15611297).
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Expression	Ubiquitously expressed at high levels. Localises to the cytoplasm. An expression profile from 11 human tissues using RNA sequencing showed 7SL was most highly expressed ncRNA and could be an order of magnitude more highly expressed than any mRNA (Castle (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20668672). 
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Function	7SL RNA is required for structural and functional properties of SRP (Walter (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6181418), being a scaffold component upon which the six proteins of the SRP bind in higher eukaryotes. In mammals SRP consists of the SRP RNA the six proteins named SRP9, SRP14, SRP19, SRP54, SRP68, and SRP72 (Walter (1983) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6196367).. Bacterial SRP has a much reduced complexity, consisting of a small SRP RNA (4.5S RNA) and a homolog of protein SRP54, also called Ffh or P48 (Bernstein (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8389475). In archaea only two SRP proteins, SRP19 and SRP54, are thought to be part of the SRP, although SRP RNA closely resembles the mammalian homolog (Bhuiyan (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10684931).. There is evidence that a highly conserved region of 7SL RNA catalyses the binding of SRP to its receptor SR, and that this RNA stimulates the GTPase activities of the SRP-SR complex (Zhang (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18617187) (Siu (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17164479) (Peluso (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10834842).
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Conservation	May have originated from the bacterial SRP (GTP-regulated ribonucleoprotein that targets secretory or membrane proteins during translation), it is ubiquitously present in eukaryotic cells and several viruses (Li (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6802847). The secondary structure of 7SL RNA is conserved from prokaryotes to distant eukaryotic species (Labuda (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7528809).
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Misc	7SL is the RNA ancestor of Alu transposon sequences, which emerged ~ 55 million years ago, are present specifically in primates and comprise ~10% of the human genome. Rodent B1 elements, as well as  4.5S and primate BC200 RNAs are also related to the terminal portions of 7SL RNA sequence (Labuda (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7528809) (Quentin (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7529207).
7SL	7S RNA, SRP RNA, 4.5S SRP RNA, 4.5S RNA, RN7SL1 RNA	Name	RN7SL1: RNA, 7SL, cytoplasmic 1
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Name	"adaptive response 33"
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Characteristics	1.46 and 0.99kb bands detected by Northern blot (Wang (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8806733).. Mouse 5430416N02Rik has 0.6 and 3.5 kb isoforms.
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Expression	Isolated from Chinese hamster ovary cell-derived HA-1 fibroblasts (Wang (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8806733).. Multiple stress-responsive gene. Hydrogen peroxide-inducible. Induction appears to be dependent on calcium, occurred as early as 90 min, and was maximal at 5h. Adapt33 induction by hydrogen peroxide is suggested to occur at the mRNA stability level, and stability analysis indicated a short half-life. (Wang (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12837039, Wang (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8806733). Cell fractionation revealed that a significant proportion of adapt33 RNA is associated with active translation in the polysomes. (Wang (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8806733). Analysis of expression following the stimulation of apoptosis with hydrogen peroxide and staurosporine indicated a strong correlation with the apoptosis response. (Wang (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12837039). In mouse probable homologue expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (ESCs) (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).. Mouse RNA found to be highly unstable with a half-life <2 hr in N2A (neuroblastoma) cells (Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755). 
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Function	Mouse RNA was found to interact with a number of chromatin binding protein/complexes in mouse embryonic stem cells including PRC1, PRC2, JARID1B, ESET, SUV39H1, SETD8 and	CBX1 with the general pattern being interaction with repressors of gene expression (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Conservation	Adapt33 sequence has homology to mouse AK017316.
Adapt33	5430416N02Rik (probable mouse homologue), linc1354	Misc	Adapt33 promoter constructs have strong activity in both hamster and human cells. (Wang (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12837039)
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Names	Antisense Igf2r RNA
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Characteristics	108 kb (unspliced). Transcribed from an antisense promoter located in intron 2 of the Igf2r (insulin-like growth-factor type-2 receptor) gene (Lyle (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10802648, Wutz (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9338788). . Also a number of spliced isoforms from 500bp to ~1.4kb (Seidl (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16874305).. Imprinted, expressed only from paternal allele (Wutz (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9338788, Lyle (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10802648).
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Function	Regulates genomic imprinting of a cluster of autosomal genes (Igf2r, Slc22a2 and Slc22a3) in cis, on mouse chromosome 17 (Sleutels (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11845212).  . Truncation of Air disrupts imprinting not only of Igf2r but also the nearby non-overlapping genes Slc22a2 and Slc22a3, leading to mice with a lower birth weight (Sleutels (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11845212).. Air RNA forms a "cloud" over the imprinted DNA locus, binding to chromatin. Recruits G9a histone methyltransferase to epigenetically silence Slc22a3 (Nagano (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18988810). Igf2r is not silenced by this mechanism.. Nb: Slc22a3 and Slc22a2 are only imprinted at a specific time point in placental development. Outside of this time point the Air "cloud"/ Air chromatin binding and repressive histone modification are not found on these gene loci (Nagano (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18988810). 
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Expression	Expressed during embryonic development, in the placenta (Wutz (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9338788, Lyle (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10802648), adult brain, lung and heart (Seidl (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16874305).. Expressed in glial cells of the developing brain but not in neurons, explains lack of Igf2r imprinting in these neurons. (Yamasaki (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16037066). Unspliced Air is unstable, localised to the nucleus. Spliced isoforms, found in nucleus and cytoplasm, are more stable (Seidl (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16874305).
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Conservation	All characterisation been carried out in mouse. Recently Air has been identified in human (Yotova (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18789384) but full length transcripts have yet to be characterised.
Air	Airn, IGF2RAS	Misc	Nb: Genebank and NCBI Gene sequences for Air are all for the spliced mouse isoforms. See http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/gene/104103. UCSC browser link below is for transcript variant 3 which covers a similar length to the unspliced transcript.
AK023948	None known	Features	AK023948 is embedded in the TG-SLA (thyroglobulin and Src-like adaptor) locus on chromosome 8q24, a susceptibility locus for papillary thyroid carcinoma (PTC). An unspliced cDNA, AK023948 is located in an intron of both the TG (sense orientation) and SLA (antisense) genes.. A 12 Kb haplotype containing 8 SNP markers for PTC is harboured in the TG-SLA locus, which also includes two additional putative noncoding RNA genes.. AK023948 (cDNA FLJ13886 fis, clone THYRO1001559) was cloned from thyroid gland and is 2,807b long (Ota (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14702039). The transcript is significantly down-regulated in most PTC tumors, thus representing a candidate susceptibility gene for PTC.
AK082072	linc-POLR3G-8	Characteristics	Intergenic, 2 exon transcript in mouse, with HeK4me3 chromtain mark at 5' (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. Human ortholog is linc-POLR3G-8 (Cabili (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21890647). Human ortholog has a number of splice isoforms with 3 or more exons.
AK082072	linc-POLR3G-8	Expression	Expressed in specific regions of embryonic and post-natal mouse brain (see Chodroff for details) including the rostal migratory stream at P3 with a âpotential association with inhibitory GABAergic neuronsâ (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. Expressed in opossum and chicken embryonic brains showing spatio-temporal conservation of expression (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).
AK082072	linc-POLR3G-8	Conservation	Highly conserved for a lincRNA 36.7% mouse transcript overlaps phastCons elements (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. Conserved in mammals and back to frog, although mouse exon 2 is not conserved in all orthologs (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. Opossum ortholog [GenBank:GU951678]. Frog and chicken ([GenBank: CX847574.1 and CR35248.1] respectively (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).
AK082072	linc-POLR3G-8	Misc	Mouse transcript contains Evofold-predicted RNA secondary structure (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. LncRNA transcripts in human from bidirectional promoter with TMEM161B (over 50kb upstream from linc-POLR3G-8 start site) can also share exons 2 and/or 3. See BC047059 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/BC047059.
Alpha 250/ Alpha 280	None known	Characteristics	Two overlapping antisense RNAs from intron 1 of the human ribosomal protein 14 (Rps14) gene, identified by RNase Protection Assay (RPA).. RPA expression analysis using both cell extracts and cell-free transcription system indicates full-length sizes of 250 and 280 nt, respectively. Transcripts terminate at the same nucleotide, therefore alpha-250 overlaps alpha-280 along its whole length.. Transcription of both RNAs is resistant to high concentrations of RNAPII inhibitor alpha-amanitin.
Alpha 250/ Alpha 280	None known	Expression	Ubiquitously expressed in the human tissues and cell lines examined. .  Alpha-250 was almost exclusively cytoplasmic. Alpha- 280 was mostly in the nucleus.
Alpha 250/ Alpha 280	None known	Function	Regulates RPS14 transcription.. Each lncRNA can interact with the Rps14 gene loci to stimulate its expression in-trans.. Each lncRNA is transcribed through a known enhancer with putative transcription factor binding abilities, suggesting the 'enhancer' may be the transcribed RNA, which could be recruiting transcription factors to the Rps14 gene. 
AncR-1	None known	Characteristics	Several splice isoforms. Main isoform is a 6-7kb transcript.
AncR-1	None known	Expression	Expressed in brain cortex (not ubiquitously expressed). Also differentially expressed between queens, drones and workers: detected in sex organs in queens and drones and in the hypopharyngeal glands and oenocytes of worker bees.. Localises to punctate foci in nucleus. Did not co-localise with the Ks-1 nuclear lncRNA.
AncR-1	None known	Conservation	Also present in another honey bee species: Apis cerana. Sequence was highly conserved but putative ORFs were not.. At time of study, AncR-1 sequence did not show homology to sequences from any other organisms
AncR-1	None known	Name	Apis noncoding RNA-1
AncR-1	None known	Misc	Nucleotide accessions of different isoforms: AB125322.1, AB125323.1, AB125324.1
ANRIL	CDKN2B-AS1, p15AS	Name	ANRIL: Antisense noncoding RNA in the INK4 locus;. CDKN2B-AS1: CDKN2B antisense RNA 1;. P15AS: P15 antisense RNA
ANRIL	CDKN2B-AS1, p15AS	Characteristics	Present in multiple splicing isoforms (Folkersen (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19888323) (such as the CDK2BAS RefSeq sequence NR_003529.3 of ~3.9kb). Also detected as an unspliced transcript of 34.8 kb (Yu (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18185590), specified as p15AS, but which seems to correspond to an isoform with the first intron of CDK2BAS retained. Antisense to the tumor suppressor gene p15/CDKN2A. (Yu (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18185590). Traverses a noncoding region centromeric to CDKN2A, a region containing the INK4b/ARF/INK4a locus and implicated in a range of complex diseases including cancer (such as melanoma-neural system tumor syndrome), type 2 diabetes, periodontitis and coronary heart disease (see extensive reference list in Literature below, and Popov (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20716961 for a review).. Transcript found to be quite unstable with a half-life >4 hr in human Hela cells (Tani (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22369889).
ANRIL	CDKN2B-AS1, p15AS	Expression	Expressed in tissues and cell types affected by atherosclerosis. Increased levels of ANRIL are found in patients carrying the atherosclerosis risk haplotype expression, including in peripheral blood mononuclear cells, whole blood and atherosclerotic plaque tissue, and the levels were directly correlated with the severity of atherosclerosis (Holdt (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20056914). . Up-regulated in prostate cancer (Yap (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20541999).
ANRIL	CDKN2B-AS1, p15AS	Function	In vitro over-expression of p15as/ANRIL RNA was originally demonstrated to induce epigenetic silencing of p15 gene expression (Yu (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18185590).. Recently, ANRIL RNA was found to interact and regulate chromobox 7 (CBX7), a component of the Polycomb Repressor Complex 1 (PRC1), which methylates histone H3 lysine 27 to promote epigenetic silencing, and is also up-regulated in prostate cancer. Interaction occurs with a conserved chromodomain of CBX7 and is essential for the ability of PRC1 to repress the INK4b/ARF/INK4a locus and control cell senescence. (Yap (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20541999)
anti-NOS2A	None known	Characteristics	RNA estimated at ~1.9kb. anti-NOS2A has homology to the NOS2A protein coding gene (NOS2: Nitric oxide synthase 2 enzyme), only a small part ~100-nt is antisense to NOS2A. Homology stretches from intron14/exon15 to exon19/intron19. Formed by partial duplication of NOS2A followed by an inversion of part of the duplicated sequence to form a ~4kb locus in human.. PolyA- RNA. Intronless (NOS2A introns now part of the anti-NOS2A exon).. Expressed from a hypothesized internal promoter.
anti-NOS2A	None known	Expression	Expressed in brain cancer. . Expressed in hESCs (at a higher level than NOS2A) but down-regulated ~7 fold in neurospheres, while NOS2A showed a reciprocal expression pattern.
anti-NOS2A	None known	Function	Reciprocal regulation with NOS2A could suggest a regulatory role for the antisense transcript but this has yet to be tested.
anti-NOS2A	None known	Conservation	Found in primates but not in rodents.
anti-NOS2A	None known	Misc	Nb: Precise genomic location and sequence of anti-NOS2A was not provided by Korneev et al.. Anti-NOS2A was identified as belonging to contig AC053481 and homologous sequence within this contig (including evidence of an invesrsion) can be found at ~chr17:57,692,139-57,696,081 in HG18, but this does not exactly define the transcript identified by Korneev et al.
antiPeg11	antiRtl1, PEG11as	Characteristics	Antisense transcript to Peg11/Rtl1. Peg11 is a retrotransposon-like protein coding gene (Charlier (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11337479, Byrne (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20072617).. Reciprocal imprinting: antiPeg11 maternally expressed whereas Rtl1/Peg11 is paternally expressed. (Charlier (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11337479, Seitz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12796779, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. antiPeg11 contains 5 maternally expressed miRNAs (4 found in mammals, 1 specific to rodents, 1 specific to non-rodents) (Seitz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12796779,	Davis (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15854907).. In humans these are mir-431, mir-433, mir-127, mir-432 and mir-136. 
antiPeg11	antiRtl1, PEG11as	Expression	Peg11 is expressed in a number of tissues in mouse, while antiPeg11 expression is restricted mostly to embryos and adult brain. In brain it was expressed at a higher level than Peg11 (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. antiPeg11 miRNAs have a similar expression profile to the full length transcript (Davis (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15854907).. High expression of antiRtl1 in sheep skeletal muscle (Charlier (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11337479).. Full length, unspliced, unprocessed, transcript was around ~5kb, with smaller (likely processed) species also present (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).
antiPeg11	antiRtl1, PEG11as	Function	antiPeg11 binds the PRC2 chromatin modification complex (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. antiPeg11 miRNAs target Rtl1 (Davis (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15854907).
antiPeg11	antiRtl1, PEG11as	Conservation	Eutherian mammals (Davis (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15854907, Edwards (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18532878).. Suggested that anti-rtl1 has evolved as part of the parental conflict hypothesis where the maternally expressed antisense gene inhibits the paternally expressed (fetal growth promoting) gene (Davis (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15854907).
antiPeg11	antiRtl1, PEG11as	Misc	No full length antiPeg11 cDNAs have been cloned but there is a partial clone from mouse EU434921.1 which is given in the UCSC browser link below. This sequence "Begins at the end of miR-431 precursor and ends at the beginning of miR-127 precursor" (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. Like in mouse the exact nature of the transcript in other mammals is not known, human browser link below is to sequence defined by the microRNAs contained within antiPeg11, others are to Peg11.
antisense TGF beta 3	None known	Characteristics	~4.5kb antisense TGF beta 3 RNA
antisense TGF beta 3	None known	Expression	Expressed during heart development.. Showed slightly higher expression in AV, when epithelial to mesenchymal transformation is initiated compared to the quiesent cells in the ventricle. By contrast TGF beta3 PTC was ~5x more highly expressed.. Antisense transcript showed increasing expression over timepoints that correlated with the loss of ability for AV cells to undergo transformation, whereas TGF beta3 PTC peaked and declined during the transformation window.
antisense TGF beta 3	None known	Misc	Heart valve formation during heart development requires an epithelial to mesenchymal transformation of cells in the atrioventricular (AV) canal.. Sequence and precise genome location of the transcript has not been defined.
At4	TPSI family 	Characteristics	At4: member of a family of RNAs induced by phosphate (Pi) starvation in plants that have a region of complementarity to miR-399 and short non-conserved ORFs (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506, Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. Other family members in Arabidopsis are At4-1, At4-2, At4-3 and IPS1 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Detail.aspx?TKeyid=158 (Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506, Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. At4 is ~750nuc (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366).
At4	TPSI family 	Expression	Expression of At4 family members is induced upon Pi starvation (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. At4 is expressed in roots (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366) and shoots (MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795).. Hormonal signaling by cytokinins and abscisic acid repressed At4 expression in the roots (MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506).
At4	TPSI family 	Function	Loss of At4 lead to increased shoot Pi content and an increase in the shoot:root Pi ratio under low Pi conditions suggesting At4 affects Pi distribution and plant growth (Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506).. Competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). At4 has complementarity to miR-399, but contains a central mismatch loop. Over-expression of At4 lead to a decrease in shoot Pi content suggesting that, like IPS1, At4 inhibits miR-399 through target mimicry thereby allowing activity of PHO2 (Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. At4 and IPS1 appear to be functionally redundant as overexpression of one gave same phenotypic change as overexpression of both (Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).
At4	TPSI family 	Conservation	At4 and IPS1 are paralogs in Arabidopsis.. At4 only shares homology with other family members (ie: At4-1 and At4-2, Mt4 in Medicago truncatula and Mt4-like in Glycine max) in the miR-399 complementarity region (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506).
At4	TPSI family 	Misc	Accession for other family members:. At4-1: AY536062; At4-2: AY334555; At4-3: AI995459
B2 SINE RNA	None known	Characteristics	Short interspersed element (SINE) repeat present in more than 10^5 copies in the mouse genome (Kramerov (1979) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/370792). Repeat is ~180nuc long (Krayev (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6296779) but expressed B2 RNAs vary from ~0.2-0.6kb (Kramerov (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6130513,Fornace (1986) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2426659). . The 5' of B2 SINE is derived from a tRNA (Lawrence (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3839306, Daniels (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3851163) while the 3' contains an A rich sequence (Krayev (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6296779).. Transcribed by RNA polymerase III (Krayev (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6296779, Singh (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2581137).
B2 SINE RNA	None known	Expression	Expression highly induced upon viral infection (Singh (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2581137), heat shock (Fornace (1986) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2426659) and differentially regulated during development (Bachvarova (1988) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2461884).. Also shows higher expression in some tumour cells (Kramerov (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6130513).. Found in the nucleus (Espinoza (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15300239) and the cytoplasm (Kramerov (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6130513).
B2 SINE RNA	None known	Function	B2 SINE RNA is a specific inhibitor of RNA polymerase II (Allen (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15300240).. During heat shock B2 RNA associated with RNA polymerase II and repressed its action. Nb: Only saw association of B2 RNA with RNA polymerase II after heat shock. (Allen (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15300240).. Represses transcription by stably binding an RNA docking site on the core polymerase II complex and blocking activity of the RNA polymerase preinitiation complex (Espinoza (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15300239). To achieve this B2 RNA disrupts polymerase DNA binding at the promoter, preventing the formation of an active closed complex around the DNA (Yakovchuk (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19307572).. 51 nucleotide sequence from 3' half is sufficient for binding to and repressing RNA polymerase II (Espinoza (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17307818).
B2 SINE RNA	None known	Conservation	Rodents: mouse, rat, chinese hamster (Krayev (1982) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6296779)
B2 SINE RNA	None known	Misc	Known that upon heat shock RNA polymerase II is transiently repressed.. In humans Alu repeat RNAs appear to play the role B2 RNA does in rodents upon heat shock. Alu and B2 elements have different origins but show convergent evolution functionally.. B2 sequence provided is 177nt sequence specified by Espinoza et al. 2004 as mouse B2 RNA gene (region 121488-121665 of Mus musculus chromosome 18, clone RP23-6p18, GenBank accession number AC020972).
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Characteristics	~2 kb; two splice variants were identified for human and mouse BACE1-AS. Transcribed  from an intron of the beta-secretase-1 (BACE1) gene in antisense direction it also completely overlapps exon 6 of BACE-1 (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408).
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Expression	BACE1 and BACE1AS are co-expressed in a wide range of tissues and cell lines in mice and humans. BACE1 mRNA expression levels are higher than BACE1-AS levels across all tissues examined, except in Alzheimer's disease (AD) where, in contrast, BACE1-AS is expressed at a higher level in brain. Bace1 and Bace1-AS transcripts are also observed in various regions of the mouse brain (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408, Faghihi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20507594).. Several cell stressors, such as high temperature, serum starvation, amyloid-beta 1-42, H2O2 and high glucose, specifically increase BACE1-AS RNA and BACE1 protein levels (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408).. Showed increased expression in sporadic inclusion-body myositis (s-IBM) muscle fibers (possibly caused by endoplasmic reticulum stress). Nevertheless, unlike in AD and AD-transgenic mouse brain samples in which BACE1-AS transcript was increased more than the sense BACE1 transcript , in s-IBM muscle biopsies the reversed was found (Nogalska (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20236612).. Mouse RNA stability was very close to median for lncRNAs, with a half-life 3.6 hr in N2A (neuroblastoma) cells (Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755). 
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Function	BACE1AS expression is elevated in Alzheimers disease (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408). It was shown to regulate BACE1 mRNA and protein expression in vitro and in vivo ie: over-expression, shRNA and siRNA knockdown of BACE1AS affected BACE1 expression, influencing amyloid-beta 1-42 levels (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408).. It was proposed that BACE1-AS and BACE1 form an RNA duplex and this increases the stability of BACE1 (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408). More recently, it was suggested that BACE1AS may prevent translational repression of BACE1 mRNA by miR-485-5p via masking the binding site for the microRNA. Supporting this hypothesis, BACE1AS over-expression prevented miRNA-induced suppression (Faghihi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20507594). Expression of BACE1-AS as well as miR-485-5p are dysregulated in RNA samples from Alzheimer's disease subjects compared to control individuals (Faghihi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20507594). . BACE1-AS may also be involved in sporadic inclusion-body myositis (s-IBM), whose muscle-fiber phenotype shares molecular similarities with Alzheimer-disease brain (including increased BACE1 protein). BACE1-AS and BACE1 transcripts are significantly increased in s-IBM, and experimental induction of endoplasmic reticulum (ER) stress increased both BACE1-AS and BACE1 transcripts. These results suggest that ER stress and increased BACE1-AS expression may be involved in s-IBM (Nogalska (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20236612).
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Conservation	BACE1-AS transcript has been identified in mouse and humans, with a conserved association with BACE1 across species (Faghihi (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587408).
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Misc	Mouse AK078885 and human CB960709 full-length clones are unspliced and are ~1.2kb- and 798b-long, but two spliced variants were extended by RACE by Faghini et al., 2008.
BACE1AS	NCRNA00177, BACE1-AS; FJ573250	Name	BACE1 antisense RNA
BC1	None known	Characteristics	152 nt; evolved from a tRNA Ala (DeChiara (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2437583).
BC1	None known	Expression	Expressed by a specific subset of neurons in the central and peripheral nervous system; localises to dendrites (Tiedge (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1706516), or both axons and dendrites (Muslimov (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12040034, Centonze (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17699670) in different subsets of neurons and in a developmentally regulated manner. . Decreased expression in brains of mice that suffer chronic epileptic seizures (GitaÃ­ (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20974111).. Also expressed in germ cells (Muslimov (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12040034).. Dendritic localisation mediated by an extended stem loop element (Rozhdestvensky (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11350036) in 5' 62 nucleotides (Muslimov (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9169532), containing two targeting codes a stem bulge motif that specifies nuclear export and a GA kink-turn (KT) motif that binds heterogeneous nuclear ribonucleoprotein A2 and mediates transport to the distal ends of dendrites (Muslimov (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17074884).
BC1	None known	Function	Summary: Functions to regulate localised translation at dendrites, controlling neuron excitability and place learning. Lack of BC1 causes a susceptibility to epileptic seizures. . Binds eIF4A, eIF4B and PABP to repress translation initiation by blocking assembly of the 48S initiation complex (Wang (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12451124, Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957, Wang (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16330711, Kondrashov (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16154588, Lin (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316401).. Translational repression is mediated by its 3' domain and A rich region (Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957, Wang (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16330711, Kondrashov (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16154588).. Inhibits eukaryotic initiation factor 4A helicase by uncoupling ATPase activity from helicase/ duplex unwinding activity (Lin (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316401).. By regulating localised translation BC1 can control neuron excitability; . ie: by regulating dopamine receptor levels and dopamine signalling in the striatum (Centonze (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17699670) . ie: inhibiting translation activation from metabotropic glutamate receptor (mGluR) signalling (Zhong (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19675232). . Knock-out of BC1 in mouse affected exploratory behaviour and anxiety, leading to higher mortality in field experiments  (Skryabin (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12944471, Lewejohann (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15302134).. Brain phenotypes of BC1 knockout mice include neuronal hyperexcitability triggered by mGluR signaling or GABAa receptor stimulation which stimulates protein translation BC1 would act to repress (Zhong (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19675232, Zhong (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21124905). Epileptogenic susceptibility (epileptic activity and convulsive seizures) upon auditory stimulation (Zhong (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19675232, Zhong (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21124905) and defects in place learning (Zhong (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21124905). . The combination of BC1 and fragile X mental retardation protein (FMRP) knockouts causes neuronal excitability, epileptogenesis, and place learning deficits of increased severity than individual knockouts suggesting BC1 and FMRP act independently to repress translation (Zhong (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21124905).
BC1	None known	Conservation	Evolved from a tRNA Ala (DeChiara (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2437583).. Rodent specific (Martignetti (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7692450).. BC1, BC200 and G22 likely form a family of independently exapted repetitive elements which have evolved to carry out similar functions in different mammalian species (Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957, Khanam (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17175535, Lin (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316401). 
BC1	None known	Name	Brain Cytoplasmic RNA 1
BC200	BCYRN1 (brain cytoplasmic RNA 1)	Conservation	Anthropoid primates (monkeys, apes and humans) (Skryabin (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9847409).. BC200, BC1 and G22 likely form a family of independently exapted repetitive elements which have evolved to carry out similar functions in different mammalian species (Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957, Khanam (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17175535). 
BC200	BCYRN1 (brain cytoplasmic RNA 1)	Characteristics	200 nucleotide ncRNA (Tiedge (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7684772) exapted from an Alu element (Watson (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2444875). Transcribed by RNA polymerase III (Martignetti (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8265590).. Three structural domains, 5' that shares homology with Alu elements, a central A rich region and a 3' unique region (Tiedge (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7684772). 
BC200	BCYRN1 (brain cytoplasmic RNA 1)	Misc.	More than 200 pseudogenes reported (Kuryshev (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11399078).
BC200	BCYRN1 (brain cytoplasmic RNA 1)	Expression	Expressed predominantly in different regions of the brain. Also shows low level expression in testis but not in other normal tissues examined (Watson (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2444875, Tiedge (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7684772, Kuryshev (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11399078). RNA sequencing of 11 human tissues confirmed up-regulation of expression in brain (hypothalamus) and low or no expression elsewhere (Castle (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20668672).. Disregulated in cancer: expressed in a number of human tumours but not in corresponding normal tissue (Chen (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9422992). . Link with aging and Alzheimer disease: BC200 expression decreases with aging but is upregulated in Alzheimer's disease (AD). In AD affected brain regions, expression increased with disease severity. RNA localisation showed intense perikaryal staining, showing build up of RNA in cell body (Mus (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17553964). . Like BC1 ncRNA found in rodents, BC200 also suggested to localise to dendrites (Tiedge (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7684772).  
BC200	BCYRN1 (brain cytoplasmic RNA 1)	Function	Binds several proteins including the signal recognition particle SRP9/14 heterodimer (Kremerskothen (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9605471), eukaryotic initiation factor 4A helicase (eIF4A) (Lin (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316401) and Poly(A)-binding protein (PABP), binding to PABP requires the central A rich region (Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957)..    . Inhibits translation in-vitro and in cultured cells similar to BC1.  BC200 binding to eIF4A inhibits it by uncoupling eIF4A ATPase activity from its helicase/ duplex unwinding activity (Lin (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316401). Translational inhibition also involves BC200 binding to to PABP (Kondrashov (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16154588). 
Beta 2.7 RNA	Beta2.7, TRL4 DE RNA, lncRNA2.7	Characteristics	2.7kb transcript, encoded in the herpesvirus HCMV genome. Unspliced and polyadenylated (Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392).
Beta 2.7 RNA	Beta2.7, TRL4 DE RNA, lncRNA2.7	Expression	Beta2.7 kb transcript is found predominantly in the cytoplasm and does associate with polysomes (Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392, Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392)(McSharry (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12917473). It is an early transcript expressed upon infection (12 to 24 hours), and rapidly accumulated in infected cells, accounting to ~20% of viral RNA transcription (Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392, Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392).
Beta 2.7 RNA	Beta2.7, TRL4 DE RNA, lncRNA2.7	Function	Beta2.7 RNA has a fundamental role in preventing stress response and apoptosis of the host cell, by binding to components of the mitochondrial respiratory chain complex I (reduced nicotinamide adenine dinucleotideâubiquinone oxido-reductase). Beta2.7 specifically binds and prevents re-localization of essential complex I subunit genes associated with retinoid/interferon-induced mortality-19 (GRIMâ19), in response to apoptotic stimuli. This interaction is also important for stabilizing the mitochondrial membrane potential and the mitochondrial ATP production, preventing metabolic dysfunction, which is essential for completion of the virus' life cycle (Reeves (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17540903).. Beta2.7 transcripts have also been shown to protect endothelial cells from rat aorta against apoptosis during ischemia/reperfusion injury, which also involves complex I of the mitochondrial respiratory chain. Overexpression of beta2.7 RNA reduced reactive oxygen species production and inhibited apoptosis (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20036157).
Beta 2.7 RNA	Beta2.7, TRL4 DE RNA, lncRNA2.7	Misc	A potential open reading frame of 170 amino acids was identified close to the 5'-terminus of the gene (Greenaway (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2436392), but no protein product of this RNA has ever been detected in infected cells.
Beta 2.7 RNA	Beta2.7, TRL4 DE RNA, lncRNA2.7	Conservation	Beta2.7 sequence is highly conserved not only in HCMV clinical isolates but also in the common laboratory strains, demonstrating that the gene sequence was not substantially modified during prolonged in vitro passage (McSharry (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12917473).
Beta-globin transcripts	None known	Characteristics	>1 kb, intergenic RNAs transcribed from the beta-globin locus.
Beta-globin transcripts	None known	Expression	Dynamically expressed during erythroid cell development.. Nuclear localised.
Beta-globin transcripts	None known	Function	Intergenic transcripts (or their transcription) are believed to participate in the developmental switch of beta-globin cluster genes, with proposed roles in chromatin remodeling and long-range cis-activation. RNAs may be processed by RNAi machinery.
Beta-globin transcripts	None known	Conservation	N/A
Beta-globin transcripts	None known	Misc	N/A
Beta-MHC antisense transcripts	intergenic beta MHC RNA, beta RNA; MHC bII, aII and xII NATs	Characteristics	Originally described as a ~6-kb transcript that initiates in the intergenic region between the alpha and beta myosin heavy chain (MHC) genes, ~2 kb downstream of the beta-MHC gene and transcribed across the entire gene in the antisense orientation (Haddad (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12851393).. Natural antisense transcripts in the MHC cluster have been described forming three major products in rats, antisense to MHC IIa, IIx, and IIb genes. These antisense RNAs are named aII, xII, and bII NATs, respectively (Pandorf (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17030512). The aII NAT begins in the IIa-IIx intergenic region in close proximity to the IIx promoter, extends across the 27-kb IIa MHC gene, and continues to the IIa MHC gene promoter (Pandorf (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17030512).
Beta-MHC antisense transcripts	intergenic beta MHC RNA, beta RNA; MHC bII, aII and xII NATs	Expression	Expressed in cardiac muscle development (Haddad (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17982008). Increasingly expressed following birth or in response to increases in T3 (3,5,3'-triiodothyronine) thyroid hormone.. Expression is inversely correlated with beta-MHC levels: for example, expression of the antisense beta MHC RNA under altered thyroid state and in diabetes directly correlates with that of the alpha MHC mRNA, but negatively correlates with beta mRNA expression (Haddad (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12851393). . Negative correlation has also been observed between the beta MHC mRNA expression and the antisense beta-RNA in response to aortic constriction-induced pressure overload, in which the beta-MHC gene is up-regulated while the alpha-MHC gene is down-regulated (Haddad (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16415074).. Expression of MHC "aII" antisense is also up-regulated in muscles after spinal cord isolation (SI) in rats, and was negatively correlated with MHC IIa expression and positively correlated with MHC IIx gene expression (Pandorf (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17030512).
Beta-MHC antisense transcripts	intergenic beta MHC RNA, beta RNA; MHC bII, aII and xII NATs	Function	Proposed to negatively regulate beta-MHC expression to coordinate the cardiac transition marked by the switch from beta- to alpha-MHC, during early neonatal development, and in adult heart in response to diabetes and to hypothyroid state (Luther (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9632112) (Haddad (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17982008).
Beta-MHC antisense transcripts	intergenic beta MHC RNA, beta RNA; MHC bII, aII and xII NATs	Conservation	Comparative analyses of the MHC intergenic DNA sequence across five mammalian species (human, rat, mouse, hamster, and rabbit) indicates a conserved region that is proposed to be a common regulatory region for the alpha and antisense beta promoter (Haddad (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12851393).
bft	bereft	Characteristics	Two alternatively spliced ~3.5kb and ~6.5kb isoforms (Hardiman (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12019237).. Another longer extended isoform that is a precursor transcript for miR-263a has also been identified (Graveley (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21179090).
bft	bereft	Expression	Expressed in external sensory organs of the embryonic peripheral nervous system. Bristles in Drosophila are sensory organs and bereft is expressed in structural support cells during bristle formation.. Shows a punctate and possibly peri-nuclear localization
bft	bereft	Function	Required for bristle morphogenesis in external sensory organs.. Appears to act downstream of cut and tramtrack
bft	bereft	Name	bft: bereft

BORG	None known	Characteristics	~2.8kb. Spliced and polyadenylated RNA with three exons.. BORG RNA contains a number of repeat sequences.
BORG	None known	Expression	Identified in a myoblast cell line (C2C12) trans-differentiating into osteoblastic cells. . Immediate early response gene to bone morphogenic proteins (BMPs), expressed within 2 hrs, peaked between 12-24 hours before declining back to basal levels.. Expression induced by BMPs and osteogenic proteins in multiple cell types that respond to BMP signaling.
BORG	None known	Function	Knockdown of BORG via transfection of antisense oligonucleotides partially inhibits BMP-induced differentiation of C2C12 cells into osteoblastic cells. Proposed involvement in bone morphogenesis.

Bsr	Rian	Characteristics	LncRNA from the Dlk1-Dio3 imprinted region (Komine (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10095072, Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654).. Similar to Rian locus in mouse and humans with a lncRNA containing intronic snoRNAs, except the Bsr locus contains a ~100kb rat specific sequence containing 86 0.9kb tandem repeats (Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654, Komine (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10095072).  Bsr appears to have evolved through a massive duplication based expansion of some snoRNAs present in the ancestral locus (Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654). . Tandem repeats in the Bsr locus consist of an intron containing the RBII-36 snoRNA and a Bsr lncRNA exon (CavaillÃ© (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11346658, Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654).. Multiple products are detected from the Bsr locus consisting of varying numbers of the 0.9kb tandem repeat from which the ~75 bp snoRNA is spliced out (Komine (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10095072, CavaillÃ© (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11346658).
Bsr	Rian	Expression	Imprinted: Maternally expressed (Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654). Like snoRD115-HG and snoRD116-HG, one Bsr allele can show evidence of less compacted chromatin, this is almost always the transcribed allele (Vitali (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20016068).. Bsr is expressed predominantly in the CNS both during development and in adults (Komine (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10095072) as is the RBII-36 snoRNA cluster (CavaillÃ© (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11346658).. Nuclear localisation (Komine (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10095072). Mature, spliced Bsr was not localised to the nucleolus, unlike most mature RBII-36 (CavaillÃ© (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11346658, Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654). Bsr was present as mutiple small foci in the interchromatin space, often found on periphery of SC35 speckles but not found in SC35 speckles or paraspeckles (Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654). Did not co-localise with rat snoRD115-HG or snoRD116-HG, two other nuclear retained snoRNA containing lncRNAs (Vitali (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20016068). . Upon cellular stress a portion of Bsr relocates to the cytoplasm where it associates with stress granules (Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654).
Bsr	Rian	Conservation	Bsr and Rian/MEG8/Irm are not highly conserved between species (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206). However, some Rian exons show good homology to Bsr and while many snoRNAs are specific to one species others are homologous (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034, CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).
Bsr	Rian	Summary	Comparing human, mouse and rat: All contain ncRNA gene(s) with intronic snoRNAs at this locus. The snoRNAs vary between species, but there are some homologous snoRNAs between each suggesting an evolutionary history with species specific snoRNA addition and duplication (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).. The expression profiles of Bsr, Rian/Irm/MEG8 and the snoRNAs they contain are similar between rat, human and mouse.
Bsr	Rian	Name	 Bsr (brain specific repetitive) RNA
Bsr	Rian	Misc	UCSC browser link is from mapping of mouse Rian/Meg8 onto rat and may not be precisely representative of full length Bsr, the sequence for which is not available.

BX118339	Hs.112750, linc-MBOAT1-4: TCONS_00012107,  linc-MBOAT1-4: TCONS_00012678	Expression	Transcript isoform(s) expressed in testis (Cabili (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21890647) and also reported in fetal brain (Vandeweyer (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22245136).
BX118339	Hs.112750, linc-MBOAT1-4: TCONS_00012107,  linc-MBOAT1-4: TCONS_00012678	Function	Transcript disrupted by a balanced translocation, 46,XY,t(2;6)(p15;p22.3), in a patient with West Syndrome (a form of infant epilepsy). Lack of effect on other nearby genes or presence of mutations in known West Syndrome disease genes leads to possible implication of BX118339 in the clinical phenotype (Vandeweyer (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22245136).
CAR Intergenic 10	Intergenic10, CR611911, AK055628	Name	CAR10: Chromatin Associated RNA 10
CAR Intergenic 10	Intergenic10, CR611911, AK055628	Characteristics	Positioned between 3' ends of of FANK1 (fibronectin) and ADAM12 (ADAM metallopeptidase domain 12) genes, with an overlap of a few hundred base pairs with ADAM12.
CAR Intergenic 10	Intergenic10, CR611911, AK055628	Expression	CAR Intergenic 10, ADAM12 and FANK1 are co-expressed in different tissues, including placenta, brain and a human skin fibroblast (HF) cell line. . CAR Intergenic 10 was most highly expressed in HF cells and very lowly expressed in brain, with placenta in-between.
CAR Intergenic 10	Intergenic10, CR611911, AK055628	Function	Positively regulates gene expression of FANK1 and ADAM12 neighboring genes through modulating the chromatin structure in cis, as siRNA knock-down of the Intergenic10 ncRNA results in reduced expression of both FANK1 and ADAM12 mRNAs, with a significant decrease in the level of active chromatin mark H3K4me2 on FANK1 and ADAM12 promoters.. Knock-down of the ncRNA had no effect on the expression of two tested distal genes, UROS and DOCK1.. Note: Despite its overlap with the 3' end of ADAM12, Intergenic 10 is not simply an Adam12 3'UTR, as siRNA knockdown of Adam12 failed to decrease FANK1 expression unlike knockdown of CAR Intergenic 10. 
CCND1 associated ncRNAs	None known	Characteristics	Multiple ncRNAs transcribed from the promoter region of the cyclin D (CCND1) gene.. Transcripts of ~200nuc, ~330nuc and longer from both strands found within 2kb of the CCND1 transcription start site.
CCND1 associated ncRNAs	None known	Expression	Expression induced by DNA damage signals.. Transcripts highly enriched in chromatin.. Transcripts expressed from PROMPT (promoter upstream transcripts) regions, PROMPT transcripts are degraded by the exosome and generally highly unstable (Preker (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19056938).
CCND1 associated ncRNAs	None known	Function	Regulates gene expression of cyclin D1. . ncRNAs have free ssRNA region plus RNA:DNA duplex region to tether them to the CCND1 locus.. Interaction of ncRNA ssRNA region with RNA-binding protein TLS (translocated in liposarcoma) promotes allosteric modification of the protein, leading to inhibition of CREB-binding protein and histone acetyltransferase activities to repress cyclin D1.. Promoter associated RNAs that can regulate expression of their associated protein coding gene by acting as a guide for a generic protein transcriptional regulator.

CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Characteristics	Identified as ~1.5kb (no internal splicing) and ~1.3kb (with internal splicing). . Circular transcript in which 5â and 3â ends have splice donor and acceptor sequences and are spliced together.. Also contains 2 internal splice sites.
CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Expression	Highly expressed in human adult and fetal brain and spinal cord. Expression in brain considerably higher than that of CDR1 mRNA. Modest expression in other human tissues including heart, lung, thymus and thyroid.. Expressed in mouse brain (cerebellum and cerebrum).
CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Function	First lncRNA identified as a miRNA target.. CDR1 AS functions to stabilize CDR1 mRNA, as a decrease in CDR1 AS levels leads to a decrease in the expression level of the sense CDR1 mRNA. Conversely, the sense transcript does not act to stabilize the antisense lncRNA and appears to destabilize it, perhaps through a feedback mechanism. . CDR1 AS and hence CDR1 sense are regulated by miR-671. A conserved miR-671 binding site is present in the antisense transcript (a site which corresponds to near the transcriptional start site of the sense CDR1 mRNA). miR-671 localises to the nucleus and can repress CDR1 AS and CDR1 sense mRNA.. Effect of miR-671 does not appear to be through an epigenetic mechanism, instead it causes Ago2 mediated cleavage and down-regulation of CDR1 AS.. Mechanism for how CDR1 AS stabilizes CDR1 is not clear but it does not appear to be due to the lncRNA acting as a miR-671 sponge.
CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Conservation	CDR1 AS found in both humans and mouse.
CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Misc	Note: Evidence of antisense transcription across locus from a number of tissues present in Illumnia Body Atlas (IBA2). These suggest antisense transcripts can extend in both 5â and 3â directions and can be longer than 1.5kb. Whether these represent longer or primary CDR1 AS transcript is unclear.. AK054921 may represent an isoform although the sequence does not reach the miR-671 binding site.
CDR1 AS	CDR1 NAT
	Name	CDR1 Antisense. CDR1 Natural antisense transcript
Centromeric alpha-satellite RNA	None known	Characteristics	Transcribed RNAs contain monomers if not multimers of a 171bp repeat but actual length of transcripts were not defined.. Alpha-satellite RNA comes from the centromeric repeats of many chromosomes.
Centromeric alpha-satellite RNA	None known	Function	Regulates the assembly of the centromeric kinetochore.. At interphase alpha-centromeric RNA is localised to the nucleolus. It is able to bind multiple centromeric proteins (CENPC1 and INCENP), which it sequesters in this subdomain. . CENPC1, a core kinetochore protein, appears to bind directly to alpha-satellite RNA.. Upon mitosis alpha-centromeric RNA re-localises to chromosomal centromeres, allowing localisation of CENPC1, INCENP and survivin (an INCENP-interacting protein) to the metaphase centromere and assembly of the kinetochore. . The regulated localisation of alpha-centromeric RNA hence regulates the activity of centromeric proteins and assembly of the kinetochore.
Centromeric alpha-satellite RNA	None known	Misc	CENPC1 (centromere protein C 1)  . INCENP (inner centromere protein antigens 135/155kDa) . Centromeric sequences from a number of chromosomes were investigated, the UCSC browser location given below is just one example of a sequence that could have been detected.
COLDAIR	COLD ASSISTED INTRONIC NONCODING RNA	Characteristics	~1.1kb sense transcript from first intron of FLC. 5â capped, but not generally polyadenylated. RNA polymerase II transcript. Transcriptional start site within vernalization response element (VRE), which is required for proper vernalization dependant repression of FLC and appears to act as the promoter for COLDAIR.
COLDAIR	COLD ASSISTED INTRONIC NONCODING RNA	Expression	Transcriptional start site within vernalization response element (VRE), which is required for proper vernalization dependant repression of FLC and appears to act as the promoter for COLDAIR.. Expression specifically and transiently induced during vernalization / cold exposure with a peak at around day 20 and return to baseline levels by day 30. . Nb: this expression pattern is similar to COOLAIR, but up to 10 days delayed.. COLDAIR transcription may be shut off in negative feedback loop, where it shuts off transcription within the FLC gene including its own.  
COLDAIR	COLD ASSISTED INTRONIC NONCODING RNA	Function	COLDAIR is required for stable repression of FLC after vernalization and a lack of COLDAIR lead to late flowering after vernalization.. COLDAIR binds PRC2 complex protein CURLY LEAF (CLF), with maximal interaction after 20 days of vernalization / cold exposure. . COLDAIR is required to recruit PRC2 to the FLC locus allowing deposition of the repressive H3K27me3 chromatin mark.. COLDAIR did not impact the expression of other genes that repress flowering. 
COLDAIR	COLD ASSISTED INTRONIC NONCODING RNA	Background	Epigenetic represssion of FLOWERING LOCUS C (FLC) is required for Arabodopsis flowering in spring.. Polycomb repressive complex 2 is required for FLC repression.. COLDAIR is distinct from COOLAIR - http://www.lncrnadb.org/Detail.aspx?TKeyID=185, which does not appear to interact with PRC2.
COOLAIR	None known	Characteristics	Multiple spliced, polyadenylated isoforms. Short version ~400bp, long version ~750 bp (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688).. Transcription initiates just 3' of the FLC polyA site. Some isoforms terminate just beyond the start of the FLC gene (antisense transcription covers the entire FLC gene) (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688).
COOLAIR	None known	Expression	Antisense transcription over much of FLC locus. Antisense transcripts show a transient accumulation upon cold treatment with a peak after 10-14 days (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688, Heo (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21127216), before declining with further prolonged cold or when plants returned to warmth. Transcription of FLC decreases during cold treatment (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688).
COOLAIR	None known	Function	COOLAIR suggested to function in early cold induced silencing of FLC transcription (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688).. COOLAIR	None known	Name	COOLAIR: cold induced long antisense intragenic RNA (Swiezewski (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010688).

DHFR upstream transcripts	DHFR minor transcript 5'-UTR	Characteristics	DHFR upstream transcripts initiate from an upstream minor promoter of the DHFR (dihydrofolate reductase) gene and extend from approximately 400 nucleotide upstream of the 5'-untranslated region of DHFR (which corresponds to DHFR major/core promoter), to the second intron of the DHFR gene where they terminate (Masters (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2859520, Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763). Therefore, the region located between minor and major transcript initiation sites (~400 bp) corresponds to a noncoding transcript and is a promoter of DHFR.. Discrete DHRF upstream initiating transcripts of diverse sizes have been reported, including five major discrete species with sizes of 4.3, 3.8, 3.1, 2.1, and 1.0 kb and four minor ones with sizes of 7.3, 5.0, 1.4, and 0.8kb. Primarily in the poly(A)+ fraction (Masters (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2859520).. DHFR upstream transcripts adopt a series of structures in vitro that are dependent on the G-tract encompassed in its sequence (Blume (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12461786).
DHFR upstream transcripts	DHFR minor transcript 5'-UTR	Expression	Enriched in the nucleus (Masters (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2859520).. At least six minor 5' ends mapping upstream of the DHFR gene correspond to approximately 1% of the DHFR-specific polysomal polyA RNA. Most of these species have been found in 6A3 cells, VA2-B cells (the parental line of 6A3), and in HeLa cells (Masters (1985) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2859520).. DHFR upstream transcripts accumulate in a population of serum-starved, contact-inhibited (quiescent) U2OS cells, in which the levels of DHFR mRNA are markedly reduced (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763).
DHFR upstream transcripts	DHFR minor transcript 5'-UTR	Function	Initial studies indicated that DHFR upstream transcripts could impair the formation of the preinitiation complex (PIC) on the major promoter in vitro, thereby repressing the transcriptional activity of the major DHFR promoter (Blume (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12461786). DHFR upstream transcripts were shown to inhibit transcription from the DHFR core promoter in-trans in a concentration-dependent manner in in-vitro runoff transcription assays. Transcription factor binding sites positioned between the minor and major promoters within the DHFR gene were indicated to be affected by the upstream regulatory transcripts, which selectively sequestered transcription factor Sp3, and to a lesser extent Sp1, preventing their binding to the DHRF core promoter. The sequestration of Sp3 and Sp1 by the DHFR upstream transcripts appears to involve an altered conformation of the RNA, and a structural domain of the protein distinct from that required for binding DNA (Blume (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12461786). However, in-vitro experiments confirmed that transcription from the major promoter could be suppressed in-trans in the absence of Sp1 or any other upstream activating sequence (Akoulitchev (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7566158, Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763).. A more recent study demonstrated that these promoter associated transcripts act as interfering transcripts, directly interacting with TFIIB and dissociate the PIC efficiently to repress DHFR expression (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763). Transcription of the regulatory RNA in trans has a repressive effect on the major DHFR promoter only when the transcript contained the sequence of the core major DHFR promoter (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763). In addition, the major DHFR promoter is GC-rich and contains several G-track sequences (Blume (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12461786), and specific and stable triplex structures have been shown to form between the DHFR upstream transcripts and the major promoter, which may contribute to promoter targeting and repression in vivo (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763) (Blume (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12461786).. A comparison of in-vitro transcription from templates containing DHFR minor, major or both promoters in their original sequential order indicated very low transcriptional activity when the minor promoter preceded the major one, but robust transcription from the major promoter, suggesting that transcriptional interference in-cis may also play a role in DHFR inhibition by DHFR upstream transcripts (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763).
DHFR upstream transcripts	DHFR minor transcript 5'-UTR	Misc	Unpublished analysis of the epigenetic effects of DHFR upstream transcripts indicated similarities to epigenetic markers associated with transcriptional gene silencing induced by the targeted application of synthetic antigene RNAs complementary to the promoter regions of mammalian genes (Martianov (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237763).. DHFR is the major target of methotrexate, a key component in childhood acute lymphoblastic leukemia (ALL) treatment. DNA variations of major promoter/noncoding transcript region and specifc haplotype subtypes involving this region have been associated with childhood ALL, including associations with high-risk patients and lower event-free survival. One particular haplotype (Haplotype *1b) is associated with higher DHFR expression (Al-Shakfa (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19861437).
Dio3os	Dio3as	Characteristics	Antisense and head to head with Dio3 from the Dlk1-Dio3 imprtinted locus (Hernandez (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14962667). A large number of isoforms are transcribed through alternative splicing and start sites some of which overlap Dio3 (Hernandez (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14962667).. Dio3os	Dio3as	Expression	Various DIO3OS isoforms are expressed in a wide range of human tissues including adult testis, adrenal cortex, heart, bladder, uterus, placenta and fetal lung (Hernandez (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14962667).  . Expressed in embryonic and extra-embryonic tissue in mouse. Weakly expressed in several neonatal and adult tissues: brain and liver (adult only), intestine and tougue (neonate only),  kidney and lung (expressed in both) (Tierling (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16309881).  . Dio3os	Dio3as	Conservation	Aside from the short exon 1, there is poor sequence conservation and no conserved ORFs between mouse and human Dio3os (Hernandez (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14962667).

DLG2AS	PSZA11q14, SZ-1	Expression	Expression downregulated in multiple brain regions in some patients with schizophrenia (by PCR)..
