DLG2AS	PSZA11q14, SZ-1	Misc	Genbank accession: AF525782.1 for Dlg2as is incorrectly listed as an mRNA but is actually a ~10kb genomic clone containing Dlg2as.. Exact start and stop not defined but:. Longer isoform (~7kb) appears to end around: chr11:84,604,583 (hg19). Shorter isoform (~4.5kb) around: chr11:84,602,058 (hg19)
DLG2AS	PSZA11q14, SZ-1	Name	DLG2AS: DLG2 antisense RNA. PSZA11q14: putative schizophrenia associated gene from 11q14
Dlx1as	None known	Characteristics	Spliced, polyadenylated ~2.8kb transcript (McGuinness (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8812481)..  . Expressed from a highly conserved enhancer element downstream of Dlx1. Second exon overlaps exons and introns of Dlx1 in the antisense direction (Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676).
Dlx1as	None known	Expression	Dlx1as and Dlx1 were progressively more highly expressed during differentiation of embryonic stem cells (Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676).. Dlx1as and Dlx1 were both up-regulated during differentiation of neuronal progenitors to GABAergic neurons in vitro, but down-regulated during oligodendrocyte differentiation from the same progenitors (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).. Expressed in developing forebrain with highest expressive in the subventricular zone (Liu (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9415433).. Expressed in adult mouse brain, including in regions associated with neurogenesis (anterior subventricular zone, rostral migratory stream, and olfactory bulb) similar to the expression of Dlx1 and Dlx2 (Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676).
Dlx1as	None known	Conservation	Exon one initiates from an enhancer highly conserved in therian mammals (found in oppossum as well as placental mammals). Second exon also overlaps highly conserved sequences but this is mostly Dlx1 exon regions.
Dlx1as	None known	Misc	Dlx1: distal-less homeobox 1. Transcription factor with an important role in brain development that is important role in specifying neuronal cell fate.
dUHGs	dUHG1, dUHG2, dUHG3, dUHG4, dUHG5, dUHG7, dUHG8	Characteristics	7 known dUHGs (dUHG 1-5, 7-8), spliced noncoding RNAs that contain intronic snoRNAs (Tycowski (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11302516, Huang (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15987805). Nb: UHG6 identified as protein coding.. These 7 genes contain around half the known box C/D snoRNAs in Drosophila with snoRNAs in almost every intron (Huang (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15987805).. dUHG1 & 2 transcriptional start sites have characteristics of the 5' TOP gene family (Tycowski (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11302516).
dUHGs	dUHG1, dUHG2, dUHG3, dUHG4, dUHG5, dUHG7, dUHG8	Expression	dUHG1 and 2 can be stabilised by inhibition of protein synthesis suggesting they are normally degraded by nonsense mediated decay (Tycowski (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11302516).
dUHGs	dUHG1, dUHG2, dUHG3, dUHG4, dUHG5, dUHG7, dUHG8	Conservation	dUHG 1 and 2 contain snoRNAs that appear homologous to some of those found in UHG/SNHG1 and Gas5/SNHG2. Calling these genes homologous is not straightforward however, ie: both dUHG1 and 2 contain snoRNAs found in UHG, dUHG2 also contain snoRNAs found within introns of mammalian protein coding genes.
dUHGs	dUHG1, dUHG2, dUHG3, dUHG4, dUHG5, dUHG7, dUHG8	Name	dUHG: Drosophila U snoRNA Host Gene.
dUHGs	dUHG1, dUHG2, dUHG3, dUHG4, dUHG5, dUHG7, dUHG8	Misc	GeneID NCBI Entrez Gene. dUHG1: 3772106. dUHG2: 3772246. dUHG3: 3772557. dUHG4: 8673973. dUHG5: 8673975. dUHG7: 8674061. dUHG8: 8674065.  
dutA	None known	Characteristics	~1.3 kb, transcribed by RNAP II, and exported to the cytoplasm (Yoshida (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8127653).
dutA	None known	Expression	"Developmentally regulated" during Dictyostelium discoideum multicellular organization: induced during aggregation and exhibits a distinct expression pattern during stalk formation, ceasing with the onset of culmination (Yoshida (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8127653) (Kumimoto (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7488100) (Maeda (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12796308). dutA expression is not affected by cAMP signaling but requires protein kinase A (PKA) signaling (Kumimoto (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8764472).. A Serial Analysis of Gene Expression (SAGE) study indicates that dutA is the most abundant polyadenylated RNA in the Dictyostelium transcriptome, expressed at a level almost twice that of the next highest gene (Whitney (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20309825).. A microarray analysis of D. discoideum cells infected with Legionella pneumophila indicated down-regulation of dutA mRNA, suggesting a possible function of dutA in hostâpathogen interaction (Farbrother (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16469056).
dutA	None known	Function	The function of dutA remains unclear. Disruption of dutA showed no morphological phenotype under normal conditions of growth and development (Yoshida (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8127653), which may be due to functional redundancy. . However, over-expression of dutA segments suppresses mutations in the signaling component Dd-STATa (the functional homolog of metazoan STAT transcriptional factors), rescuing stalk formation that is impaired in the mutants and indicating an inhibitory role of dutA in culmination. It also restores expression of target genes and tyrosine phosphorylation, indicating that dutA acts upstream of Dd-STATa in the signal transduction pathway and has an important role in Dictyostelium multicellular development switch (Shimada (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17435008).
dutA	None known	Misc	Contains some peculiar sequence motifs.
dutA	None known	Name	DutA: Development-specific but UnTranslatable RNA A
E2F4 antisense	None known	Characteristics	~5.5kb transcript originating from the 3'UTR of E2F4. Antisense to E2F4. 
E2F4 antisense	None known	Expression	Localised to the nucleus and the cytoplasm although it is mainly cytoplasmic.. Expression identified in HCT116 colorectal carcinoma cells.. Expression is driven by Wnt signalling with beta-catenin and TCF/Lef binding to the E2F4 3'UTR to upregulate E2F4 antisense transcription.
E2F4 antisense	None known	Function	Expression of E2F4 antisense lead to a decrease in E2F4 protein levels and reduced binding of E2F4 to its target gene promoters. This effect did not occur with, and could be blocked by, an E2F4 3'UTR sense construct.. Disruption of Wnt signalling is very common in colorectal cancer and it was hypothesised that induction of E2F4 antisense by Wnt signaling may contribute to carcinogenesis by reducing levels of the E2F4 cell cycle repressor.   
E2F4 antisense	None known	Misc	E2F4 acts in cell cycle controls where it is thought to act as a repressor of proliferation.. Neither the sequence nor exact coordinates of E2F4 antisense are available.
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known		EBER: Epstein-Barr virus (EBV)-encoded small RNA
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known	Characteristics	Encoded by Epstein-Barr virus. EBER genes are separated by 161 base pairs (Rosa (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9279391, Lerner (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6262773).. EBER1: 167nt, EBER2: 172nt. Show significant sequence similarity with each other. Heterogeneity resides at the 3' termini (Rosa (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9279391, Lerner (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6262773). Highly structured, resulting in the formation of several stable stem-loops (Glickman (1988) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2828685).. Transcribed by RNA polymerase III. Possess 5' pppA termini. Non-polyadenylated (Rosa (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9279391, Lerner (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6262773).
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known	Expression	Highly expressed during EBV latency in infection of many cell types and all associated human malignancies (EBERs are the most abundantly expressed RNAs during latency).. Nuclear localisation.
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known	Function	Bind to La autoantigen protein (Rosa (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9279391, Lerner (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6262773) and PKR in vitro, and have been suggested to block PKR activity and confer resistance to Fas-mediated apoptosis of host cells (Clarke (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1673026, Sharp (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7901835, Nanbo (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16160154), although inhibition of PKR has not been observed in vivo (Ruf (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16282456).. EBER-1 interacts with RPL22 (ribosomal protein L22), which is known to interact with components of different viruses (Dobbelstein (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7494316, Fok (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16556938). EBER-1 mediates stable relocalisation of L22 from nucleoli to nucleoplasm in EBV-infected cells, which is critical for EBER-dependent functions (Houmani (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19640998). Burkitt's lymphoma (BL) cells expressing mutated EBER-1 RNAs incapable of binding L22 have reduced capacity to enhance BL cell growth (Houmani (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19640998).. Role in the growth and maintenance of BL cell malignant phenotype (Shimizu (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8057484, Ruf (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11024153). Also contribute to the growth of other B-cell lymphoma-, gastric carcinoma-, and nasopharyngeal carcinoma-derived cell lines (Iwakiri (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14612496, Iwakiri (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15608666, Yamamoto (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11068051).. Inhibit alpha interferon-induced apoptosis in latently infected B-cell lines. EBER RNAs induce the expression of interleukin (IL)-10 in BL cells (Kitagawa (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11118209), as well as insulin-like growth factor (IGF)-1 in gastric carcinoma and nasopharyngeal carcinoma cells, and IL-9 in T cells, which acts as an autocrine growth factor.. EBERs can be secreted from EBV-infected cells and can be detected in the sera of infected patients. RNAs are recognized by toll-like receptor (TLR)3, leading to induction of type-I IFNs and inflammatory cytokines (Iwakiri (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19720839), suggesting that activation of TLR3 signaling could lead to the pathogenesis of active EBV infectious diseases (Iwakiri (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19720839, Iwakiri (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20399962).. Functionality of EBER1 and 2 does not appear to be redundant, as transforming capacity of EBER2-deleted virus is comparable to that of EBV lacking both EBERs, but that of EBER-1-deleted virus is as high as wild-type EBV, indicating that EBER1 does not play a critical role in EBV-induced B-cell growth transformation. (Wu (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17686859)
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known	Conservation	The primary sequences of EBERs are strongly conserved among EBV strains (Arrand (1989) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2536122).
EBER1 and EBER2 RNAs	None known	Misc	Many similarities with adenovirus VAI and VAII RNAs (Rosa (1981) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9279391), as well as other virus-encoded ncRNAs (eg. Howe (1988) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2839701).
EGO	EGOT	Characteristics	Two isoforms:. ~1.0kb unspliced EGO-A and ~1.5 kb spliced (two exons) EGO-B.. Transcribed antisense from a conserved intron of ITPR1 gene.
EGO	EGOT	Expression	Highly expressed in human bone marrow CD34+ cells and BMMC (bone marrow mononuclear cells).. Highly upregulated during eosinophil development from CD34+ human hematopoietic stem cells before returning to basal levels within 72 hours. Despite a return to basal levels, EGO transcripts were present and inducible in mature eosinophils.
EGO	EGOT	Function	Proposed to affect myeloid development by regulating eosinophil gene expression, as knockdown of EGO in vitro in CD34+ cells decreases eosinophil granule protein MBP (major basic protein) and EDN (eosinophil derived neurotoxin) mRNA levels.
EGO	EGOT	Conservation	EGO and some of surrounding sequence is conserved. However the presence of EGO has not been investigated outside of humans. 
EGO	EGOT	Name	Eosinophil granule ontogeny (EGO) RNA
Emx2os	None known	Characteristics	5 kb. Spliced, bi-directional to Emx2, with a 271 nucleotide head-to-head antisense overlap. Riboprobe Northern blot indicates the existence of three additional Emx2os splicing isoforms differentially detected in the murine urogenital system, with sizes of 6.0, 2,3 and 1,8 kb, which are supported by cDNA evidence (Noonan (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12573261).
Emx2os	None known	Expression	EMX2 and EMX2OS and their murine orthologs have similar profiles and extensively coincident cellular expression patterns in the endometrium. Expressed in the uterus, abundant in normal postmenopausal endometrium, reduced in premenopausal endometrium (Noonan (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12573261).. Emx2os is expressed in the developing mouse CNS. Examination of expression at E10.5, E12.5, E14.5 and E18.5 showed, similar to Emx2, that its levels reduce progressively from E10.5 to E18.5. At E12.5, it is detected in a number of CNS structures also expressing Emx2 mRNA, such as the pallium and basal ganglia, mammillary recess of the hypothalamus, optic tectum, olfactory placode and otic vesicle. Emx2os is found in the developing telencephalon in periventricular proliferative layers and the cortical plate (Spigoni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20066053).. However, the sense/antisense pair may also show mutually exclusive patterns, such as within the cortex. Emx2os is detected in periventricular precursors that also express Emx2, but peaks in newly born post-mitotic neurons, which do not express Emx2, whereas Emx2 is expressed Cajal-Retzius neurons lying in the marginal zone, which do not express the antisense RNA (Spigoni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20066053).. In human brain, expression has been detected in normal nucleus accumbens (Michelhaugh (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21128942).
Emx2os	None known	Function	EMX2OS is suggested to regulate EMX2 expression (Noonan (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12573261), which may involve distinct regulatory mechanisms in different cell types (Spigoni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20066053).. In vitro knock-down experiments indicate that Emx2os contributes to post-transcriptional down-regulation of its sense partner in cortical precursors and their neuronal progenies, possibly by a Dicer1-dependent process  (Spigoni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20066053).. However, ectopic expression of a 5' fragment (OS1-179+) of Emx2os in neural precursors of the rhombo-spinal tract stimulates expression of Emx2, indicating a complex regulatory mechanism, perhaps at transcriptional level. In addition, Emx2 knock-out results in a strong reduction of Emx2os transcript levels, indicating a possible reciprocal regulatory loop (Spigoni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20066053).
Emx2os	None known	Conservation	Association of Emx2os and Emx2 is conserved between mouse and humans, but no sequence conservation was found (Noonan (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12573261).
Emx2os	None known	Misc	EMX2OS lies in the minimal interval with allelic loss in endometrial tumors and is a candidate endometrial cancer tumor suppressor (Noonan (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12573261).
Emx2os	None known	Name	Emx2os: Emx2 opposite strand transcript.
ENOD40	None known		**Annotation in Progress**
ENOD40	None known	Characteristics	Family of RNAs.. In legumes, it encodes a conserved 10â25 amino acid peptide, and contains up to six inverted repeats (IRs) (Girard et al. 2003).
ENOD40	None known	Expression	***The Enod40 family is expressed in differentiating cells of the primordial nodule (Yang et al. 1993; Crespi et al. 1994), but also has varying levels of expression in all parts of the plant, particularly the vascular system, where its expression correlates with the emergence of lateral roots and emerging leaves (Vleghels et al. 2003, Kouchi et al. 1999, Varkonyi-Gasic and White 2002).***. Expression regulated by growth conditions affecting root tissues  (Campalans (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15037734).
ENOD40	None known	Function	ENOD40 transcripts are required for correct subcellular localization of RNP particles in legume plants (Campalans (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15037734).
ENOD40	None known	Conservation	N/A
ENOD40	None known	Misc	N/A
Evf2	Evf-2, Dlx6as1, Dlx6os1	Characteristics	~3.8 kb. Antisense to Dlx6 genes in the Dlx5/6 cluster. Evf1 and 2 are isoforms with alternative promoters expressed from ultraconserved enhancers. Different Evf-1 and Evf-2 transcripts result from alternative transcription initiation, alternative splicing of exon 3, and alternative polyadenylation. Therefore, Evf-1 and Evf-2 cDNA sequences have unique 5' and 3' ends, and share a 2561bp region of identity (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037, Kohtz (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15183307).. A large (7.5-kb) non-polyadenylated form recognized by both Evf-1 and Evf-2 Northern blot probes is present in the total RNA fraction and absent from the poly(A) containing fraction. The Evf-2-specific probe also identifies a smaller (500-bp) transcript (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).
Evf2	Evf-2, Dlx6as1, Dlx6os1	Expression	Nuclear localisation (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037, Sone (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17623775).. Similar expression pattern to Dlx6 and Dlx5 mRNAs. Developmentally regulated, expressed in the ventral forebrain. Detected in immature neurons as they exit the ventricular zone (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).. Ectopic expression of Sonic hedgehog (Shh) induces the expression of Evf-2, Evf-1, Dlx-2, Dlx-5, and Dlx-6 in the dorsal telencephalon in vivo (mouse embryos)  (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).. Up-regulated in vitro during differentiation of neuronal progenitors to GABAergic neurons and during mouse embryonic stem cells differentiation (Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676) (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068). Also found co-expressed in the first and second branchial arches of E10.5 mouse embryos (Jeong (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18697905).. Brain expression of Evf2 and Evf1 is dependent on Dlx1/2 function. Expression of Evf2 and Evf1 is also greatly reduced in Dlx5/6, and Dlx5 or Dlx6, knock-out mutants, indicating that they may be their direct or indirect regulatory targets (Kohtz (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15183307, Jeong (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18697905). Evf1 and Evf2 were more down-regulated in Dlx5-/- than in Dlx6-/- mutants (Jeong (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18697905).
Evf2	Evf-2, Dlx6as1, Dlx6os1	Function	Evf-2 ncRNA and Dlx-2 proten display an intranuclear colocalization (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).. The ultraconserved region* of Evf-2 binds and co-operates with Dlx-2 in vivo to increase the transcriptional activity of the Dlx-5/6 enhancer in a target and homeodomain-specific manner (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037). *The Evf-2 5' region is both necessary and sufficient for activity.. Evf2 recruitment of DLX2 and MECP2 controls the expression of targets Dlx5, Dlx6 and Gad1 through trans and cis-acting mechanisms in developing ventral forebrain. Evf2 function is also required for proper gene regulation and formation of hippocampal GABA-dependent neuronal circuitry in mouse adult brain (Bond (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19620975).
Evf2	Evf-2, Dlx6as1, Dlx6os1	Conservation	Evf-2 is transcribed from (and contains in its first exon) a vertebrate ultraconserved element. Analysis of transcripts by isolation from a cDNA library (rat), RTâPCR (zebrafish and chicken), or expressed sequence tag (EST) databases (human and mouse) showed that transcription of the ultraconserved element associated with Evf-2 (enhancer ei) is conserved in vertebrates (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).. Evf-1 and Evf-2 exhibit a high degree (86%â93%) of conservation between rat and mouse sequences in their 5' and 3' regions, and a compilation of transcripts found in human, rat, mouse, zebrafish, and chicken shows that only transcription from exon 2 is conserved (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037).
Evf2	Evf-2, Dlx6as1, Dlx6os1	Misc	Evf-2 is proposed to belong to a class of transcription regulating, ultraconserved ncRNAs (trucRNAs), and may be part of a broader Dlx gene/antisense RNA regulatory network (Feng (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16705037, Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676).
fbp1+ promoter RNAs	None known	Characteristics	LncRNA transcripts from promoter of fbp1+ gene.. Three transcripts A to C.  Expressed in sense direction. Unspliced.. Transcript A initiates furthest upstream from fbp1+ start site, B and C initiate progressively closer to fbp1+. . Although they are transcribed into fbp1+, A-C do not necessarily cover the whole coding sequence and no detectable protein was produced.
fbp1+ promoter RNAs	None known	Expression	Transiently expressed upon glucose starvation before fbp1+ is switched on.. A shows very low constitutive expression and is expressed up to 20 min after glucose starvation. B expressed from 10-60 min, C from 20-60 min. . NB: fbp1+ switches on after 60 min.
fbp1+ promoter RNAs	None known	Function	Transcription of ncRNAs was required for opening of chromatin and activation of fbp1+ transcription.. Progressive movement of transcription from 5' to 3' towards the fbp1+ start site correlates with chromatin remodeling to open up DNA and RNA polymerase II movement.. Termination of upstream transcription prevented chromatin remodeling and fbp1+ induction, showing the necessity of the noncoding cascade in activating transcription.. Unknown if lncRNAs themselves are carrying out a function.
fbp1+ promoter RNAs	None known	Conservation	Identified in fission yeast: Schizosaccharomyces pombe
Frigidair	None known	Characteristics	Transcript on the antisense strand of the HoxC locus between Hoxc4 and Hoxc5 (Guttman (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19182780).. LincRNA - Large intervening noncoding RNA.
Frigidair	None known	Expression	Expression is highly anti-correlated with HOTAIR during limb development (Guttman (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19182780).. Putatively regulated by NFkB. Amongst lincRNAs differentially expressed after TLR4 (Toll-like receptor 4) stimulation of CD11C+ bone-marrow-derived dendritic cells (BMDC) (Guttman (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19182780).
Frigidair	None known	Misc	Sequence and exact genomic coordinates of the lncRNA have not been defined. 
frq antisense RNAs	None known	Characteristics	2 RNAs of ~5 and ~5.5kb transcribed antisense to the frequency (frq) gene  (Aronson (1994) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8052643, Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).. Antisense transcription initiates at several sites (217, 241 and 278bp) downstream of the frq sense stop codon (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).
frq antisense RNAs	None known	Expression	Antisense RNA showed a cyclic expression pattern but with the opposite rhythm to frq sense RNA and at a lower expression level when Neurospora was grown in the dark (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).. Strongly up-regulated when cells exposed to light (as is frq sense) (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).
frq antisense RNAs	None known	Function	Required for entrainment of the circadian clock in Neurospora crassa (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).. Loss of antisense transcript altered circadian rhythms with the clock set several hours earlier than normal and causing delayed onset of rhythmic conidiation (spore production) (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).. Antisense transcripts were also necessary for proper clock resetting on exposure to light. In the wild type light exposure caused a small resetting of the clock, while loss of antisense transcripts caused a massive resetting of the clock (Kramer (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12607002).
frq antisense RNAs	None known	Misc	Cyclic expression of the the sense frequency RNA (and frq protein) is required for Neurospora circadian timing.
G22	None known	Characteristics	~280 nucleotides, dimeric Alu sequence (Kuryshev (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11399078).. Same genetic locus has been targeted independently to create Alu derived BC200 and G22 genes in different primate lineages (Kuryshev (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11399078, Ludwig (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15922354). 
G22	None known	Conservation	Found in strepsirhini primates (Lemurs and Lorises) (Kuryshev (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11399078). However, G22 appears under selection only in lorisiformes (Galago moholi) (Ludwig (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15922354).. BC200, BC1 and G22 likely form a family of independently exapted repetitive elements which have evolved to carry out similar functions in different mammalian species (Muddashetty (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12162957, Khanam (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17175535).
G22	None known	Function	Binds to poly(A) binding protein (PABP) and the SRP9/14 heterodimer (Khanam (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17175535).
G22	None known	Expression	Transcribed in lorisiform brain (Ludwig (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15922354).. Localised to dendrites in a transgenic mouse (Khanam (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17175535).  
G22	None known	Misc	Galago moholi G22 can be found in REGION: 8494..8776 of  AF314807.. L13, (version in lemurs) can be found in REGION: 6983..7295 of AF314807. 
Gadd7	adapt15	Characteristics	Gene involved in the cellular response to a number of stressors.. 754 nt (Hollander (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8649973).
Gadd7	adapt15	Expression	Induced by DNA damage (Hollander (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8649973), lipotoxic-stress (Brookheart (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19150982), non-lipid oxidative stress (ie hydrogen peroxide exposure) (Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8561505, Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8638945), serum starvation (Hollander (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8649973, Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8638945) and heat shock (Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8638945).
Gadd7	adapt15	Function	Regulation of lipid-induced oxidative and ER stress (Brookheart (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19150982).. Causes growth arrest and cell death (Hollander (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8649973, Brookheart (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19150982). . Found in cytoplasm associated with active ribosomes (Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8561505), however all attempts at in-vitro and in-vivo translation have failed to express any peptides from the short ORFs found in the sequence (Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8561505, Hollander (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8649973, Brookheart (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19150982). Suggests ribosomal association could be regulatory, though translation of gadd7 can't be completely ruled out. . Induction by hydrogen peroxide required calcium (Crawford (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8638945). 
Gadd7	adapt15	Conservation	Identified in hamster.
GAL10-ncRNA		Characteristics	GAL10-ncRNA runs antisense through the GAL10 gene, through the bidirectional GAL1-10 promoter and through to the 3â of GAL1 gene in the sense direction. 4kb transcript.. Transcripts are 5â capped and 3â polyadenylated.
GAL10-ncRNA		Expression	Under non-induced and repressed conditions, marks of active transcription (H3 K4 me2/me3) are not present at GAL protein coding gene promoters but instead found at 3â end of GAL10. Histone modifications require binding of Reb1.. Reb1 drives expression of ncRNAs under repressive, and non-induced nutrient conditions. GAL10-ncRNA was the 4kb major transcript but also a weaker 2.3kb transcript is also present. All characterisation was on the 4kb GAL10-ncRNA.. GAL10-ncRNA stability was tested, half life ~8 min (relatively stable for a yeast transcript) and targeted for degredation by the TRAMP / exosome complexes.. Steady state expression level ~0.07 transcripts per cell / ~ 1 transcript per 14 cells. . Estimate ncRNA transcribed once every 50 minutes.
GAL10-ncRNA		Function	Summary: GAL10-ncRNA enhances repression of GAL10 and GAL1 expression when yeast are growing in repressive nutrient conditions.. Transcription of GAL10 ncRNA causes changes in chromatin. . - H3 K36 me3 is deposited over the chromosomal region GAL10-ncRNA is transcribed from.. - GAL10 transcription also causes a decrease in some histone 3 acetlyation.. GAL10 ncRNA acts in cis, recruiting the Rpd3S HDAC complex. Unknown if GAL10 ncRNA can physically recruit any chromatin modifying complexes or if transcription dependent chromatin changes independent of the GAL10-ncRNA sequence are responsible.. Note: this is not a transcriptional interference mechanism (see infrequent GAL10-ncRNA trancription) but a chromatin modification mechanism.
GAL10-ncRNA		Misc	GAL cluster of 3 genes (GAL1, GAL7, GAL10) are involved in galactose metabolism. Yeast has complex regulation of nutrient metabolism genes and the cluster can be induced, non-induced or repressed depending on the carbon sources available.
GAS5	SNHG2	Characteristics	Growth arrest-specific transcript (Schneider (1988) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3409319), multiple splice isoforms (Coccia (1992) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1630459) of ~250, ~450, ~600nuc and longer (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18354083), encodes 9 (10 in humans) snoRNAs in its introns (Smith (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9819378).
GAS5	SNHG2	Expression	Widely expressed in adult tissues and over embryonic development (Coccia (1992) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1630459).. Transcript undergoes post-transcriptional regulation, highly unstable but stabilised by growth arrest, serum starvation and inhibition of protein synthesis (Coccia (1992) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1630459, Smith (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9819378, Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551). Associates with ribosomes in the cytoplasm (Smith (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9819378).. Localises to both the nucleus and the cytoplasm (Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551).. Down-regulated in breast cancer (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18836484).. Transcript was classified as unstable with a half-life >4 hr in human Hela cells (Tani (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22369889). Similar half-lives were identified in human B cells and mouse 3T3 fibroblasts (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
GAS5	SNHG2	Function	Necessary and sufficient for growth arrest in human peripheral blood T-cells. Functions by  controlling apoptosis and the cell cycle in lymphocytes (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18354083).. In some cell lines certain Gas5 isoforms act to sensitise the cells to apoptosis but can't induce apoptosis on their own. In other cells types Gas5 can both induce apoptosis and growth arrest and sensitise the cells to further apoptosis (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18836484).. Gas5 can be regulated by mTOR, with mTOR (which promotes cellular proliferation) acting to inhibit the function of Gas5 (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20421347).. Gas5 carries out its function by binding the DNA binding domain of the glucocorticoid receptor (GR) with a sequence that mimmics the glucocorticoid response element (GRE). Gas5 is translocated into the nucleus bound to the GR where it prevents GR from binding GREs and regulating transcription of target genes including apoptosis inhibitors (Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551).. Gas5 also appears to repress the action of many steroid hormone receptors, showing some similarities to another lncRNA SRA (Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551).. Gas5 is a snoRNA host and a functional RNA. Function does not require putative but nonconserved ORF, or the intronic snoRNAs (Mourtada-Maarabouni (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18354083, Mourtada-Maarabouni (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18836484, Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551).
GAS5	SNHG2	Conservation	Gas5 in mouse and human do not show high sequence identity (Tanaka-Fujita (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17468437) although the GRE mimmic region is conserved (Kino (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20124551).. Most of the snoRNAs found in human Gas5 also cluster in the same order in a putatively noncoding RNA host gene in chicken. 42% homology was found between human Gas5 and the chicken gene which was named Gas5-like (Shao (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19232134).
GAS5	SNHG2	Misc	Mourtada-Maarabouni., et al (2010) provide an interesting hypothesis for how Gas5 levels and therefore function is regulated.. - Gas5 is stabilised by inhibition of protein synthesis suggesting it may normally be a target for nonsense mediated decay (NMD). mTOR regulates 5' TOP genes (which includes Gas5) promoting translation, whereas mTOR inhibition inhibits translation. This could allow mTOR to inhibit Gas5 by promoting Gas5 NMD. . This suggests that since Gas5 is known to be functional at the RNA level, any Gas5 translation may be a regulatory to control Gas5 levels and not necessarily to produce a functional protein.  
Gomafu	MIAT, RNCR2	Characteristics 	Intergenic, ~9-10kb alternatively spliced transcript in mammals (Ishii (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17066261, Sone (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17623775).. Contains tandem UACUAAC repeats, which match the conserved intron branch point sequence in Saccharomyces cerevisiae (Tsuiji (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21463453).
Gomafu	MIAT, RNCR2	Expression	Expressed predominantly in the nervous system (Ishii (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17066261, Sone (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17623775, Mercer (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18184812, Tsuiji (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21463453).. Shows dynamic regulation during retinal development (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823), differentiation of neural stem cells into oligodendrocytes (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068) and in mouse embryonic stem cell (mESC) differentiation (Sheik Mohamed (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20026622)(Dinger (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18562676). . Expressed in the nucleus accumbens of normal human brains and one of a few genes up-regulated in this brain region in both cocaine and heroin abusers (Albertson (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16710320, Michelhaugh (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21128942).. Nuclear specific localisation to novel nuclear matrix subdomain (Sone (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17623775).
Gomafu	MIAT, RNCR2	Function	Gomafu can bind the splicing factor 1 (SF1) protein through its UACUAAC repeat sequences. This sequence is a much stronger intron branch point sequence than found in most mammalian introns. In-vitro Gomafu binding to SF1 can inhibit splicing and spliceosomal complex formation suggesting Gomafu can function to regulate splicing efficiency (Tsuiji (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21463453).. Regulates retinal cell fate specification (Rapicavoli (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20459797).. Variants confer susceptibility to myocardial infarction, possibly through altering the RNA's protein binding properties (Ishii (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17066261).. Probable target of transcription factor Oct4 in mESCs. Appears to maintain Oct4 expression in a feedback loop helping to maintain pluripotency (Sheik Mohamed (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20026622).  
Gomafu	MIAT, RNCR2	Conservation	Well conserved in placental mammals, present in chicken and appears to be conserved back to amphibians (Rapicavoli (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20459797, Tsuiji (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21463453).  . Outside of mammals sequence conservation is low but the SF1 binding UACUAAC repeats are conserved (Rapicavoli (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20459797, Tsuiji (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21463453).
Gomafu	MIAT, RNCR2	Names	MIAT: myocardial infarction associated transcript (Ishii (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17066261).. RNCR2: retinal noncoding RNA 2 (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823).
Gtl2-as	Gtl2 antisense, Meg3-as	Characteristics	Northern suggests a transcript of around 3kb.. Transcript initiation and termination sites not defined, however at least some of transcript is located between Rtl1 and Meg3/Gtl2.
Gtl2-as	Gtl2 antisense, Meg3-as	Expression	Identified in mouse embyonic stem cells (mESCs)
Gtl2-as	Gtl2 antisense, Meg3-as	Function	Binds PRC2 chromatin modifying complex
Gtl2-as	Gtl2 antisense, Meg3-as	Misc	As the transcript itself is not defined no accurate ucsc browser link is possible.
H19	None known	Characteristics	2.3 kb. Imprinted at the Igf2 locus (Bartolomei (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1709450, Zemel (1992) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1303252).. Also contains a microRNA (miR-675) in exon one (Cai (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17237358).
H19	None known	Expression	Expressed from the maternal allele, while the neighbouring Igf2 gene is transcribed from the paternal allele (Bartolomei (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1709450). . In mice, H19 is activated in extra-embryonic cell types at the time of implantation. Strongly expressed during embryogenesis, down-regulated after birth with strong expression only retained in skeletal muscle and cartilage (Pachnis (1984) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6206499, Pachnis (1988) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3396539, Poirier (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1811930, Castle (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20668672, Dudek (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20529846); upregulated in various tumors (Matouk (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17786216).. Can be found in both the nucleus and the cytoplasm (Runge (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10875929, Schoenfelder (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17948025, Brannan (1990) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1688465). 
H19	None known	Function	Complex functions: . Influences growth via control of Igf2 expression, with a H19 knockout showing an overgrowth phenotype due in part to bi-allelic expression of Igf2 (Ripoche (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9203585).. Can also function in trans to downregulate the expression of a number of imprinted genes in the hypothesised Imprinted Gene Network (IGN) including Igf2r, Dlk1 etc. Allowing H19 to regulate growth during development (Gabory (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19762426).. Implicated as both a tumor suppressor (Hao (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7692308, Yoshimizu (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18719115) and an oncogene upregulated by c-myc and hypoxia (Matouk (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17786216, Barsyte-Lovejoy (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16707459 and references therein). A number of reports have also shown upregulation / reactivation of H19 in various cancers although the functional significance (if any) is unclear in many cases (Gabory (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20486133, Adriaenssens (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9811352).. The mode of action by which H19 functions is still unclear: . Focusing on its regulation of Igf2, H19 has been hypothesised to act at the level of transcription since an H19 knockout lead to methylation changes and loss of imprinting of Igf2 (Ripoche (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9203585, FornÃ© (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9294195). However, H19 can bind Igf2 mRNA binding-protein (IMP) family members (Runge (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10875929), which appear to act to promote translation of Igf2 (Hansen (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15121863, Liao (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15753088), therefore competition between Igf2 and H19 for IMP1 binding may allow H19 to regulate Igf2 post-transcriptionally.. Both sense and antisense transcripts from the H19 locus were identified as binding to the PRC2 chromatin modification complex in mouse embryonic stem cells, suggesting a potential function for H19 RNA (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. miR-675 may be responsible for the oncogenic activity of H19 as it was found to down-regulate the tumour suppressor retinoblastoma (RB) in human colorectal cancer, causing increased tumour cell growth (Tsang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19926638). Also, in adult human chondrocytes, expression of H19 (and subsequently miR-675) is driven by SOX9 with miR-675 acting to positively regulate COL2A1 which encodes a collagen protein important to the cartilage matrix (Dudek (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20529846).. H19 appears to be a bi-functional RNA acting as both a miRNA and a lncRNA. Such properties may help to explain the conflicting reports that it is both a tumour suppressor and an oncogene (Smits (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587395). Additionally its effect on tumour development may be heavily context dependent (Gabory (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20486133). 
H19	None known	Conservation	Conserved and imprinted in therians (eutherians and marsupials). Both the miRNA and the  H19 lncRNA exon structure are conserved (Smits (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18587395).
H19	None known	Misc	First long noncoding RNA described in mammalian cells (Brannan (1990) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1688465). Gabory 2010 provides a useful review of some of the extensive literature on H19 (Gabory (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20486133).
H19 antisense	91H	Characteristics	Expression identified upstream and downstream of H19 including through H19 enhancers and imprinting control region (ICR) in cancer cell lines (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369). . Suggested to be an antisense transcript covering ~120kb which starts in intron 1 of the (non-imprinted) MRPL23 gene and runs through H19 towards Igf2. A full length clone has not been identified so the presence of splicing is unknown. Transcript hypothesised to cover much of MRPL23 in sense direction as well as the H19 enhancers and ICR plus H19 in the antisense direction (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).
H19 antisense	91H	Expression	Transcript appears to be nuclear and highly unstable. It is lowly expressed in normal cells with up-regulation in cancer cells due to transcript stabilisation (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).. Antisense transcription throughout locus was also identified in mouse (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).. Imprinted: Maternally expressed (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).
H19 antisense	91H	Function	Knockdown lead to a decrease in Igf2 expression. Knockdown had little effect on H19 expression (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369) and it is unclear if it affected expression of H19 enhancers or the ICR.
H19 antisense	91H	Conservation	Mouse and human (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).
H19 antisense	91H	Misc	It is difficult to define the independent transcripts throughout this locus since enhancer and ICR sequences are known to be transcribed, sometimes bi-allelically (Drewell (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11874916, Schoenfelder (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17948025).  . Question of whether a 120kb unspliced antisense transcript exists in that form, or if there are a mixture of antisense transcripts throughout this loci or both. . Note that at least one protein coding gene has now been identified antisense to H19 (Onyango (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21940503), although its genomic location is only a small segment of the genomic region H19 antisense is hypothesized to cover.
H19 ICR ncRNAs	None known	Expression	Nuclear localised sense and antisense transcripts were expressed from the ICR. Transcripts came from both maternal and paternal alleles (Drewell (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11874916, Schoenfelder (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17948025).. Berteaux 08 also reported bi-allelic expression from the ICR region (Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369). 
H19 ICR ncRNAs	None known	Function	In a transgenic Drosophila system H19 ICR ncRNAs were necessary to silence a reporter gene, indicating that they may regulate imprinting of the Igf2 locus (Schoenfelder (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17948025).
H19 ICR ncRNAs	None known	Name	H19 imprinting control region (ICR) noncoding RNAs
H19 ICR ncRNAs	None known	Conservation	Mouse and human (Schoenfelder (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17948025, Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369).
H19 ICR ncRNAs	None known	Misc	Sequence and precise genome location of the transcripts have not been defined.
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Characteristics	Huc 1 & 2 are ~400bp conserved DNA elements separated by 1.4kb found ~10kb 5' of the H19 gene and the H19 ICR.. Both Huc 1 & 2 are transcribed producing individual transcripts which do not appear to join or overlap. 
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Expression	Huc1 and 2 were bi-allelically expressed as individual transcripts in same orientation as H19.. Expressed in a range of tissues in mid-gestation embryos, with only partial overlap to H19. No sign of antisense transcription as reported by Berteaux (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18794369 at this locus.
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Function	Huc1 & 2 acted as strong mesodermal enhancers in a transgenic enhancer assay. Likely drive mesodermal expression of H19.. Contribution of expressed RNAs to Huc enhancer function is unknown.
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Conservation	Mice and humans.
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Name	Huc: H19 upstream conserved
H19 upstream conserved 1 & 2	Huc 1 & 2	Misc	Sequence and precise genome location of the transcripts have not been defined.
HAR1A	HAR1F 	Characteristics	~2.8kb, spliced 2 exon transcript. Contains a 'human accelerated region' (HAR). Overlaps with an antisense noncoding RNA, HAR1B - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=232 (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Conserved HAR1 sequence (common to both HAR1A and HAR1B) forms a secondary structure which is highly conserved (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236) but has undergone changes from a hairpin structure in chimps to a cloverleaf structure in humans (Beniaminov (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18511501).
HAR1A	HAR1F 	Expression	Expressed in adult brain and during cortical development (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236). . Expressed in Cajal-Retzius neurons in the neocortex during early to mid-gestation (7-9 to 17-19 weeks) in humans and macaques (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).  . During mid-gestation expressed in developing hippocampus, dentate gyrus and cerebellar cortex in human. Expression was found in adult brain, ovary and testis (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Repressed transcriptionally by REST, which causes repression of HAR1A in the striatum of Huntington's disease patients (Johnson (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20179156). . The overlapping antisense RNA (HAR1B - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=232) is also expressed in adult brain (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. In mouse, locus is expressed during embryonic development (peak at E15) and in adults it is specifically expressed in the brain (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).
HAR1A	HAR1F 	Conservation	Contains a 'human accelerated region', which is a sequence highly conserved in amniotes (negative selection) but which has evolved rapidly in the human lineage (positive selection) since the divergence of humans and chimpanzees from the last common ancestor (18 bases out of 118 are different between human and chimpanzee but only 2 differences between chimpanzee and chicken) (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. HAR1A has orthologues in a number of closely mammals but in mouse and more distantly related species only the HAR1 sequence is conserved (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).
HAR1B	HAR1R	Characteristics	~900bp in humans. Contains a 'human accelerated region' (HAR). Overlaps with an antisense noncoding RNA, HAR1A - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=95 (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Two splice isoforms, one with 2 exons, one with 3 exons (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Conserved HAR1 sequence (common to both HAR1A and HAR1B) forms a secondary structure which is highly conserved (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236) but has undergone changes from a hairpin structure in chimps to a cloverleaf structure in humans (Beniaminov (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18511501).
HAR1B	HAR1R	Expression	Expression was found in adult brain, ovary and testis in human. Expression level was much lower than HAR1A - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=95 (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Repressed transcriptionally by REST, which causes repression of HAR1B in striatum of Huntington's disease patients (Johnson (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20179156).   . The mouse locus is expressed during embryonic development (peak at E15) and in adults it is specifically expressed in the brain. Unlike in human, "HAR1B" was expressed at similar levels to "HAR1A" in mouse (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).
HAR1B	HAR1R	Conservation	Contains a 'human accelerated region', which is a sequence highly conserved in amniotes (negative selection) but which has evolved rapidly in the human lineage (positive selection) since the divergence of humans and chimpanzees from the last common ancestor (18 bases out of 118 are different between human and chimpanzee but only 2 differences between chimpanzee and chicken) (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).. Rest of HAR1B sequence has little conservation outside of chimp and macaque (Pollard (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16915236).
HOTAIR	Gm16258	Characteristics	2.2 kb; spliced, polyadenylated and comprised of 6 exons in humans (Rinn (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17604720). . Transcribed from the HOXC locus from a position intergenic and antisense to the flanking HOXC11 and HOXC12 genes (Rinn (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17604720).
HOTAIR	Gm16258	Expression	Expressed in posterior and distal fibroblasts (Rinn (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17604720).. Expression level in cancer is an efficient predictor of metastasis and survival with high expression levels predictive of poor outcomes (Gupta (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20393566). Also in patients with stage IV colorectal cancer (CRC), HOTAIR expression levels were higher in cancerous tissues than in noncancerous tissues, with high HOTAIR expression tightly correlated with the presence of liver metastasis and associated with poor prognosis (Kogo (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21862635) .. Some HOTAIR transcripts localise to the nucleus (Khalil (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19571010).. In situ hybridization analysis of the mouse cognate RNA (mHotair) showed expression similar to Hoxc11, with distinct levels in parts of the proximal hindlimbs, genital bud and tail in embryos at E11.5, as well as in in posterior part of the hindlimb and genital bud at E12.5 (Schorderet (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21637793). . Transcript found to be quite unstable with a half-life >4 hr in human Hela cells (Tani (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22369889). 
HOTAIR	Gm16258	Function	Originally identified as silencing the HoxD locus but has since been found to epigenetic silence gene expression at many sites across the genome by recruitment of PRC2 and LSD1/CoREST/REST repressive chromatin modifying complexes (Rinn (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17604720, Tsai (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20616235).. HOTAIR acts as a scaffold for protein complexes. A 5' domain binds PRC2 while a 3' domain binds LSD1 (Tsai (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20616235).. Oncogene - regulates metastatic progression (Gupta (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20393566)(Schorderet (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21637793).. HOTAIR dysregulated in breast cancer with frequent overexpression in metastases. . Overexpression of HOTAIR leads to PRC2 re-targeting across the genome to a state similar to that in embryonic fibroblasts, promoting tumour invasion and metatasis.  Oncogenic effects of HOTAIR upregulation were dependent on PRC2 (Gupta (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20393566).. Deletion of the HoxC cluster containing the cognate Hotair transcript in mouse showed little phenotypic effect, with little change in the expression on levels of H3K27me3 coverage in corresponding human HOTAIR Hoxd target genes (Schorderet (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21637793).
HOTAIR	Gm16258	Conservation	HOTAIR exists in mammals but with poor sequence conservation (Rinn (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17604720)(He (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21496275). A 239 bp domain in HOTAIR exon 6 is especially conserved in mammals (He (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21496275).. The mouse EST (AK035706) homologous to human HOTAIR is comprised of two exons only, with the second half of the first exon showing similarity to exon 4 of HOTAIR, whereas the second exon is homologous to exon 6 of HOTAIR (Schorderet (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21637793). This may underlie differences in function since the first three exons of HOTAIR (absent from mHotair) contain binding sites for EZH2, while the 3' extremity of human HOTAIR that interact with LSD1 is part of the least conserved DNA sequence within mHotair exon 2 (Schorderet (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21637793).
HOTAIR	Gm16258	Name	Hox antisense intergenic RNA
HOTAIRM1	HIT06113, HIT92376, linc1548	Characteristics	Bidirectional transcript with HoxA1. Located between HOXA1 and HOXA2 genes (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766, Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990).. Identified transcript is 483 nt (Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990) but other splice isoforms are also likely to be expressed.
HOTAIRM1	HIT06113, HIT92376, linc1548	Expression	Expressed in the myeloid lineage (Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990). Has also been identified as showing a similar expression pattern to HoxA1 and A2 with expression in thymus, muscle, colon, lung, kidney, spleen etc (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. Induced by retinoic acid (RA) (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990).. Shows collinear regulation of expression like HOX PTC genes (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360).. Expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (ESCs) (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018)
HOTAIRM1	HIT06113, HIT92376, linc1548	Function	HOTAIRM plays a role in the regulation of gene expression during RA-induced myeloid differentiation (Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990). Knock-down of HOTAIRM prevented induction of HOXA1 and HOXA4 expression during myeloid differentiation as well as the induction of myeloid differentiation genes CD11b and CD18 (Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990).. Found to interact with a number of of chromatin binding proteins/complexes in mouse embryonic stem cells including PRC1, PRC2 and CBX1 (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).
HOTAIRM1	HIT06113, HIT92376, linc1548	Conservation	Sequence quite highly conserved in mammals, with transcripts also detected in mouse and rat (Zhang (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144990). 
HOTAIRM1	HIT06113, HIT92376, linc1548	Name	HOTAIRM1: HOX antisense intergenic RNA myeloid 1
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Characteristics	Gene located at 5â end of HoxA cluster, bidirectional transcript with HOXA13 (Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. ~3.8kb, transcript in human, spliced and polyadenylated (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. ~2.3kb transcript in mouse, different splice isoforms, currently known transcripts initiate downstream from the syntenic site in human. 
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Expression	Shows collinear regulation of expression like HOX protein coding genes (Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. Has bivalent chromatin marks (both H3 K4me3 and H3 K27me3) whether expression off or on, but only expressed in more distal cells (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. Has a similar expression profile to HOXA13, expressed in colon, prostate, placenta and uterus, as well as hand, foreskin and foot fibroblasts (Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17451645, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766, Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168). Mouse E13.5 in-situs gave similar results (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. Nuclear localised, generally to a single small nuclear spot (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. Lowly expressed, estimated at ~0.3 copies/cell in expressing tissues (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Conservation	Present in human and mouse. Portions of HOXA13as sequence are well conserved throughout mammals (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168). . Appears to be present in chicken although there is little homology (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. RNA contains some highly conserved sequences which are predicted to form a conserved structure (Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Misc	Background: Hox genes are found in 4 clusters. Genes in each cluster are expressed in certain tissues along body axes dependent on their position in the cluster. In the HoxA cluster genes near the 5â are expressed in more distal tissues while genes near the 3â are expressed in more proximal tissues.. Expressed genes have active chromatin marks and show close physical association (likely due to chromosomal looping). Inactive genes do not associate and have repressive chromatin marks (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168).. Human clone accession: GU724873. Mouse clone accession: BC046496
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Function	Summary:. Controls activation of 5â HOXA genes. Chromosomal lopping bring it into close association with 5â gene loci. HOTTIP binds WDR5 and recruits a MLL chromatin modifiying complex to maintain a domain of active chromatin over the 5â of HOXA cluster (Wang (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21423168). . - HOTTIP controls activation of 5â HOXA genes in mammals and chicken. . - Impact on HOXA genes decreases with increased genomic distance from HOTTIP.. - Phenotypic impact in chicken forelimb of HOTTIP knockdown was shorter than normal distal bones. . - HOTTIP doesnât affect chromosomal structure and looping but it was necessary for maintenance of H3 K4me3 chromatin marks over the distally expressed 5â half of the HOXA locus. HOTTIP RNA binds WDR5 a component of MLL/Trithorax complexes recruiting a MLL complex to lay down H3 K4me3 marks.. - WDR5 binding mediated by sequence(s) in 5â 1kb of HOTTIP. . HOTTIP appears to act in cis, its function is facilitated by the chromosomal looping that brings it into close proximity with 5â HOXA genes. 
HOTTIP	HOXA13as, HIT18844, NCRNA00213	Name	HOTTIP - HOXA transcript at the distal tip
Hoxa11as	Hoxa11s, Hoxa11os, NCRNA00076	Characteristics	Bidirectional promoter with HOXA11. Multiple splice isoforms are present which share a common 3' exon (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268, Potter (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9745033), only some overlap HOXA11 (Potter (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9745033).. Annotated human isoform is ~1.6kb. A number of isoforms including ~1.4, ~1.9, ~2.9 and ~3.2kb transcripts have been identified in mouse (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268).
Hoxa11as	Hoxa11s, Hoxa11os, NCRNA00076	Expression	More highly expressed than HOXA11 in mouse development (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268).. Expressed in developing limbs where it showed a complementary expression pattern to HOXA11 (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268). Also expressed in fetal kidney (Potter (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9745033),  placenta, adult colon, muscle and prostate (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766). Shows collinear regulation of expression like HOX PTC genes (Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. Expressed in same cell types as HOXA11 in the uterus. HOXA11as was dynamically expressed in the uterus during the menstrual cycle, with a peak in the endometrial late-proliferative phase, showing a pattern inverse to HOXA11 (Chau (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12050232). . HOXA11as levels were down-regulated by progesterone in primary uterine stromal cells, which correlated with HOXA11 up-regulation in the same cells (Chau (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12050232). 
Hoxa11as	Hoxa11s, Hoxa11os, NCRNA00076	Function	Due to the inverse or complementary expression pattern between Hoxa11 and HOXA11as mRNA expression levels, in the developing limbs (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268) and adult endometrium (Chau (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12050232), HOXA11as has been proposed to negatively regulate Hoxa11 mRNA levels (Chau (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12050232).
Hoxa11as	Hoxa11s, Hoxa11os, NCRNA00076	Conservation	Sequence highly conserved (Potter (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9745033), found throughout mammals.
Hoxa11as	Hoxa11s, Hoxa11os, NCRNA00076	Misc	Some HOXA11as isoforms have long ORFs, however these ORFs are not conserved between human and mouse (despite high nucleotide sequence conservation) (Hsieh-Li (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7789268, Potter (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9745033). So while HOXA11as is thought to be noncoding, a possible role for HOXA11as encoding a protein cannot be completely discounted.
HOXA3as	HIT12844, HIT94153	Characteristics	Antisense to the long isoform of HOXA3 and to the 3' end of HOXA4 (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. HOXA3as	HIT12844, HIT94153	Expression	Various antisense transcripts show similar expression profiles to each other and to HOXA3 and HOXA4. Expressed in the lung, kidney and testis (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).. Expression can be induced by retinoic acid (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360).. Shows collinear regulation of expression like HOX PTC genes (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).
HOXA3as	HIT12844, HIT94153	Conservation	Antisense transcripts to HoxA3 and HoxA4 also exist in mouse but unclear if they are homologous.

HOXA6as	HIT16800	Characteristics	Multiple spliced transcripts between HoxA6 and HOXA7 on the antisense strand, share some splice junctions but have different 5' and 3' ends (Sessa (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17185360, Sasaki (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17445766).  .  . HOXA6as	HIT16800	Expression	Expressed in adult lung, kidney, testis, placenta, colon, muscle. HOXA6as	HIT16800	Misc	Example accessions: AK091933, AK092154.
HOXA6as	HIT16800	Conservation	HOXA6as transcripts contain sequences conserved in mammals and even sequences ultra conserved in vertebrates.. Hoxd3as	Dxoh-3, Hoxd3os	Characteristics	Spliced antisense transcript. Northern identified transcripts of 2.8 and 1.5kb.. Partial cDNA clone started 3' of Hoxd3, contained homeobox in antisense direction and continued into the Hoxd3 intron.
Hoxd3as	Dxoh-3, Hoxd3os	Expression	Antisense transcript only found in a subset of tissues expressing Hoxd3.. Expressed in 12.5 day embryo liver along with sense Hoxd3 and in adult CNS tissue.
