hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs		hsr omega: heat shock RNA omega
hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs	Characteristics	Product of the 93D (or hsr-omega) locus, one of the largest heat-shock puffs in Drosophila polytene chromosomes. This locus produces three major long transcripts (by alternative polyadenylation and splicing) in all Drosophila species examined (reviewed in Jolly (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17020918). The locus spans 10â20 kb, composed of two small exons (~475 and 700 bp in Drosophila melanogaster) separated by a 700 bp intron, and followed by a long stretch (5â15 kb) of short (280 bp in D. melanogaster) tandem repeat units (Jolly (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17020918).. Long noncoding transcripts produced include three major hsr-omega transcripts, which share the same 5' end (Bendena (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1704862, Garbe (1986) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3097014):. Hsr-omega-n (omega-1) is >10kb-long and nuclear transcript that covers the entire length of the gene (including the tandem repeats), is polyadenylated, and retains the intron.. Hsr-omega-c (omega-3 ) is 1.2-kb, spliced and cytoplasmic. . The third common RNA, omega-pre-c (omega-2) is spliced to produce the mature omega-c transcript. It is 1.9kb-long and terminates at a first polyadenylation site located at the 3' end of exon 2.
hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs	Expression	Transcripts are constitutively expressed at relatively high levels in many tissues, in almost all cell types analysed, and are developmentally regulated (Lakhotia (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11255511)(Bendena (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1704862)(Mutsuddi (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8641048).. Transcripts were not detected in gonadal cell types such as male and female gonial cells and in follicle cells and oocytes in ovary. Polytenised tissues such as salivary glands, and certain regions of larval gut and the Malpighian tubules, showed a greater abundance of hsr-omega transcripts with a strong hybridization in nuclei (Bendena (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1704862). . Expression is stress-induced, being highly active after heat exposure, but also responsive to other stresses such as amides benzamide and colchicine (Tapadia (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9364937).. Nuclear hsr-omega-n is localized in nuclear granules called omega-speckles (Sengupta (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17114940, Bendena (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1704862, Prasanth (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10984439).
hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs	Function	Flies null for Hsr-omega mostly die at embryonic stage, and the surviving flies are weak, sterile and die within a few days of emergence (Jolly (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17020918).. Transcribed from a locus involved in the heat shock response in Drosophila. hsr-omega-n nuclear transcripts form complexes with various hnRNP proteins and related proteins in nucleoplasmic omega-speckles, distributed in the interchromatin space in close proximity to the chromatin (Sengupta (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17114940, Bendena (1991) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/1704862, Prasanth (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10984439).. Many proteins are found associated with the hsr-omega-n transcripts, including: (i) various hnRNPs Hrp40 (hnRNP A), Hrb87F (hnRNP A1/A2), Hrb57A (hnRNP K), Hrb98DE (44); (ii) other nuclear RNA-binding proteins like NonA, PEP, Sxl, nuclear non-histone proteins recognized by Q14, Q16, T29, P75 antibodies; (iii) Snf; (iv) Hsp83 and (v) Tpr (see Jolly (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17020918 for review and references).. Omega speckles disappear after heat shock, except from the hsr-omega/93D locus, and speckled distribution of associated hnRNPs is disrupted in hsr-omega nullosomics (Prasanth (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10984439). It is suggested that the ncRNA may regulate the availability of hnRNPs in active (chromatin bound) and inactive (in omega-speckles) compartments and interfere with the processing of pre-mRNAs in cyst cells (Rajendra (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11910129).. Altered expression of the hsr omega RNAs enhances poly-Q-induced neurotoxicity in Drosophila (Sengupta (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17114940, Mallik (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19667761, Fernandez-Funez (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11081516).
hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs	Conservation	The hsr-omega/93D locus and genomic organization is conserved among Drosophila species. However, the hsr-omega transcripts have poor sequence conservation among different Drosophila species (Garbe (1986) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3097014), but, similar to other ncRNAs, have short stretches of conservation.
hsr omega transcripts	hsr(omega) RNA, omega1-3 RNAs	Misc	Heat shock puffs in Chironomus genus also produce non-conding transcripts analogous to Drosophila  hsr omega transcripts, and interaction of Hsp90 with puffs is dependent on transcription (Morcillo (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8306827). Analogy is also drawn with non-related human heat-shock induced Satellite III (Sat III) transcripts (Jolly (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17020918).. Natural variation in hsr-omega expression influence rates of protein synthesis in Drosophila lines (Johnson (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19280368).. Small open reading frames (ORFs) present in hsr-omega are poorly conserved in different Drosophila species. A short ORF of 23â27 amino acids present in the hsr-omega-c sequence of three examined Drosophila species is translatable, but the predicted protein has not been detected (Fini (1989) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/2500443).
Hsr1	None known	Characteristics	~600 nt. Likely to be unspliced and does not have a polyA tail (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823).
Hsr1	None known	Expression	Constitutively expressed (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823). . Appears to undergo some sort of conformation change upon heat shock (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823).
Hsr1	None known	Function	Required for the heat shock response (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823).. HSR1 and eEF1A (eukaryotic translation elongation factor 1) are required to activate heat shock factor 1 (HSF1) upon heat shock. HSR1 binds to eEF1A upon heat shock, which then forms a complex with HSF1 (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823).. Knockdown/inhibition of HSR1 prevents HSF1 activation and makes cells heat shock sensitive (Shamovsky (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16554823).
Hsr1	None known	Conservation	604 nuc HSR1 seq couldn't be found in any mammalian genome examined, nor in expressed sequence libraries (Kim (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20040589).. 3' of HSR1 shows nucleotide and protein sequence homology to bacterial chloride channel proteins (Kim (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20040589).. Sequence is most similar to chloride channel from bacterial species of order Burkholderiales.. Unclear if this is horizontal gene transfer or due to bacterial infection of the studied cells (Kim (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20040589).
Hsr1	None known	Misc	Robust experimental results for functionality of HSR1, despite uncertainty regarding its origins.
Hsr1	None known	Name	Hsr1: Heat shock RNA 1
HSUR1 and HSUR2	None known		Encoded by Herpesvirus saimiri, acts as a target mimic to miR-27, directing its degradation and manipulating host T cell gene expression. Similar to mechanism in murine cytomegalovirus.
HULC	None known	Characteristics	~500nuc, spliced, polyadenylated, two exon transcript (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).. Exon 1 mainly consists of an LTR (MLT1A) (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).
HULC	None known	Expression	Binding of phospho-CREB to the HULC promoter activates HULC expression. Phosphorylation of CREB was stimulated by PKA signaling (Wang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20423907). . Highly up-regulated in hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC) and to a lesser extent in liver focal nodular hyperplasia (FNH). Up-regulation was specific to HCC with high expression not detected in normal liver, other tissues and their associated neoplasms (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).. HULC expression was also up-regulated in colorectal carcinomas that metastasised to the liver but not in primary colorectal carcinomas or carcinomas that metastasised to lymph nodes (Matouk (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19445043).. HULC RNA could be detected in the blood of HCC patients (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).. Localised to the cytoplasm, may associate with ribosomes, but no sign of translated products could be found (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).. HULC expression was also identified in 3 old world monkeys (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).
HULC	None known	Function	Competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). Functions as a sponge/ target mimic for miR-372 through a conserved target site, reducing the expression and activity of miR-372 (Wang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20423907).. One of targets of miR-372 is Prkacb (catalytic subunit of PKA) which is able to phophorylate CREB. Hence expression of HULC stimulates further HULC expression by inhibiting miR-372, and allowing PRKACB to create active CREB (Wang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20423907).. HULC knockdown affects expression of other genes including some described in liver cancer (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).
HULC	None known	Conservation	HLUC also present in other primates, gene shows good conservation above that of surrounding sequence. Not detected in rodents so may be primate specific (Panzitt (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17241883).
HULC	None known	Name	HULC: Highly upregulated in liver cancer RNA
ICR1	None known	Characteristics	~3.15kb capped and polyadenylated single exon transcript.. Expressed in FLO11 regulatory region.. ICR1 has variable start and termination sites. Begins between ~3.2 and 3.4kb upstream of FLO11, runs towards FLO11 in sense direction, some transcripts stop before FLO11 while others can overlap the 5' of the PTC gene.. A second 1.2kb lncRNA PWR1 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyID=236 is expressed antisense to ICR1.
ICR1	None known	Expression	Expression of ICR1 and PWR1 is inversely correlated. . ICR1 expression requires the Sfl1 transcription factor, which is known to repress FLO11, and is repressed by the Flo8 transcription factor and the Rpd3L HDAC protein.. PWR1 expression requires Rpd3L and Flo8 and is repressed by Sfl1.
ICR1	None known	Function	ICR1 regulates expression of the FLO11/MUC1 gene in cis, in conjunction with a second lncRNA PWR1 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyID=236.. Expression of ICR1 represses expression of FLO11, probably by promoter occlusion. . Expression of ICR1 is repressed by PWR1 (again probably by promoter occlusion in-cis), allowing expression of FLO11, so the regulatory circuit depends on whether PWR1 is expressed or repressed.. ICR1 is lowly expressed constitutively and competition between Flo8 and Sfl1 transcription factors determines which ncRNA is expressed and therefore if FLO11 is on or off.
ICR1	None known	Misc	FLO11/ MUC1 - cell surface glycoprotein that controls cell-cell adhesion and shows variegated expression in a clonal population of yeast cells (ie: expressed at high levels in some cells, silenced in others).. Sequence of ICR1 on chromosome IX from coordinates 397079 to 393881 available from http://www.yeastgenome.org/cgi-bin/locus.fpl?sgdid=S000132612
ICR1	None known	Name	ICR1: interfering Crick RNA 1
IGF2AS	PEG8	Characteristics	Spliced transcript from bidirectional promoter with Igf2. Overlaps some Igf2 isoforms in antisense direction (mouse and human).. ~4.8kb mouse transcript, four exons. Multiple splice isoforms in human, 2 or 3 exons, ~2 or ~2.8kb. Most homology is towards 3' of transcripts (Okutsu (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10731720).
IGF2AS	PEG8	Expression	Imprinted, expressed from paternal allele (Okutsu (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10731720). Igf2as generally retains imprinting in tumours even when Igf2 becomes bi-allelically expressed (Vu (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12702581). . Ubiquitously, but lowly, expressed in human adult and fetal tissues. 2 exon (has retained intron) isoform was specific to adult liver (Vu (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12702581). . Like Igf2, Igf2as showed highly up-regulated expression in Wilms tumour samples compared to neighbouring normal kidney tissue. 
IGF2AS	PEG8	Function	SNP polymorphisms in Igf2as associate with increased muscle damage (strength loss and soreness) after eccentric exercise, as do SNPs found in IGF2 (Devaney (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17289909).
IGF2AS	PEG8	Conservation	Human Igf2as contains a predicted ORF, however this is not present in mouse (Okutsu (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10731720).. Also expressed and imprinted in pig (Bischoff (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19571260).
IGF2AS	PEG8	Name	IGF2AS: Insulin-like growth factor 2 antisense . PEG8: Paternally expressed gene 8
IPS1	TPSI/Mt4 family	Characteristics	IPS1 is a member of a family of RNAs induced by phosphate starvation in plants that have short non-conserved ORFs (Liu (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9106510, Burleigh (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9207836, Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506) and a region of complementarity to miR-399  (Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. IPS1	TPSI/Mt4 family	Expression	Expression induced upon phosphate starvation and accumulates into the roots and shoots (MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795).. Hormonal signaling by cytokinins repressed IPS1 expression in the roots (MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795).
IPS1	TPSI/Mt4 family	Function	IPS1 has complementarity to miR-399, but contains a mismatch loop that renders it uncleavable when miR-399 binds. Since target cleavage is the usual plant miRNA pathway the non-cleavable nature of IPS1 acts to sequester the miRNA (Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).. Competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). IPS1 carries out target mimicry to sequester miR-399 and attenuate its effects allowing increased expression of miR-399 targets including PHO2 (Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101).
IPS1	TPSI/Mt4 family	Conservation	IPS1 family members have been identified in a number of plant species (Liu (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9106510, Burleigh (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9207836, Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, MartÃ­n (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11123795, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506, Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101). . However apart from At4 and IPS1 homology between family members is generally limited to the miR-399 binding site (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506).
IPS1	TPSI/Mt4 family	Misc	Other family members include At4 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/detail.aspx?TKeyid=215, At4-1 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/42741749, At4-2 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/41396887 and At4-3 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nucest/5842364?report=genbank in Arabidopsis thaliana (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366, Shin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16460506 Franco-Zorrilla (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17643101), TPS11 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/1009717?report=genbank  in tomato (Liu (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9106510), Mt4 - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/2231317 in Barrel Clover and Alfalfa (Burleigh (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9207836), Mt4-like in Soybean (Burleigh (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9880366).

Jpx	Enox, NCRNA00183	Names	Jpx; Enox (expressed neighbor of Xist)
Jpx	Enox, NCRNA00183	Characteristics	Spliced (5 exons), with multiple isoforms. Located at the X-inactivation center (XIC), transcribed from an unmethylated CpG island 10 kb upstream of Xist. Transcribed in antisense orientation to Xist. (Johnston (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12160738)
Jpx	Enox, NCRNA00183	Expression	Ubiquitously expressed.. Up-regulated during both male and female embryonic stem cell differentiation (Tian (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21029862).
Jpx	Enox, NCRNA00183	Function	Involved in the regulation of X chromosome inactivation in mammals via activation of the Xist RNA, possibly by interfering with Tsix expression (Tian (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21029862).. Jpx seems to act in trans, as its deletion prevents Xist up-regulation also from the Xist allele on the wild type chromosome (Tian (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21029862).
Jpx	Enox, NCRNA00183	Conservation	First exon is highly conserved in mouse, human and cow (Chureau (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045143).
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Characteristics	91 kb, unspliced; imprinted (paternally expressed), it is transcribed from intron 10 of the maternally expressed Kncq1 (KvLQT1) gene from a CpG island that is the imprinting control region (IC2) (Smilinich (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10393948). This imprinted region contains at least eight genes that are expressed exclusively or preferentially from the maternal allele (Kanduri (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21345374).
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Expression	Nuclear localised. . Expressed in most human tissues.. Mouse RNA found to be highly unstable with a half-life <2 hr in N2A (neuroblastoma) cells (Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755)
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Function	Summary: Kcnq1ot1 has a role in the organization of a tissue/lineage-specific nuclear domain involved in epigenetic silencing of the Kcnq1 imprinting control region.. Genes imprinted by kcnq1ot1 include Kcnq1, Cdkn1c, Slc22a18 and Phlda2, which are ubiquitously imprinted and Cd81, Osbpl5, Tssc4, Tspan32 and Ascl2, which are only imprinted in placenta (reviewed in Kanduri (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21345374. An expansion of the Kncq1ot1 imprinted domain to include splice variants of Th and Ins2 was recently described (Jones (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21576366). . Kcnq1ot1 silences genes by coating chromatin and recruiting repressive chromatin remodeling complexes such as G9a, PRC1 and PRC2 (Terranova (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18848501, Pandey (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18951091, Umlauf (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15516932, Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659) .. Kcnq1ot1 transcript has a modular structure, the silencing element (that mediates the epigenetic silencing and directs the imprinted locus to a heterochromatin environment in the perinucleolar region) appears to be a short <1kb conserved sequence near the 5' of the transcript (Mohammad (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18299392).. Kcnq1ot1 forms a silenced subdomain (Terranova (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18848501)(Redrup (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19144718) commonly localised to the perinucleolar region during S phase (Mohammad (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18299392). The silenced subdomain may be important to the maintenance of transcriptional repression.. Kcnq1ot1 interacts with Dnmt1 and recruits it to somatically acquired differentially methylated regions (DMRs) of imprinted genes (Mohammad (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20573698).. In vivo knockout study shows that paternal inheritance of a deletion encompassing an 890-bp (Delta890) silencing domain downstream of the Kcnq1ot1 promoter leads reduced interaction with DNMT1 and to selective incomplete relaxation of the imprinting of imprinted genes in a tissue-specific manner (Mohammad (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20573698).. Delta890 showed altered DNA methylation at somatically acquired DMRs but not in histone modifications of the ubiquitously imprinted genes. Thus, it has been proposed that the ubiquitous and placental-specific imprinting of genes within the Kcnq1 domain might be mediated by distinct mechanisms, and Kcnq1ot1 RNA might mediate the silencing of ubiquitously imprinted genes by maintaining allele-specific methylation through its interactions with Dnmt1 (Mohammad (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20573698).
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Conservation	Patches of highly conserved repeats in 5' side of transcript, which contains the silencing domain (Mohammad (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18299392). Promoter control elements are highly conserved between mouse and humans, including CCAAT elements that are targets of NF-Y regulation (Pandey (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15459184), as well as the position of CpG islands in the imprinting control region (Paulsen (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15590939).
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Misc	(Syndromes and diseases associated, eg Beckwith-Wiedemann syndrom, and cancers (see references list):. Associated with multiple balanced chromosomal rearrangements in Beckwith-Wiedemann syndrome (BWS) and an additional break-point in embryonal rhabdoid tumours; in particular, aberrant methylation of the CpG island associated with Kcnq1ot1 promoter is strongly associated with cancer risk and specific birth defects in BWS (Smilinich (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10393948)). . For review on Kcnq1ot1 mechanism of action see (Kanduri (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21345374).
Kcnq1ot1	LIT1, KvLQT1-AS, KvLQT1OT1	Name	Kcnq1ot1: Kcnq1 opposite transcript 1. LIT1: long QT intronic transcript 1

	Characteristics	Spliced two exon transcript.. Multiple splice variants, ~550- ~750 nt in length, second exon varies.. Expressed bidirectionally with KDM5B.. In-vitro translation showed no sign of protein product.

Khps1a	Khps1	Characteristics	1290 nt*; originates from the CpG island and overlaps a "tissue-dependent differentially methylated region" (T-DMR) of Sphk1. Single-exon, 5'-capped and 3'-polyadenylated, it spans the region -2095 to -3384 in relation to the commonly used +1 translation start site for Sphk1 subtypes, which covers the entire region of the T-DMR (-3233 to -3023) and the alternative first exons of both Sphk1a and -c (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).. *Northern blot with probes for Khps1 also indicates the presence of transcripts with different sizes (600-20,000nt).
Khps1a	Khps1	Expression	Expression of Khps1 is detected in many tissues, with high levels in the kidney and only weakly expressed in the liver and brain. Expression was detected in the cytoplasm of primary cell culture from rat  fetuses, as well as nuclei in some cells, indicating that Khps1 is exported to the cytoplasm (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).. Similar to Sphk1, the expression of Khps1 is also detected from only one allele (demonstrating that it is also imprinted), and Khps1 and Sphk1 show mutually exclusive expression in individual cells (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).. Identified as a PROMPT (promoter upstream transcript) which are degraded by the exosome and generally highly unstable (Preker (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19056938).
Khps1a	Khps1	Function	Regulates DNA methylation in the T-DMR of Sphk1 promoter (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271; Preker (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19056938). In vitro over-expression of two fragments of Khps1 in NRK cells cause demethylation of CG sites of the T-DMR, but which is accompanied of DNA methylation at three CC(A/T)GG sites (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).
Khps1a	Khps1	Conservation	Rat Khps1a exhibits 88.7% and 56.2% nucleotide sequence identity with corresponding DNA sequences in the genome databases at NCBI for human and mouse  (Accession Nos. NT_1010641 and NT_039521), respectively (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).. ESTs overlapping Sphk1 T-DMR CpG island in mouse, homologous to the CpG island of rat Sphk1, are described (mouse EST AA796730 shows 87% similarity with the CpG island of rat  Sphk1). Human transcripts in the region were also detected by RT-PCR in HEK293 and HeLa cells (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).
Khps1a	Khps1	Misc	There are possible open reading frames in Khps1a, in which the maximal size is 306 bp, but no recognizable amino acid motifs or domains in the possible proteins were found, and three possible start codons in the rat  Khps1a aligned with different codons in the corresponding human genomic DNA sequences (Imamura (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15325271).
Khps1a	Khps1	Name	Khps1a : Sphk1a antisense transcript
KRASP1	None known	Characteristics	Processed pseudogene of KRAS oncogene on 6p12-p11 (McGrath (1983) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6308466).
KRASP1	None known	Function	Probable competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). linc-MD1		Characteristics	Three exon transcript. Contains miR-206 in second intron and miR-133b in third and final exon. Has binding sites for miR-135 in exon2 and miR-133 in exon 3. This structure is conserved in mouse and humans.. Shows evidence of alternative splicing of exon 2 in mouse. This alternative isoform no longer contains the miR-135 binding sites. Functional characterization was on the standard isoform containing the miRNA recognition sequences.. PolyA+
linc-MD1		Expression	Expression induced during myoblast differentiation but absent in proliferating myoblasts in mouse and humans.. In mouse tissues expression was restricted to certain skeletal muscles where it was found only in "newly regenerating fibres". Expression is found more widely found amongst skeletal muscle of mutant mice which do not express dystrophin. . Conversely in myoblasts from humans with Duchenne Muscular Dystrophy (DMD), there was little linc-MD1 expression and MYOG and MHC expression was also reduced.  . Predominately cytoplasmic.. Promoter regions near the linc-MD1 and miR-206 TSSs contain conserved CANNTG (E-box) sequences, and are bound by the muscle transcription factor MyoD. During myoblast differentiation and in muscles where linc-MD1 is expressed these promoter regions (plus others) form long distance chromatin interactions.
linc-MD1		Function	Competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). Binds miR-135 and miR-133 and inhibits their repressive action, including on MEF2C and MAML1, two transcription factors required for proper muscle differentiation.. linc-MD1 required for normal up-regulation of MYOG, MHC and MCK genes during myoblast differentiation. . Nb: These linc-MD1 effects were also observed when linc-MD1 was mutated so miR-133b could not be released from the sequence, showing this effect was due to the lincRNA transcript. 
linc-MD1		Conservation	Exon 1 and the region of exon 3 containing miR-133b is conserved in mammals and also back to chicken. Exon 2 conserved in mammals.
linc-MD1		Misc	Expression of miR-206 and miR-133b is specific to muscle tissue. miR-133b expression profile closely corresponds to that of linc-MD1.. Sequence provided is only partial length, it was reported that the transcript 3' ends are 1060 and 1450 nt further downstream.

LincRNA-p21 is necessary for p53-dependent apoptotic induction, but not cell cycle arrest.

LINoCR	None known	Characteristics	Antisense RNA from the lysozyme regulatory region.. Promoter is -1.9kb hormone response element. Transcript extends several hundred nucleotides from a -2.120bp start site through the -2.4kb CTCF binding site to the -2.7kb enhancer.

This demonstrated that LINoCR expression was necessary for CTCF eviction.. Whether the LINoCR transcript has a function or if it is simply the act of transcription which is necessary is unknown.

LOC100887755	Noncoding RNA activating7: ncRNA-a7, ENST00000431460.1
	Characteristics	Two exon, 600 nt transcript. Around 50 kb 3â from SNAI1 on the opposite strand.. In-vitro translation showed no sign of protein product.
LOC100887755	Noncoding RNA activating7: ncRNA-a7, ENST00000431460.1
	Expression	Expressed in A549 cells.
LOC100887755	Noncoding RNA activating7: ncRNA-a7, ENST00000431460.1
	Function	LncRNA regulates gene expression through SNAI1 dependant and independent mechanisms. . Stimulates SNAI1 gene expression (in A549 cells) and like SNAI1 is required for cell migration.. Stimulates Aurora-kinase A (AURKA) expression, a gene found ~6 megabases from LOC100887755 on chr20. LOC285194	LSAMP-AS3	Features	Together with the noncoding RNA BC040587 and the tumor suppressor gene LSAMP (limbic system-associated membrane protein), LOC285194 is present in the focal region of chr3q13.31 (osteo3q13.31), which is the most altered region in osteosarcomas. These genes are proposed to be cooperatively acting tumor suppressors.. Recurrent focal copy-number changes and loss of heterozygosity (LOH), which usually involves loss of LOC285194 and BC040587 expression, implicate these ncRNAs in ostecosarcoma. Focal osteo3q13.31 CNAs and LOH are also common in cell lines from several other cancers (such as lung, autonomic and central nervous system, blood, endometrium, soft tissue, skin, gastrointestinal tract, urinary tract, and breast).. Depletion of LOC285194 by siRNA promoted proliferation of normal osteoblasts (with a mild increase in the G1 population) by cell-cycle transcripts (Cyclin D1, VEGF, and VEGFR1 up-regulation, and cyclin A2 and cyclin B1 suppression) as well as regulation of apoptotic genes (such as suppression of BCL2 and BimEL pro-apoptotic genes).. Genetic deletions of LOC285194 or BC040587 in  tumor DNA were also associated with dramatic decrease in survival of osteosarcoma patients.
LUST	Je2	Characteristics	~1.4 - 2.4 kb. Intronic, unspliced and transcribed antisense to the putative tumour suppressor gene RBM5/LUCA-15/H37, spanning introns 6 to 4 (Rintala-Maki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19559772).. Contains SINE elements.
LUST	Je2	Expression	Originally cloned from an human bone marrow library (Sutherland (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10949932), this transcript is abundant in skeletal and cardiac muscle (as detected by Northern blot) (Rintala-Maki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19559772).
LUST	Je2	Function	*Transfection of Jurkat T cells with a 326 bp fragment of LUST (originally termed Je2) suppresses CD95-mediated apoptosis (Sutherland (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10949932).. *Ectopic over-expression of LUST affects splicing of RBM5: it correlates with elevated expression of the full-length RBM5+5+6 splice variant, and with reduced expression of the truncated RBM5+5+6t isoform, which is cytotoxic (Rintala-Maki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19559772). 
LUST	Je2	Name	LUST: LUCA-15-specific transcript.
LXRBSV	None known	Characteristics	In mouse, LXRBSV is an alternative splicing isoform of LXR-beta that has a 270bp intronic sequence retained between exons 4 and 5 (or exons 2 and 3 depending on LXR-beta isoform). Quantitative expression and promoter reporter assays indicated that LXRBSV is preferentially transcribed and expressed in the pituitary (Hashimoto (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20211147).. 5'-rapid amplification of cDNA ends (5'-RACE) produced a 677 bp PCR product and indicated that the transcriptional start site (TSS) of LXRBSV is located 40 bp downstream of LXR-beta's TSS (Hashimoto (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20211147).. A LXRBSV construct was translated as an approximately 22 kDa protein by in-vitro translation.
LXRBSV	None known	Expression	LXRBSV was detected in various tissues, such as liver and different regions of the brain (pituitary, hypothalamus, cerebrum, cerebellum). It was expressed at lower levels than LXR-beta (Hashimoto (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19878653).. Quantitative expression and promoter reporter assays indicated that LXRBSV is preferentially transcribed and expressed in the pituitary. LXRBSV expression in the whole brain and especially in the pituitary was significantly higher compared to that in the liver. This is in contrast to LXR-beta mRNA that showed similar expression in the liver and brain and significantly reduced expression in the pituitary and hypothalamus compared to liver (Hashimoto (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20211147).
LXRBSV	None known	Function	LXRBSV acts as a specific transcriptional co-activator for LXR-beta to enhance its receptor-mediated transactivation. LXRBSV synergistically augmented ligand-dependent activation of the SREBP-1c promoter (Sterol Response Element Binding Protein-1c promoter), but not of thyroid hormone receptor (TR) and peroxidase proliferator and activating receptors (PPARs).. The intronic sequence inserted into LXRBSV is required for its transactivation activity.. LXRBSV protein was deduced to be 64 amino acids in length, but different evidence demonstrated that the alternative splicing transcript acts as a RNA co-activator: 1) a GAL4-LXRBSV fusion protein was not able to induce transactivation; 2) an ATG mutant of LXRBSV was able to induce transactivation as wild type, and 3) LXRBSV functions in the presence of cycloheximide (Hashimoto (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19878653).
LXRBSV	None known	Name	LXRBSV: Liver X receptor (LXR)-beta alternative splicing variant (Hashimoto (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19878653).
LXRBSV	None known	Misc	Because the LXRB locus produces both functional protein-coding and regulatory RNA transcripts, it may be considered a 'bi-functional' locus.
Malat1	Neat2	Characteristics	Intergenic ~7kb single exon transcript (Ji (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12970751, Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048).. A conserved tRNA-like sequence at the 3' end is cleaved off and processed to generated a short tRNA-like ncRNA mascRNA (MALAT1-associated small cytoplasmic RNA) (Wilusz (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19041754).. Post transcriptional processing of Malat1 therefore allows two ncRNAs to be created from the one original transcript (Wilusz (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19041754).
Malat1	Neat2	Expression	Both Malat1 and the processed mascRNA transcript are expressed in a wide range of tissues (Ji (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12970751, Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048, Wilusz (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19041754), Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808), (Ulitsky (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22196729). . Malat1 is highly expressed in the brain. RNA fluorescence in-situ hybridization (RNA-FISH) on adult mouse brain sections showed high expression of nuclear-localized Malat1 transcripts in pyramidal neurons of the hippocampus, Purkinje cells of the cerebellum and neurons of the substantia nigra and motoneurons, but very low levels in non-neuronal cells (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808). In the hippocampus and in Purkinje cells, Malat1 was first detected between post-natal day 0 (P0) and P7 and its level increased until P28 (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808). This high expression appears to come from up-regulation of Malat1 during differentiation, with in-vitro differentiation of neural stem cells showing significant up-regulation of expression in neuronal and glial differentiated progeny (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).. Expressed in the nucleus accumbens of normal human brains and upregulated in this brain region in heroin abusers (Michelhaugh (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21128942). . In neuroblastoma cells Malat1 was up-regulated by the hormone oxytocin (Koshimizu (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20149803). . Malat1 is up-regulated in a range of cancers (Ji (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12970751, Yamada (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16441420, Lin (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16878148, Guffanti (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19379481).. High expression of Malat1 is associated with metastasis in certain histological subtypes of non-small cell lung cancer (NSCLC) and is predictive of poor prognosis (Ji (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12970751).. Malat1 is up-regulated in placenta previa increta/percreta, a disease characterised by excessive invasion of fetal placental trophoblasts into the uterus  (Tseng (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19690017).. Malat1 is stable in human B cells and Hela and wt MEFs (half-life >7 hrs) but has significantly lower stability in mouse 3T3 and N2A cells. Suggesting differences in Malat1 stability both within and between species (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755, Tani (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22369889).. Malat1 localises to SC35 domain nuclear speckles in several cell lines (Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048) (Clemson (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19217333). Localisation to nuclear speckles is transcription-dependent, as RNA pol II inhibition promoted re-distribution of Malat1 ncRNA from nuclear speckles to a homogenous nuclear localisation (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808). Malat1 co-localises with pre-mRNA-splicing factor SF2/ASF and CC3 antigen in the nuclear speckles (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808).. MALAT1 is enriched in nuclear speckles in interphase cells and concentrates in mitotic interchromatin granule clusters (IGCs, structural analogs of nuclear speckles present in mitotic cells), but unlike Neat1 it is not required for the structural integrity of the nuclear domain (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886).. mascRNA derived from Malat1 is transported to the cytoplasm (Wilusz (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19041754).
Malat1	Neat2	Conservation	Therian mammals (found in oppossum as well as placental mammals) (Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048).. Recently described in zebrafish. Sequence homology to zebrafish was limited to the 3â end, but the ~7kb long, single exon structure as well as positional synteny was conserved, as was the high expression in brain found identified in mammals (Ulitsky (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22196729).
Malat1	Neat2	Name	Malat1: Metastasis-associated lung adenocarcinoma transcript 1. Neat2: Nuclear enriched abundant transcript 2
Malat1	Neat2	Function	Summary: Malat1 has been found to regulate alternative splicing of endogenous target genes, and it is implicated in cancer and a series of molecular and cellular phenotypes, as indicated below.. Identified as an oncogene that promotes tumorigensis. Expression of a Malat1 fragment in NIH 3T3 cells transformed cells (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619). . Knockdown inhibited cell mobility and lead to decreased expression of several genes (CTHRC1, CCT4, HMMR, or ROD1) that promoted cell migration (Tano (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20937273). This result may also explain why knockdown inhibited trophoblast-like cell invasion in-vitro, with MALAT1 hypothesised to regulate the level of trophoblast invasion into the uterus in vivo (Tseng (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19690017).. MALAT1 depletion resulted in aberrant mitosis, with a large fraction of cells accumulating at G2/M boundary, and increased cell death (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886).. Depletion of Malat1 in neuroblastoma cells indicated that Malat1 affects the expression of genes involved not only in the organization and the function of the nucleus, but also in synapse function and dendrite development. In cultured hippocampal neurons, knock-down of Malat1 decreased synaptic density, whereas its over-expression resulted in a cell-autonomous increase in synaptogenesis (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808).. There is a significant enrichment for SRSF1 (SF2/ASF) binding sites within the 5' half of both human and mouse MALAT1, whose direct interaction has been demonstrated, and is dependent on its canonical RRM (RRM1) or the pseudo RRM (RRM2) domains (Sanford (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19116412, Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886). Independent sequence elements in MALAT1 influence its distribution to nuclear speckles and the recruitment of SRSF1 (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886).. Additional interactions have been found between MALAT1 and SRSF1, SRSF2, and SRSF3 proteins, but only weak interactions with SRSF5 and PSP1 (an RNA-binding protein that is a component of paraspeckles) have been identified (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886).. Knock-down of nuclear Malat1 in a transfected U2OS cell line showed that it modulates the recruitment of SR proteins (SRSF1 or SF2/ASF and SC35) to a transcriptionally active transgene array (stably integrated), indicating a role in the regulation of the association of pre-mRNA-splicing factors to transcription sites and control of post-transcriptional gene expression (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808). Malat1 modulates the speckle association of a subset of pre-mRNA splicing factors, such as SF1, U2AF-65, SF3a60, and B-U2snRNP (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886).. Malat1-depleted HeLa cells show increased cellular levels of dephosphorylated SRSF1 (SF2/ASF) (Bernard (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20729808), as well as a moderately increased cytoplasmic pool of poly(A)+ RNA (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886). It has recently been shown to regulate alternative splicing of endogenous target genes by modulating SR splicing factor phosphorylation, affecting their levels and the distribution and ratio of phosphorylated to dephosphorylated pools (Tripathi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20797886). 
Malat1-as	Malat1 antisense, Neat2 antisense	Characteristics	Northern identifies a transcript of around 6kb.
Malat1-as	Malat1 antisense, Neat2 antisense	Expression	Identified in mouse embyonic stem cells (mESCs).
Malat1-as	Malat1 antisense, Neat2 antisense	Function	Binds PRC2 chromatin modifying complex, while the sense Malat1/Neat2 transcript does not.
Malat1-as	Malat1 antisense, Neat2 antisense	Misc	As the transcript itself is not defined no accurate ucsc browser link is possible, although it's putative length combined with the PCR primers and northern probe utilized by Zhao 2010 suggest a significant overlap with Malat1.
mascRNA	Malat1	Characteristics	mascRNA is a conserved, 61 nucleotide, tRNA-like sequence at the 3' end of Malat1 that is cleaved off the full length transcript and processed to generate a short tRNA-like ncRNA.. Mature mascRNA undergoes a post-transcriptional CCA addition and folds into a tRNA like structure but could not be amino acylated.
mascRNA	Malat1	Name	mascRNA (MALAT1-associated small cytoplasmic RNA)
mascRNA	Malat1	Conservation	Conserved in mammals and back to reptiles and amphibians. More highly conserved than most of Malat1.
mascRNA	Malat1	Expression	mascRNA was cleaved off Malat1 in a wide variety of human tissues. . mascRNA is cleaved off Malat1 by RNaseP in the nucleus before further processing by RNaseZ and then exported to the cytoplasm.
Maternal RNA templates	Oxytricha trifallax genome unscrambling guide RNAs	Characteristics & Expression	Template/ Guide RNAs believed to arise from the maternal somatic nucleus (Nowacki (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18046331).. Long sense and antisense RNA transcripts, which appear to be transcribed full length nanochromsomes (contained telomere sequences), from the somatic nucleus were identified during early development when rearrangement is believed to be occurring (Nowacki (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18046331).
Maternal RNA templates	Oxytricha trifallax genome unscrambling guide RNAs	Function	Maternal RNAs programming DNA rearrangements in progeny (Nowacki (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18046331).. Act as RNA guides or scaffolds to direct rearrangements. RNAi against them prevented unscrambling and injection of guides with altered gene sequences lead to the rearranged DNA containing the alteration (Nowacki (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18046331).. Cellular machinery required to carry out the DNA fragmentation and recombination is not fully understood but transposase proteins from Oxytricha trifallax transposons are required (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19372392).. Also found that mutations in guide RNA can be transferred to the rearranged somatic genome. Suggesting the presence of RNA directed DNA repair and also of DNA variants inherited via RNA without changing the germline genome (Nowacki (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18046331).
Maternal RNA templates	Oxytricha trifallax genome unscrambling guide RNAs	Inheritance	Non-mendelian epigenetic inheritance, independent from the germline (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. Inheritance of the somatic genome via a transient RNA genome separate to the nuclear germline DNA genome (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).
Maternal RNA templates	Oxytricha trifallax genome unscrambling guide RNAs	Biological background	Ciliated protozoa contain two nuclei, a germline nucleus and a somatic nucleus.. - The somatic nucleus is transcriptionally active but not passed on after fertilization.. - The germline nucleus is transcriptionally inert in the mother cell but is transmitted to        progeny. The new somatic nucleus is created from this germline nucleus (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. In Oxytricha trifallax creating the new somatic nucleus involves chromosomal fragmentation and deletion to remove ~95% of the genome (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. Hundreds of thousands of short sequences must then be "unscrambled" by reordering or inversion to create a compact somatic genome of nanochromosomes  (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. This extremely specific and reproducible  rearrangement has now been found to guided by maternal RNAs (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).
Maternal RNA templates	Oxytricha trifallax genome unscrambling guide RNAs	Misc	See Nowacki and Landweber 2009 reivew: Epigenetic inheritance in ciliates, for a wider overview of the field.
Maternal somatic nucleus RNAs	Paramecium tetraurelia maternal macronucleus noncoding RNAs	Biological background	Ciliated protozoa contain two nuclei, a germline nucleus and a somatic nucleus.. - The somatic nucleus is active but not passed on after fertilization.. - The germline nucleus is transcriptionally inert in the mother cell but is transmitted to progeny. The new somatic nucleus is created from this germline nucleus (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. In Paramecium tetraurelia creating the new somatic nucleus requires widespread deletion of repetitive sequences and tens of thousands of internal eliminated sequences (IES) to create the compact somatic nucleus in the progeny (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).. Elimination of DNA appears to depend on whether it was present in the maternal somatic nucleus, with DNA present in the maternal somatic nucleus being retained in the progeny somatic nucleus. This process appears to be controlled by interactions between homologous short and long noncoding RNAs (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).
Maternal somatic nucleus RNAs	Paramecium tetraurelia maternal macronucleus noncoding RNAs	Characteristics & Expression	DNA in the somatic nucleus is transcribed into sense and antisense noncoding RNAs during both vegetative growth and sexual reproduction (LepÃ¨re (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18519642).
Maternal somatic nucleus RNAs	Paramecium tetraurelia maternal macronucleus noncoding RNAs	Function	RNA transcripts derived from DNA sequences in the maternal somatic nucleus are necessary but not necessarily sufficient to cause retention of this sequence in the progeny somatic nucleus (LepÃ¨re (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18519642).. For example: introduction of an IE sequence into the maternal somatic nucleus is able to maintain the presence of that IES in the somatic nucleus of the progeny in some cases (Duharcourt (1995) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/7649484, Duharcourt (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9819394).. However degradation of IES RNA transcripts during the vegetal growth stage prevented maintenance of that IES in progeny somatic nuclei, showing long noncoding transcripts from the maternal somatic nuclei were necessary for maintenance of the DNA in progeny (LepÃ¨re (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18519642).. Paramecium expresses a complex population of ~25 nuc germline Scan RNAs (scnRNAs) during early meiosis which have homology to all types of germline sequences. Knockdown of scnRNAs allows retention of sequences normally deleted from the progeny somatic nucleus (LepÃ¨re (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19103667).. ScnRNA : Maternal ncRNA model . ScnRNAs signal sequences to be deleted while maternal RNAs signal sequences to be maintained. Hypothesised that maternal somatic RNAs deplete homologous germline scnRNAs, preventing excision of these sequences in progeny somatic nuclei. Whereas undepleted scnRNAs do cause excision of target DNA sequences (LepÃ¨re (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18519642, LepÃ¨re (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19103667, Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).
Maternal somatic nucleus RNAs	Paramecium tetraurelia maternal macronucleus noncoding RNAs	Inheritance	Non-mendelian epigenetic inheritance, independent from the germline (Nowacki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19879799).
Maternal somatic nucleus RNAs	Paramecium tetraurelia maternal macronucleus noncoding RNAs	Misc	See Nowacki and Landweber 2009 reivew: Epigenetic inheritance in ciliates, for a wider overview of the field.
MEG3	Gtl2	Characteristics	~1.6 kb in humans with a number of splice isoforms and evidence of retained introns creating longer transcripts (Miyoshi (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10759892, Zhang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20032057). . Similar situation in mouse and sheep with ~2kb - ~10kb transcripts due to alternative splicing, alternative 5' and 3' ends and retained introns.  (Schuster-Gossler (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9626496, Bidwell (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11683710, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500)..  . Imprinted: Maternally expressed from the Dlk1-Gtl2 imprinted locus (Schuster-Gossler (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9626496, Miyoshi (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10759892). 
MEG3	Gtl2	Expression	Expressed in a temporal and spatially regulated manner: expressed early in mouse embryos in visceral yolk sac and embryonic ectoderm. Later in paraxial mesoderm, epithelial ducts, and also in skeletal muscle, cochlea, brain and eye (Schuster-Gossler (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9626496, Manji (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16342203). . Dynamically expressed during mouse CNS development. This includes expression during retinal development (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823) and in many developing forebrain areas including the "diencephalon, ventral telencephalon, post mitotic cell layers of the neocortex and pyramidal cell layer of the hippocampus" (McLaughlin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16356785). Also found to be up-regulated during differentiation of neuronal progenitors to GABAergic neurons in vitro (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).. Expressed in adult brain (Miyoshi (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10759892) but in a more restricted manner (McLaughlin (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16356785).  . Isoform Meg3a is detected in human normal pituitary gland, but is absent in nonfunctioning pituitary adenomas (Zhang (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14602737).. Expressed in the nucleus accumbens of normal human brains and upregulated in this brain region in heroin abusers (Michelhaugh (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21128942). Conversely, levels are decreased in the caudate nucleus of patients suffering from the neurodegenerative condition, Huntington's disease (Johnson (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22202438). . See cited papers for a more detailed analysis of developmental and tissue specific expression.
MEG3	Gtl2	Function	<b>Summary:</b> Meg3 is important for proper growth and development and is a putative tumour suppressor which functions to activate p53 and inhibit cell proliferation. Meg3 can also control gene expression at imprinted loci through recruitment of the PRC2 complex. . <b>Function in Cancer:</b>. Expression of the Meg3a splicing isoform was silenced in pituitary tumours and ectopic expression was found to inhibit growth in human cancer cells, leading to the proposition that Meg3 RNA acts as a growth suppressor (Zhang (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14602737).. Silencing of Meg3 is associated with meningioma pathogenesis and progression while ectopic expression inhibited growth and stimulated p53 (Zhang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20179190).. Meg3 knock-out increased expression of VEGF (Vascular Endothelial Growth Factor) signaling pathway genes in the brain, suggesting the RNA has a role in the control of vascularization, and therefore may function as a tumor suppressor in part by inhibiting angiogenesis (Gordon (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20392836).. <b>Mechanism of action:</b>. Meg3 stimulates p53 expression and can also inhibit cell proliferation/ DNA synthesis in the absence of p53 suggesting these functions are independent of each other (Zhou (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17569660), Zhang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20032057. Meg3 contains several predicted secondary structural elements common to all isoforms. Replacement of the motif most important in p53 activation with a different sequence that formed the same structure maintained Meg3 function showing the RNA structural motifs are critical to Meg3 function (Zhang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20032057). . Meg3 binds the PRC2 chromatin modification complex in mouse embryonic stem cells.  Binding appears to be mediated by the 5â 1kb of the RNA (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. Controls expression of Dlk1 at the Dlk1-Meg3 imprinted locus, likely by recruiting PRC2 to the Dlk1 locus in cis. Knockdown lead to increased expression of Dlk1 and Gtl2-as along with a decrease in Ezh2/PRC2 recruitment to and H3K27me3 marks at the Dlk1 promoter (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. <b>Developmental phenotypes:</b>. Knockout of Meg3 and the Meg3 differentially methylated region (DMR) on the maternal allele lead to post-birth lethality, while paternal knockout lead to increased pre and post-birth lethality and growth retardation. However other lncRNAs (Rian, Meg9) were also down-regulated, perhaps due to the loss of the DMR, making attribution of the phenotype to specific lncRNAs difficult (Takahashi (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19264764). A potentially more specific lacZ gene trap insertion gave a parent of origin dwarfism phenotype (Schuster-Gossler (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9626496).. Aberrant repression of Meg3 and other maternally expressed lncRNAs from the DLK1-Dio3 imprinting cluster is present in most induced pluripotent stem cell (iPSC) lines and is responsible for the failure of iPSCs to form viable mice (Stadtfeld (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20418860). . NB: iPSC embryos died mid-gestation, which was more severe than a maternal Meg3 KO (Takahashi (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19264764) indicating the phenotypic impact of other lncRNAs from this locus (Stadtfeld (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20418860).
MEG3	Gtl2	Conservation	Mammals.. Both the human and mouse gene have ten exons with the middle exons being those which are alternatively spliced in both species (Zhang (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20032057).
MEG3	Gtl2	Misc	Contains a microRNA: miRNA 770 in the last intron, (although it appears that this intron is sometimes retained) (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. A number of probes for Meg3 exist in NRED due to the large number of isoforms, accession IDs given are for probes that are common to most isoforms.
MEG3	Gtl2	Localisation	Localisation was generally nuclear, but some cells showed localisation to the cytoplasm or to both compartments (Schuster-Gossler (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9626496). In the nucleus Meg3 has been found associated with chromatin (Mondal (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20404130).
MEG3	Gtl2	Regulation	Expression of Meg3 is stimulated by cyclic-AMP (cAMP). cAMP stimulates CREB transcription factor(s) to bind a cyclic-AMP-response element (CRE) in the proximal promoter which is important for Meg3 expression. Methylation of this promoter region blocks cAMP action (Zhao (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16793321).
MEG9	Mirg	Characteristics	Imprinted: Maternally expressed lncRNA from the Dlk1-Dio3 locus, downstream from Rian (Seitz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12796779, Tierling (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16309881, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500). Contains intronic miRNAs which are also maternally expressed (Seitz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12796779, Seitz (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15310658).. Mirg suggested to be a processed form of Meg9. Northern blot analysis identified a number of transcripts from this locus from ~1kb (putative Mirg transcript) to ~5.5kb (longer than cloned Meg9 transcript) (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).
MEG9	Mirg	Expression	Meg9/ Mirg show similar expression to other lncRNA from locus. Expressed in embryonic and extraembronic tissue but also found in adult skin and testis (Tierling (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16309881, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500)..  . The large cluster of intronic miRNAs show a similar pattern of expression inlcuding in embryos and adult brain (Seitz (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15310658).  
MEG9	Mirg	Function	Transcript(s) from the Meg9 locus bind to the PRC2 chromatin modification complex in mouse embryonic stem cells (mESCs) (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. Aberrant repression of Meg9 and other maternally expressed lncRNAs from the DLK1-Dio3 imprinting cluster is present in most induced pluripotent stem cell (iPSC) lines and is responsible for the failure of iPSCs to form viable mice, with embryos dying mid-gestation (Stadtfeld (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20418860).. Some Meg9 miRNAs have a known function, including one known to be important in brain development (Schratt (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16421561). Others are predicted to target Dlk1, a paternally expressed gene from the same imprinted locus (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).
MEG9	Mirg	Conservation	Meg 9 is present in mammals. However the Meg9 host mRNA for the miRNAs has not been identified in each species.. Meg9 microRNAs are mammalian specific (Seitz (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15310658).
MEG9	Mirg	Misc	Currently unclear if there is any overlap of transcripts from Rian/MEG8 and MEG9/Mirg loci. RNA sequencing by Guttman (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20436462 found no evidence for overlap in mESCs, but there is imprinted transcription in the region between them with the same expression patterns (Tierling (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16309881, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. Sequence given is EU616813.1 from mouse. Note that northern blotting has suggested longer (characterised) transcripts also exist.

meiRNA	sme2	Characteristics	~0.5kb. Unspliced, polyadenylated. Alternative polyadenylation may give rise to different isoforms of ~510 and ~440 nt (excluding polyA tail).
meiRNA	sme2	Expression	Mainly cytoplasmic but when bound to Mei2p becomes mainly nuclear localised in the Mei2p nuclear granule/ dot structure.. Expression of meiRNA is induced by nitrogen starvation in Schizosaccharomyces pombe, which causes a switch from the mitotic cell cycle to meiosis that is dependent on mei2.
meiRNA	sme2	Function	meiRNA specifically binds (both in-vivo and in-vitro) and is required for nuclear localisation of Mei2, which is an RNA-binding protein essential for premeiotic RNA synthesis and meiosis. Mei2p relocalises to nuclear granules/dot structures after binding to meiRNA, resulting in a cell switch from mitosis to meiosis.. Overexpression of meiRNA suppresses a temperature-sensitive defect of mei2+.. Mei2-meiRNA complex functions specifically at Meiosis I, and loss of function of meiRNA blocks meiosis, but not premeiotic DNA synthesis. 
meiRNA	sme2	Misc	Mei2 may interact with other regulatory RNAs. A Mei2 defective in RNA binding cannot promote meiosis, and causes premeiotic DNA synthesis inhibition. In addition, the cytoplasmic function of Mei2, which is independent of meiRNA, is also abrogated in the RNA-binding mutant.

MER11C	HERVK11	Expression	Expressed in tumour cell lines but little expression in fibroblasts (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).

Expression caused increased colony formation in culture and a small increase in tumour formation in mice (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).. Suggests Mer11C has oncogenic activity by repressing hPSF tumour suppressor activity  (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).

Mistral	Mira	Characteristics	Transcribed from region between Hoxa6 and Hoxa7.. 798 nt, single exon, polyA+.
Mistral	Mira	Expression	Expression in mouse embryonic stem cell (mESC) induced by retinoic acid treatment.. Activation of Mira expression occurs before expression of Hoxa6 and Hoxa7.
Mistral	Mira	Function	Role in activation of gene expression and cell differentiation. Required for the epigenetic activation of Hoxa6 and Hoxa7 and hence their target genes during mESC differentiation.. Mira was required for the recruitment of MLL1 to the Mira gene locus and the activation of Hoxa6 and Hoxa7. Mira mediated a local rearrangement in chromatin structure to bring the Mira, Hox66 and Hoxa7 loci into a complex providing a mechanism for MLL1 to act on HoxA6/A7 after recruitment to the Mira locus.. Mira bound to the SET domain of MLL1 through a short hairpin (activator binding motif, ABM) near the 3â end of the RNA. In vitro binding studies suggested MLL1 recruitment was mediated by Mira forming a RNA/DNA hybrid with a protruding ssRNA 3â end containing the ABM.

Mrhl	Meiotic recombination hotspot locus non-coding RNA	Expression	Expressed in mouse testis, liver, kidney and spleen (by northern).
