MSUR1	None known	Characteristics	~1.7kb transcript consisting of the first 1700nuc of 18s rRNA followed by 31bp of non rRNA sequence. 3' sequence contains a polyA signal and the transcript is polyadenylated.. Length and identity of transcript was confirmed by RT-PCR and northern blotting with a 3' probe.
MSUR1	None known	Expression	Expressed in a broad range of tissues.. Up-regulated in the spinal cord of SOD1 mutant mice prior to onset of amyotrophic lateral sclerosis (ALS) type symptoms.
MSUR1	None known	Function	In cell culture, mutations in SOD1 cause cell death, MSUR1 protect cells in a dose dependent manner and acts to decrease levels of hydroxl radicals and the oxidation of cellular proteins.. MSUR1 didn't affect the level of SOD1 protein, instead acting to reduce cellular oxidative stress. The mechanism of MSUR1 action is unknown.
MSUR1	None known	Misc	Mutations in superoxide dismutase (SOD1) are linked to amyotrophic lateral sclerosis (ALS) a fatal neurodegenerative condition. A mouse SOD1 mutant replicates this condition.. Genomic position of MSUR1 transcript not known.
MSUR1	None known	Name	MSUR1: mutant SOD1(G93A)-up-regulated RNA 1
Msx1as	None known	Characteristics	>2 kb, spliced, complementary (antisense) to the region extending from of the 3' end of exon 2 to the middle of intron 1 of the Msx1 gene (Berdal (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12489151, Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985).
Msx1as	None known	Expression	Msx1as transcript is expressed in mouse embryos at E9.5 before the initial steps of skeleton morphogenesis and cell differentiation, and continuously up to birth (Coudert (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16157866). Expressed in differentiated dental and bone cells, being up-regulated during osteoblast differentiation and in developing tooth, bone and limb bud  (Coudert (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16157866, Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985, ID=	12489151). Also detected in hair follicles and neural tube, tissues where Msx1 are expressed (Coudert (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16157866).. Inversely correlated with Msx1 during mouse dental and bone differentiation with the two genes also showing a complementary spatial expression pattern (Coudert (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16157866, Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985, Berdal (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12489151).. Msx1as transcript has also also detected by Northern blot analysis in dental epithelium and mesenchyme from a rat incisor (Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985).
Msx1as	None known	Function	Over-expression of Msx1as in-vitro results in the reduction of Msx1 protein in a dose-dependent manner (Berdal (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12489151). Msx1as is proposed to negatively regulate Msx1 during craniofacial and skeleton development. (Coudert (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16157866, Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985, Berdal (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12489151)
Msx1as	None known	Conservation	Msx1as RNA has been detected in mice, rats, and humans. The transcription initiation site for Msx1as RNA was located by primer extension in both mouse and human in an identical region, including a consensus TATA box present in a highly conserved 66-bp region at the 3' UTR of Msx1 (Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985).
Msx1as	None known	Misc	The Msx1as putative TATA box is conserved in Msx2 cDNA sequences, suggesting a more general regulation pathway of the Msx gene family (Blin-Wakkach (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11390985).
ncR-uPAR	NCRUPAR	Characteristics	~400 bp. RNA polymerase II transcript. Found several kb upstream of the human protease-activated receptor-1 (PAR-1) gene.. Mostly made up of repeat sequences including an Alu element.
ncR-uPAR	NCRUPAR	Expression	Expressed during embryonic development.. Presence of the ncR-uPAR promoter sequence drives expression of a transgene during embryonic vascular development at E9, which recapitulates PAR-1 expression at E9 quite well. At E16 expression was seen in brain and in arteries but not veins.
ncR-uPAR	NCRUPAR	Function	ncR-uPAR can act in-trans to stimulate PAR-1 expression.. ncR-uPAR binds nuclear proteins in-vivo, which could provide a mechanism for it to positively regulate the PAR-1 promoter during embryogenesis.
ncR-uPAR	NCRUPAR	Misc	Refseq ncR-uPAR appears to be the ncR-uPAR promoter and the lncRNA sequence. UCSC genomic co-ordinates are to this Refseq annotation, while the sequence provided is from the identified transcriptional start site to the end of the polyadenylation sites (exact 3' terminus is unknown).
ncR-uPAR	NCRUPAR	Name	ncR-uPAR: non-protein coding RNA, upstream of F2R/PAR1
NDM29	29A	Characteristics	~130 nt. 'Alu-like RNA', it has a canonical Alu/7SL-derived sequence structure. Transcribed by RNA Polymerase III from the first intron of the ASCL3 (Achaete Scute-Like homologue 3) gene (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).
NDM29	29A	Expression	NDM29 expression was analyzed in 6 different cell types and found in abundant levels in neural cells (neuroblastoma cell lines SHSY5Y and SKNBE2, and primary culture of human glioma cells), but  at a very low levels in epithelial-derived cells (HeLa, HEK293, and primary cultures of skin fibrobroblast). NDM29 expression was increased in differentiating cells (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).. NDM29 RNA was detected in both the nucleus and cytoplasm of SKNBE2 and HeLa cells, but enriched (~70%) in the latter (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).
NDM29	29A	Function	In humans, NDM29 maps in a genomic region whose deletion has been shown to be involved in neuroblastoma development (De Preter (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16000168).. In-vitro over-expression of NDM29 promoted differentiation of neuroblastoma (NB) cells into cells with neuron-like features (including marker expression, morphology,  anchorage-dependent growth and excitatory properties), and a reduction in the tumor initiating ('stem-like') cell fraction in the NB cell population. In-vitro and in-vivo experiments indicated that increased expression of NDM29 restricts NB development and malignancy. It also lead to reduced expression of multidrug resistance 1 (MDR1) mRNA in malignant NB cells, and so increased their susceptibility to doxorubicin and cis-platinum antiblastic drugs used in NB therapy (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).
NDM29	29A	Conservation	RNA was detected in humans - Alu-derived elements are restricted to primate lineage  (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).
NDM29	29A	Misc	NDM29 transcript comprises Alu sequences and unique sequences and might have been inserted into the genomic locus by retrotransposition (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224).. Similar to 21A RNA, it is also a short interspersed nucleotide element, marked as AluJb elements. (Pagano (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17274687)
NDM29	29A	Name	NDM29: neuroblastoma differentiation marker 29 (Castelnuovo (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20581224, Pagano (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17274687).
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Characteristics	Two isoforms: ~3.7 (NEAT1 v1/ MEN epsilon) and ~23 kb (NEAT1 v2/ MEN beta) transcribed from the MEN1 locus (Guru (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9253601, Saha (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16760401, Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332).. Intergenic, single exon transcript. One transcriptional start site, long isoform is a continuation of the short isoform (Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048).
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Expression	Expressed in a wide range of human and mouse tissues (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482, Saha (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16760401, Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332). Although expression of the long isoform (Neat1 v2/ Men beta) is much lower than Neat1 v1/ Men epsilon in many tissues (Nakagawa (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21444682).. Up-regulation of Neat1 (and subsequent formation of/increase in paraspeckles) may be a general feature of differentiation. Neat1 is up-regulated upon human ESC differentiation (Chen (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19716791), muscle differentiation (Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332) and in-vitro neuronal differentiation (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).. Up-regulated upon infection of mice with Japanese encephalitis virus or Rabies virus (Saha (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16760401).. Expressed in the nucleus accumbens of normal human brains and upregulated in this brain region in heroin abusers (Michelhaugh (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21128942). In addition, expression levels are elevated in the caudate nucleus of patients suffering from the neurodegenerative condition, Huntington's disease (Johnson (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22202438).. Localised to paraspeckles within the nucleus (Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332).. Mouse Neat1 found to be highly unstable (half-life <2 hr) in N2A (neuroblastoma) and 3T3 cells, although low stability did not prevent paraspeckle formation (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755), while human NEAT1 appears to be more stable (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Sasaki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19188602, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332). The two Neat1 isoforms also have differing stability, with the long (v2/Men beta) isoform more stable than than the shorter (v1/Men epsilon) isoform in N2A and 3T3 cells (Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Function	Transcription of Neat1 is essential for the assembly, maintenance and structural integrity of paraspeckles (Clemson (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19217333, Sasaki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19188602, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332, Mao (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21170033).. Newly transcribed Neat1 RNA nucleates the formation of paraspeckles at its transcription site, recruiting paraspeckle proteins. Continued expression is required to maintain paraspeckles, identifying the dynamic nature of this nuclear body (Mao (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21170033).. Literature currently provides conflicting evidence about whether Neat1 v1 is sufficient for the formation of paraspeckles, or if this requires full length Neat1 v2 (Sasaki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19188602, (Shevtsov (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21240286). In vivo however, significant expression of Neat1 v2 appears to be required for cells to form more than 1 or 2 paraspeckles (Nakagawa (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21444682).. Neat1 appears to constrain the size and mediate the cylindrical geometry of paraspeckles. Neat1 short and the identical 5' end of Neat1 long plus the 3' of Neat1 long all localise to the periphery of paraspeckles, while the central region of Neat1 long is found in the interior of the nuclear body (Souquere (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20881053).. Interacts with paraspeckles proteins PSPC1, PSF/SFPQ and NONO/P54NRB either directly or in a complex (Clemson (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19217333, Sasaki (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19188602, Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332).. Interaction of short isoform with p54 requires protein interaction regions near the 5' and 3' of the transcript (Murthy (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20211624).. Neat1 knockout lead to loss of paraspeckles, however mice were viable and fertile with normal morphology and populations of differentiated cells in one Neat1 v1 and v2 expressing tissue tested (Nakagawa (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21444682).. Neat1 has also been reported to interact with a number of chromatin binding protein/complexes in mouse embryonic stem cells including PRC1, PRC2,	JARID1B, ESET	and SUV39H1, with the general pattern being interaction with repressors of gene expression (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018)
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Conservation	Placental mammals. Dog Neat1 is found in several genomic locations, version that is found near single dog Malat1 gene is given below (Hutchinson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17270048). 
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Misc	A conserved tRNA like sequence at the 3' end is cleaved off and processed to generate a short tRNA-like ncRNA from the long (Men beta) transcript, similar to Malat1 (Sunwoo (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19106332).. The last ~500bp of the short (Men epsilon) isoform has been shown to be expressed in trophoblast cells with a function potentially independent from the Neat1 transcript. This transcript, TncRNA has its own entry.
NEAT1	MEN epsilon/beta, VINC, TncRNA, linc1317	Name	Neat1: Nuclear enriched abundant transcript 1. Short isoform - Neat1 v1. Long isoform - Neat1 v2. Multiple endocrine neoplasia 1 (MEN1). Short isoform - MEN epsilon. Long isoform - MEN beta. . VINC:  Virus-inducible ncRNA
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Characteristics	Northern blot with a probe for Nespas detects a smear and discrete band of 4.4kb and larger (Wroe (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10716699). In addition to an unspliced form, five alternatively spliced forms of up to 1.4 kb in length have also been detected (Williamson (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11889554).. Imprinted (transcribed from the paternal allele). Transcribed from intron 2 of Nesp (Gnas), encompassing exons 2 through 1. The imprinted GNAS locus encodes the alpha-subunit of the stimulatory G protein as well as additional imprinted transcripts including the maternally expressed NESP55 and other paternally expressed transcripts (XLalphas and A/B transcripts).
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Expression	Tissue-specific expression with signal in heart, in cerebral cortex, adrenal, and spleen, where Nesp is also expressed. Nesp and Nespas transcripts show expression from opposite parental alleles in most (but not all) tissues (Li (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11056047), and Nespas may be abundant in some tissues where Nesp is not detected (Williamson (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11889554). Furthermore, the Nesp transcripts can also remain imprinted in tissues that lack Nespas.
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Function	A 4.2 kb microdeletion in humans that ablates two GNAS antisense exons is associated with pseudohypoparathyroidism type Ib.  When maternally transmitted, this mutation causes loss of maternal GNAS imprints, partial gain of NESP55 methylation, and resistance to parathyroid hormone (PTH) in affected and obligate carrier individuals. Paternal transmission leads to epigenetic alterations in cis, including a partial loss of NESP55 methylation and a partial gain of A/B methylation. (Chillambhi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20444925). Nespas RNA was identified as binding to the repressive PRC2 chromatin modification complex in mouse embryonic stem cells, suggesting that like noncoding RNAs from other imprinted region, nespas could act to regulate the imprinting cluster it is transcribed from (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).  
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Conservation	N/A
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Misc	**Annotation in progress**
Nespas	Gnas-as, GNAS antisense transcript, GNAS1as, SANG	Names	Nespas: neuroendocrine secretory protein (Nesp) antisense.
Nkx2.2AS	None known	Characteristics	4.3 kb. Spliced, antisense to Nkx2.2 (upstream sense of Pax1).
Nkx2.2AS	None known	Expression	Preferentially expressed in the nervous system.
Nkx2.2AS	None known	Function	Over-expression of the ncRNA enhances oligodendrocytic differentiation.

npc48	npcRNA 48	Characteristics	983 nucleotides, unspliced. Contain regions that display significant Z-score values for potential secondary structures, which span > 8% of its total length (Hirsch (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16500993).
npc48	npcRNA 48	Expression	Broadly expressed in all tissues analyzed (roots, rosettes, stems, inflorescences, etc) (Hirsch (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16500993).
npc48	npcRNA 48	Function	Overexpression of npc48 in Arabidopsis thaliana led to strong leaf serration (a symptom of defects in cell proliferation along the margins of leaf primordia). Plants overexpressing npc48 showed other drastic developmental anomalies, including an increase in the rosette diameter and a delay in flowering time compared with wild-type plants.. The phenotype of npc48-over-expressing plants resembles that of plants over-expressing MIR168, which have reduced levels of the miR168 AGO1 target, and of AGO1-sensitive miRNAs such as miR166. They also show decreased miR166 accumulation, but presence of AGO1 mRNA and miR168 at wild-type levels.. In addition, npc48 plants exhibited reduced accumulation of miR164, suggesting that npc48 could regulate a subset of miRNAs. Interestingly, mir164a mutants also display abnormal serrations of the leaf margins, which are milder than the serrations induced by overexpression of npc48, suggesting that the reduction in miR164 alone cannot account for the phenotype.. Over-expression of npc48 did not have a general effect on miRNAs or AGO1 accumulation (Ben Amor (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18997003).
npc536	npcRNA 536	Characteristics	597 nucleotides, unspliced. Sequence from full-length cDNA clone GSLTSIL78ZH02 is 645 bp-long.. Npc536 transcript is antisense to the AT1G67930 mRNA (encoding a Golgi-transport complex related protein) (Ben Amor (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18997003).
npc536	npcRNA 536	Expression	npc536 has a large dynamic range of expression across a wide range of tissues and hormonal, biotic, or abiotic treatments.. Up-regulated in roots and leaves of Arabidopsis thaliana plants submitted to stress by phosphate starvation and salt (NaCl) stress (Ben Amor (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18997003).
npc536	npcRNA 536	Function	Transformed plants over-expressing npc536 showed heightened root growth under salt stress conditions, with increased primary root growth and secondary root length.. No phenotype could be observed in mutants that carry T-DNA insertions within npc536.. In response to certain abiotic stresses such as drought or cold treatment, the root expression of these two genes (AT1G67930 and npc536) tends to be anti-correlated (Pearson correlation coefficient of -0.636 and -0.983, respectively). However, accumulation of the AT1G67930 transcript was not significantly modified in plants over-expressing npc536 or in npc536 mutants (Ben Amor (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18997003).
npc536	npcRNA 536	Misc	Annotated as AT1G67920 hypothetical protein, Gene ID: 843120, in Genbank, and contains a small ORF conserved in rice (Ben Amor (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18997003). The 'hypothetical protein' is 67 aa.
NRON	None known	Characteristics	noncoding repressor of NFAT (NRON). ~2.7 kb. Composed of three exons, which can be alternatively spliced to yield transcripts ranging in size from 0.8 to 3.7 kb.
NRON	None known	Expression	Expressed in relatively low levels. Present in mouse embryos and enriched in cells derived from human and mouse placenta, muscle, and lymphoid tissues such as the spleen, thymus and lymph nodes, with differential expression of isoforms.
NRON	None known	Function	Identified in a shRNA knock down screening for conserved long noncoding RNAs that modulate the activity of nuclear factor of activated T cells (NFAT).. Knockdown of human or mouse NRON sequences in human embryonic kidney (HEK) 293 cells or mouse 3T3 and Jurkat cell lines resulted in significantly increased NFAT activity.. Knockdown of NRON increases NFAT transcription factor activity by specifically affecting NFAT nuclear trafficking. This effect is observed on the activity of multiple NFAT family members (NFATc1, NFATc2, NFATc3, and NFATc4).. Using an RNA-protein affinity purification strategy with part of NRON sequence, 11 proteins were reported to putatively bind NRON. These included: calmodulin-binding protein (IQGAP1), a nuclear transport factor (KPNB1), the structural subunit of a phosphatase (PPP2R1A), a component of the proteasome (PSMD11) and an RNA helicase (DDX3X); as well as three members of the importin-beta superfamily, factors which mediate the nucleocytoplasmic transport of cargoes such as NFAT. Direct interaction was demonstrated with importin-beta 1 (KPNB1).. In summary, having a repressive effect on NFAT signaling, NRON is proposed to regulate NFAT's subcellular localization as an RNA component of a protein complex that acts to represses NFAT activity.. It has presumed implications in immune response and developmental processes regulated by NFAT.
NRON	None known	Conservation	NRON contains blocks of sequence which are highly conserved back to chicken. In particular, it contains two large regions of 300 to 400 bases regions of near-perfect sequence conservation between rodents and primates.
NTT	None known	Characteristics	17kb, polyadenylated, but not spliced. . Sense intronic to Phosphodiesterase 7B, also covers one exon.. Contains a number of repeats, mostly near the 3 end.
NTT	None known	Expression	Expressed in activated, but not resting, CD4+ T cells. Also found in stimulated peripheral blood mononuclear cells (PBMC) and CD8+ T cells.. Localisation is predominately nuclear.. Shows a similar expression pattern to the interferon-gamma receptor gene, found ~1Mb away, which may suggest a co-regulation of the two transcripts in immune cell activation/development.
NTT	None known	Conservation	Has short regions of conserved sequence.
NTT	None known	Misc	Phosphodiesterase 7B is a cAMP-specific phosphodiesterase, a member of the cyclic nucleotide phosphodiesterase family. Involved in cAMP and cGMP signaling.. Sequence given is from genomic DNA, which corresponded to results from RT-PCR and RACE.
NTT	None known	Name	NTT: noncoding transcript in T cells.
Otx2os1	OTX2-AS1	Characteristics	Alternatively spliced transcripts found in a head to head arrangement with Otx2.. Mouse ~750nuc.  Humans ~2.4kb.. Contains a number of repeat sequences (human). Mostly free of repeats (mouse).
Otx2os1	OTX2-AS1	Expression	Expression restricted to retina in panel of adult tissues (retina also shows the highest expression of Otx2).. Otx2 and Otx2os1 had a partially complementary expression pattern in adult retinal layers. Otx2 was predominately expressed in the outer nuclear layer (ONL) and into the inner nuclear layer (INL), while Otx2os was predominately expressed in the ganglion cell layer (GCL) and into the INL.
Otx2os1	OTX2-AS1	Conservation	Low conservation between mouse and human transcripts.
Otx2os1	OTX2-AS1	Misc	Otx2 is a transcription factor involved in brain and eye development.. Otx2os1 Mouse: GeneID: 606497.  Human GeneID: 100309464
Otx2os1	OTX2-AS1	Name	Otx2os1: OTX2 opposite strand transcript 1
p53 mRNA	None known	Characteristics	Messenger RNA that encodes the p53 protein, but also has a role as regulatory RNA that interacts with Mdm2 protein, controlling its function and p53 gene expression.
p53 mRNA	None known	Expression	N/A
p53 mRNA	None known	Function	"p53 mRNA region that interacts with the Mdm2 RING domain also encodes the amino acids which bind the N-terminus of Mdm2 protein"
p53 mRNA	None known	Conservation	N/A
p53 mRNA	None known	Misc	p53 is a key tumour suppressor gene which "responds to diverse cellular stresses to regulate target genes that induce cell cycle arrest, apoptosis, senescence, DNA repair, or changes in metabolism - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/gene/7157". MDM2 is an important regulator of p53, with binding of MDM2 protein to p53 protein promoting p53 degradation.
PANDA	P21 associated ncRNA DNA damage activated
PANDA antisense RNA	Characteristics	Bidirectional transcript from the CDKN1A promoter.. 1.5kb single exon.. Sequence runs antisense through a processed LAP3 pseudogene and contains a SINE.
PANDA	P21 associated ncRNA DNA damage activated
PANDA antisense RNA	Expression	One of five lncRNAs surrounding the transcription start site of the cell cycle gene CDKN1A that, along with the CDKN1A protein coding gene, were induced in human fetal lung fibroblasts upon DNA damage by doxorubicin.. Induced up to 40 fold upon DNA damage peaking 16 h after doxorubicin treatment, a much greater response than shown by CDKN1A.. Expression of PANDA and CDKN1A were positively regulated by p53. CDKN1A did not induce PANDA.
PANDA	P21 associated ncRNA DNA damage activated
PANDA antisense RNA	Function	P53 effector gene, acts in response to DNA damage to limit apoptosis while CDKN1A induces cell cycle arrest.. Loss of PANDA leads to the apoptosis of doxorubicin treated cells.. Loss of PANDA affected the expression of many genes during the DNA damage response.  Upregulated genes were enriched for those involved in apoptosis, including the apoptotic activators APAF1, BIK, FAS and LRDD. Leading to apoptosis of doxorubicin treated cells.. Cell death genes downstream of p53 are known to have NF-YA binding sites. PANDA RNA interacts with the transcription factor NF-YA and attenuates its occupany of target gene promoters.
PANDA	P21 associated ncRNA DNA damage activated
PANDA antisense RNA	Conservation	Syntenic sequence appear to be present in apes and old world monkeys (the Catarrhini).

	Expression	Expressed in Jurkat cells, but not in MCF7 cells (unlike CYP4A22-AS1).
PDZK1IP1-AS1	Noncoding RNA activating4: ncRNA-a4, PDZK1IP1 antisense RNA 1
	Function	PDZK1IP1-AS1 expression appears to stimulate CMPK1 gene expression (in Jurkat cells). A gene located over 150 kb 3â of PDZK1IP1-AS1 on the same strand. 
PHO5 lncRNA	PHO5as	Characteristics	~2.4kb. Appears to be antisense. Covers PHO5 gene region and promoter.
PHO5 lncRNA	PHO5as	Expression	Expressed during high phosphate conditions when PHO5 is repressed.. Transcript degraded by the exosome and accumulates in exosome mutants.
PHO5 lncRNA	PHO5as	Function	LncRNA transcription involved in remodeling the PHO5 promoter and activation of the gene.. Loss of ncRNA transcription delayed nucleosome eviction and RNA polymerase II recruitment to the PHO5 promoter, showing it was necessary for proper activation.. Note: shows that transcription which generates short lived/ exosome degraded transcripts can be functionally relevant. Although it not known if the transcript itself is functional.
PHO5 lncRNA	PHO5as	Misc	The PHO5 gene encodes a protein involved in phosphate metabolism that is repressed under high phosphate conditions and activated under phosphate starvation.
PHO84 antisense	None known	Characteristics	Antisense to PHO84.. 2 transcripts, one covers the entire PHO84 gene, the other is longer and extends into the YML122C (a short hypothetical ORF) locus. Both initiate transcription near the 3' of PHO84. 
PHO84 antisense	None known	Expression	There was low expression of antisense transcripts constitutively but abundance increased in aged cells as PHO84 was silenced.. PHO84 antisense transcripts are degraded by the exosome, but increased in abundance in aged cells due to transcript stabilisation. 
PHO84 antisense	None known	Function	Summary: Silences PHO84 in aged cells. In aged cells exosome dissociates from PHO84 locus allowing the stabilisation and accumulation of PHO84 antisense transcripts.. Antisense RNAs recruit the histone deacetylase complex (Hda1, Hda2, Hda3) to the PHO84 locus, causing deacetylation and PHO84 silencing.. Blocking expression of full length PHO84 antisense transcripts prevented PHO84 silencing, demonstrating the antisense transcripts (not just transcription) was necessary for silencing. . Nb: not clear if PHO84 antisense binds HDAC complex directly.
PHO84 antisense	None known	Misc	PHO84 is an inorganic phosphate transporter
PINC	None known	Characteristics	~1 and 1.6 kb isoforms identified.
PINC	None known	Expression	Developmentally regulated (Ginger (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16574773). Expressed in alveolar structures of the mammary gland and induced by pregnancy and hormonal stimulation (Ginger (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11682629). Also present in testis, liver and heart. Different isoforms show a tissue-specific distribution.. Isoforms localise in distinct foci predominantly in the cytoplasm or nucleus depending on stage of cell cycle (Ginger (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16574773).
PINC	None known	Function	siRNA knock-down experiments indicate that PINC RNA performs dual roles in cell survival and regulation of cell-cycle progression (Ginger (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16574773).
PINC	None known	Conservation	PINC identified in rodents. Other mammals contains several conserved sequence blocks (Ginger (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16574773). However, it is unclear if a PINC homologue exists in these species, for example the syntenic human locus is antisense to the 3' of DIRC3 and no sense RNAs have been identified which contain the conserved sequence blocks.
Pinci1 family RNAs	None known	Name	Pinci1: P. infestans non-coding infection-specific family
Pinci1 family RNAs	None known	Characteristics	Analysis of a member (Pinci1-1) indicates a minimum size of 850 bases. Polyadenylated.. The described Pinci1 RNA family comprises more than 400 members with sequence homolgy (110 full-length and 297 single-domain homology), which are arranged in clusters of up to nine copies throughout the P. infestans genome.
Pinci1 family RNAs	None known	Expression	Identified in a suppression subtractive hybridization (SSH) screen for exprressed sequences upregulated during Phytophthora infestans of potato.. Expression of members of five classes of Pinci1 transcripts was found markedly upregulated from 12 to 33h post-inoculation of potato with P. infestans, a period defining the biotrophic phase of the infection.
Pldi	None known	Characteristics	~850nuc, alternatively spliced 2 or 3 exon transcript.. Evolution of a lncRNA gene from an intergenic region.. Has an overlapping antisense transcript.
Pldi	None known	Expression	Expressed in postmeiotic cells in the testis.. May regulate the expression levels of other genes in testis. 
Pldi	None known	Function	Knockout showed reduced sperm motility and reduced testis weight.
Pldi	None known	Conservation	Gene is specific to certain Mus species. Intergenic region is present in other mammals (rat, human) and other more basal Mus species but no transcripts are expressed showing evolution of this gene in the past 2.5-3.5 million years.. Splice and polyA sites utilised by Pldi were present as crytpic sites in other mouse species, mutations in the 5' regulatory region of Pldi appear to have allowed its expression, which has subsequently been selected for. 
Pldi	None known	Name	Pldi: Polymorphic derived intron containing ncRNA
PR antisense transcripts	AT1, AT2, AT3	Characteristics	Found several antisense transcripts which initiate in the progesterone receptor (PR) promoter region. . AT1 and AT3 were unspliced.. AT2-T47D and AT2-MCF7 were spliced with seven exons and transcribed over a 70kb region. AT2 isoforms initiated between the PR A and B start sites, had different (cell line specific) start sites but were otherwise identical. . AT2-T47D ~1.35kb. AT2-MCF7 ~1.5kb.
PR antisense transcripts	AT1, AT2, AT3	Expression	Expression identified in human breast cancer cell lines (MCF7 and T47D).. AT2 isoforms were the most highly expressed antisense transcripts.. AT2 isoforms could be detected in the nucleus.
PR antisense transcripts	AT1, AT2, AT3	Function	All function characterisation was on the AT2 isoforms.. PR antisense transcripts act as a scaffold for other RNAs and proteins to bind, allowing them to regulate transcription of the progesterone receptor.. Different small RNAs targeted at PR antisense transcripts can activate or repress PR transcription. A PR antisense transcript was necessary for activating PR transcription via a small RNA.. PR antisense transcripts could associate with small RNAs, Argonaute proteins and hnRNP-k to bring about regulation of the PR protein coding gene. 
PR antisense transcripts	AT1, AT2, AT3	Name	Progesterone receptor promoter antisense transcripts
PR antisense transcripts	AT1, AT2, AT3	Misc	Accessions:. AT-1: FJ515871. AT-2-MCF7: FJ515872. AT-2-T47D: FJ515873.  
PRINS	None known	Characteristics	~3.6 kb, transcribed by RNA Polymerase II; spliced (2 exons) and polyadenylated (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153).
PRINS	None known	Expression	Elevated expression in psoriatic epidermis. Regulated by the proliferation and differentiation state of keratinocytes (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153).. Expressed at different levels in various human tissues, with highest levels detected in veins (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153).. Several stress signals such as ultraviolet-B (UV-B) irradiation, viral infection (herpes simplex virus), and translational inhibition increased the RNA level of PRINS (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153), as well as HaCaT keratinocyte cell treatment with microbial agents such as bacteria peptidoglycan, lipopolysaccharide (LPS) and wall extract (Bari (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21750967). 
PRINS	None known	Function	siRNA knock-down shows that PRINS is required for cell viability after serum starvation (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153), and also alters cell morphology and gene expression (Szegedi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20377629).. Elevated PRINS expression in the epidermis is suggested to contribute to psoriasis susceptibility (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153).. In keratinocytes PRINS regulates the expression of the G1P3 gene, an anti-apoptotic protein that is overexpressed in psoriasis (Szegedi (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20377629), although the mechanism is unknown. 
PRINS	None known	Name	Psoriasis susceptibility-related RNA Gene Induced by Stress (PRINS)
PRINS	None known	Misc	PRINS RNA contains contains two Alu elements, as well as a short sequence stretch with ~70% similarity to an element in a small cytoplasmic noncoding RNA, named G8, from Tetrahymena thermophila, whose expression responds to heat shock and is involved in thermotolerance (Sonkoly (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15855153).
Prion-associated RNAs	None known		Annotation in Progress. [[. RNAs of unknown identity associate with prion protein PrP, and participate in the conversion of human cellular PrP to its altered infectious conformation.. ]]
pRNA	IGS RNAs, intergenic nc-rRNA	Characteristics	Originate from the intergenic spacers (IGS) that separate rRNA genes (Rungger (1979) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/291055, Morgan (1983) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6579535).. Like rRNA genes, spacers also contain polymerase I promoters and the ~2kb from the spacer promoter to the rRNA gene promoter is transcribed (Kuhn (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3428263). These long lncRNAs must be processed to create the a shorter ~150-300 nt RNA sequence(s), pRNAs, from just upstream of the rRNA promoter that bind TIP5 (the large subunit of the chromatin remodeling complex NoRC) (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107).. In human cells transcription runs from ~1kb upstream of the rRNA transcriptional start site to over 200bp into the gene (Shiao (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19838300). 
pRNA	IGS RNAs, intergenic nc-rRNA	Expression	Nuclear localised (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107).. Expression of IGS sequences is regulated by the cell cycle with expression up-regulated in mid-S phase. There are many rRNA repeats and only a subset these express IGS sequences (Santoro (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010804).. Expression in human lung cancer cell lines was generally higher than in a non-transformed lung cell line, with a negative correlation between the intergenic nc-rRNA and the 45s rRNA precursor transcript (Shiao (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19838300). Investigation of intergenic nc-rRNA SNPs also identified one that correlated with lower expression of the intergenic nc-rRNA (Shiao (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19838300).
pRNA	IGS RNAs, intergenic nc-rRNA	Function	Required for the nucleolar localization of NoRC and epigenetic control of the rDNA locus (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107).. Details:. Conserved stem-loop structure binds to the TIP5 protein in the chromatin remodeling complex NoRC (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107, Mayer (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18600236). This binding is controlled by the acetylation state of TIP5, with IGS RNA binding the de-acetylated version TIP5 (Zhou (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19578370).. Required for nucleolar localization of NoRC, recruitment of NoRC to chromatin, and subsequent addition of repressive histone modifications and DNA methylation at the rRNA gene promoter (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107). . Without IGS RNA, NoRC regulation is lost and rRNA expression is increased (Mayer (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16678107). . pRNAs processed by IGS sequences can function in-trans, suggesting they could silence the rRNA genes they originate from or other rRNA gene clusters (Santoro (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20010804).
pRNA	IGS RNAs, intergenic nc-rRNA	Conservation	Expressed IGS sequences are found in widely diverged species ie: Xenopus, Drosophila and mouse (Rungger (1979) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/291055, Miller (1983) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/6306560, Kuhn (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3428263), but may not carry out the same function.. In mammals the functional IGS sequences are poorly conserved at the nucleotide level but fold into similar stem-loop secondary structures (Mayer (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18600236). 
pRNA	IGS RNAs, intergenic nc-rRNA	Misc	The actual rRNA gene loci that express IGS and pRNAs have not been catalogued.
PSF inhibiting RNA	None known	Characteristics	Transcript not characterised, RNA fragment maps to repeat rich intergenic region.
PSF inhibiting RNA	None known	Expression	Specifically expressed in melanoma cell lines (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).
PSF inhibiting RNA	None known	Function	Fragment from PSF inhibiting RNA was found to bind hPSF, could release it from GAGE6 proto-oncogene regulatory DNA in-vitro and in-vivo (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).. Expression caused increased colony formation in culture and a modest increase in tumour formation in mice (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).. Suggests PSF inhibiting RNA has oncogenic activity by repressing the hPSF tumour suppressor (Li (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19625619).
PSF inhibiting RNA	None known	Conservation	Only studied in human cells.
PSF inhibiting RNA	None known	Misc	Referred to as "unidentified RNA fragment/gene" in Li et al paper.
psvA antisense RNA	None known	Characteristics	1.8 kb, cis-antisense to the pre-spore gene psvA, initiated from a promoter located within the translated region of the psvA gene.
psvA antisense RNA	None known	Expression	Exhibits a temporal expression inverse to psvA during development.
psvA antisense RNA	None known	Function	Excess transcription of antisense RNA in vegetative cells and after disaggregation suggests its involvement in the control of psvA RNA levels. This has been suggested to operate at the control of mRNA stability, given that inhibition of RNA synthesis during disaggregation prevented destabilization of the psvA mRNA.
PTENP1	None known	Name	PTENP1: PTEN Pseudogene 1
PTENP1	None known	Characteristics	Processed pseudogene of PTEN tumour suppressor gene at 9p13.3.. ~3.9kb.. PTENP1 "coding sequence" quite similar to PTEN but has lost start codon, while 3'UTR is ~1kb shorter than PTEN. Part of the PTENP1 3'UTR sequence is highly conserved compared to PTEN (~95%) with seed matches to the same miRNAs.
PTENP1	None known	Expression	Expressed in a very wide variety of human tissues and in prostate cancer. Good correlation between PTENP1 and PTEN levels.. Inhibition of endogenous miRNAs with seed matches to PTEN and PTENP1 leads to an increase in PTENP1 expression, validating it is targeted by miRNAs known to repress PTEN. 
PTENP1	None known	Function	Competing endogenous RNA (ceRNA). PTENP1, through its 3'UTR, acts as a decoy for miRNAs that target PTEN.. PTNEP1 functions as a tumour suppressor gene.. Overexpression of the PTENP1 3'UTR lead to an increased level of PTEN and cellular growth inhibition, an effect dependent on the presence of mature miRNAs, supporting PTENP1's role as a miRNA decoy. While knockdown of PTENP1 lead to a decrease in PTEN levels and faster cell growth.. The PTENP1 locus was lost in a subset of colon cancers and a relationship was reported between PTENP1 copy number and PTEN expression level.
PTENP1	None known	Misc	Cells are very sensitive to levels of PTEN, with even subtle changes influencing cancer susceptibility (Alimonti (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20400965).. A wider role for pseudogenes as miRNA decoys has been proposed.
PWR1	None known	Characteristics	~1.2kb capped, polyadenylated, single exon transcript.. PWR1 expressed in FLO11 regulatory region.. Expressed on opposite strand to FLO11. Starts within a region covered by a second lncRNA ICR1 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=235, transcribed in antisense direction to ICR1 and terminates around the area of ICR1 initiation.
PWR1	None known	Expression	Expression of ICR1 and PWR1 is inversely correlated. . ICR1 expression requires the Sfl1 transcription factor known to repress FLO11 and is repressed by the Flo8 transcription factor and the Rpd3L histone deacetylase (HDAC).. PWR1 expression requires Rpd3L HDAC and Flo8 and is repressed by Sfl1.
PWR1	None known	Function	PWR1 regulates expression of the FLO11/MUC1 gene in cis, in conjunction with a second lncRNA ICR1 - http://www.lncrnadb.com/Default.aspx?TKeyid=235.. Expression of ICR1 represses expression of FLO11, probably by promoter occlusion. . Expression of ICR1 is repressed by PWR1 (again probably by promoter occlusion in cis), allowing expression of FLO11, so the regulatory circuit depends on whether PWR1 is expressed or repressed.. ICR1 is lowly expressed constitutively and competition between Flo8 and Sfl1 transcription factors determines which ncRNA is expressed and therefore if FLO11 is on or off.
PWR1	None known	Misc	FLO11/ MUC1 - cell surface glycoprotein that controls cell-cell adhesion and shows variegated expression in a clonal population of yeast cells (ie: expressed at high levels in some cells, silenced in others).. Sequence of PWR1 is found on chromosome IX from coordinates 395996 to 396936. See. http://www.yeastgenome.org/cgi-bin/locus.fpl?sgdid=S000132614
PWR1	None known	Name	PWR1: promoting Watson RNA1 
RepA transcript	None known	Characteristics	~1.6 kb transcript containing the RepA repeats (Zhao (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18974356). Repeats are internal to Xist, near the 5' end (Wutz (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11780141). . The RepA repeat sequence is expressed as part of full length Xist and as part of the shorter RepA transcript.. RepA repeats: 7.5 repeat units separated by spacers. Each repeat forms 2 stem loops (Wutz (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11780141).
RepA transcript	None known	Expression	RepA transcript is expressed prior to the onset of X-inactivation (Zhao (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18974356).
RepA transcript	None known	Function	RepA repeats are required for X-chromosome silencing but not for localisation of Xist to the X-chromosome (Wutz (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11780141).  . The repA transcript recruits polycomb repressor complex 2 (PRC2) to the inactive X chromosome, with Ezh2 serving as the RNA binding subunit (Zhao (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18974356, Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659).. Recruitment of PRC2 by the RepA transcript allows deposition of HE-K27me3 marks at the Xist locus which is needed for up-regulation of full length Xist. Suggests the RepA transcript is necessary for the initiation of X-chromosome inactivation (Zhao (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18974356).
RepA transcript	None known	Conservation	Sequence at 5' of Xist containing the A repeats and from where the separate RepA transcript is expressed show conservation throughout placental mammals.
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Characteristics	These overlapping but non-identical transcripts are found in the Dlk1-Dio3 imprinted region (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034, Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500) and should probably be viewed as different isoforms of the Rian gene. The human and mouse loci are quite similar, whereas the rat loci (Bsr gene) has undergone significant divergence and so has its own entry in the database.. Spliced lncRNAs that contain a number of intronic snoRNAs and sometimes miRNAs (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206, Royo (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17507654, Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500). . In human and mouse, transcription of the Meg8 isoform can extend through the snoRNA clusters. Mouse Meg8 is ~4.4kb with over 20 exons. In mouse the ~2.5 kb Irm transcript contains the last 10 exons of Meg8 but has its own transcriptional start site. Mouse Meg8 contains intronic miRNAs not found in Irm (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. RNA sequencing confirms a large number of isoforms with alternative splicing and also retained introns exist at this locus though no evidence was found for Rian overlapping the Meg9/Mirg transcript (Guttman (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20436462). It is unclear if the Irm isoform exists in humans.
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Expression	Imprinted: Maternally expressed (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034, Charlier (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11337479, CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).. Expressed predominately in brain (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034), embryo and muscle (Charlier (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11337479) with generally weak expression in other tissues (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500). Expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018). In mouse the longer 'Meg8' transcript is also expressed in skin whereas the shorter 3' 'Irm' is not (Hagan (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19194500).. Up-regulated during differentiation of neuronal progenitors to GABAergic neurons in vitro (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).. Localised to the nucleus (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034).. Intronic snoRNAs also show brain and embryo imprinted expression (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Function	LncRNAs contain a number of miRNAs and snoRNAs, little is known about the molecular function of the lncRNAs.. Rian transcript(s) bind to the PRC2 chromatin modifying complex in mouse embryonic stem cells (Zhao (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21172659, Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018). Rian was also found to interact with a number of other chromatin binding protein(s)/complexes in mouse embryonic stem cells including PRC1, JARID1B, JARID1C and CBX3, with the general pattern being interaction with repressors of gene expression (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).. Aberrant repression of Rian and other maternally expressed lncRNAs from the DLK1-Dio3 imprinting cluster is present in most induced pluripotent stem cell (iPSC) lines and is responsible for the failure of iPSCs to form viable mice, with embryos dying mid-gestation (Stadtfeld (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20418860).
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Conservation	Bsr and Rian/MEG8/Irm are not highly conserved between species (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206). However, some Rian exons show good homology to Bsr and while many snoRNAs are specific to one species others are homologous (Hatada (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11481034, CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).. Rian gene is present in mammals.
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Name	Rian: RNA Imprinted and Accumulated in Nucleus . Irm: Imprinted RNA near Meg3/Gtl2. MEG8: Maternally expressed gene 8
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Summary	Comparing human, mouse and rat: All contain ncRNA gene(s) with intronic snoRNAs at this locus. The snoRNAs vary between species, but there are some homologous snoRNAs between each suggesting an evolutionary history with species specific snoRNA addition and duplication (CavaillÃ© (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12045206).. The expression profiles of Bsr, Rian/Irm/MEG8 and the snoRNAs they contain are similar between rat, human and mouse.
Rian	Irm, MEG8 and Bsr, linc1458	Misc	Human UCSC browser link below is for Refseq Meg8, however it is clear from known human mRNAs that transcripts from the Meg8 locus can extend much further than the current Refseq annotation.
Rmst	Dmt2 (Dorso-medial telencephalon gene 2)	Characteristics	Several isoforms of ~1.4, ~2 and ~3kb identified (Uhde (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20062813). Has splice variants, multiple alternative promoters (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).. Intergenic, transcription start site contains a HeK4me3 locus (Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288).
Rmst	Dmt2 (Dorso-medial telencephalon gene 2)	Expression	Expressed in specific regions of embryonic and post-natal mouse brain (see Chodroff (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20624288 and Uhde (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20062813 for details).  . Expression in embryonic brain includes in â ventral midbrain where dopaminergic neurons are formedâ (Uhde (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20062813). So Rmst may be a marker for developing dopaminergic neurons (Uhde (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20062813).. 2kb transcript also expressed in adult brain, eye and lowly expressed in muscle and ovary (Uhde (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20062813).. Transcript found to be highly unstable with a half-life <2 hr in N2A (neuroblastoma) cells (Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
RNCR3	A930011O12Rik, LOC157627	Characteristics	Intergenic, four exon transcript in mouse.. Gene contains a highly expressed, brain specific microRNA (mir124a-1) in an exon (Lagos-Quintana (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12007417).
RNCR3	A930011O12Rik, LOC157627	Expression	Dynamic expression in mouse retinal development (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823).. RNCR3	A930011O12Rik, LOC157627	Conservation	LncRNA is conserved in mammals and overlaps the LOC157627 noncoding Refseq gene in humans (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).
