rncs-1	None known	Characteristics	847 bases. Spliced and polyadenylated. Highly structured, with an almost perfectly double-stranded helix of ~300 nuc.. Expressed from F55A4.9 noncoding RNA gene.
rncs-1	None known	Expression	Transcript is enriched in males. Detected in all developmental stages tested (embryos, larval stages (L1-L4), and young adults). Spacial expression localized to intestine (robustly detected in E cell lineage of midgut from 28-cell stage to adulthood), as well as to hypodermis (starting by the comma stage, including Hyp7 syncytium and head and tail hypodermis).. RNA has higher expression in arrested L1s, and dauer larvae purified from exhausted liquid culture, by transcriptional modulation in response to food supply (induced by starvation).
rncs-1	None known	Function	Forms extensive double-stranded RNA structures and inhibits Dicer cleavage of other dsRNA in-vitro, although rncs-1 itself is not a substrate for Dicer (because of branched structures at its termini). Expression of rncs-1 reduces Dicer-generated siRNA, and affects levels of Dicer-regulated genes (5 identified genes).. Lines overexpressing rncs-1 may result in increased frequency of males among hermaphrodite self-progeny.
rncs-1	None known	Conservation	Absence of an identifiable rncs-1 homolog in closely related Caenorhabditis briggsae and Caenorhabditis remanei species.
rncs-1	None known	Misc	Functional analogy is drawn with certain viruses dsRNA expressed to compete with cellular dsRNA-mediated pathways, such as VAI adenovirus RNA (McKenna (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16580685).. It is a substrate of ADAR deamination.
rncs-1	None known	Name	rncs-1: RNA noncoding, starvation up-regulated 1
roX1 and roX2	None known	Characteristics	rox1 and 2 are two X-linked genes. The primary and secondary structures of roX RNAs, including splice variants, are important for their function.
roX1 and roX2	None known	Expression	RNAs are male-specific.. RNAs are retained in the nucleus.. Expression is developmentally regulated in Drosophila male embryos. roX1 is specifically expressed in males from mid-embryogenesis onward and roX2 from 6h of embryo development onward.
roX1 and roX2	None known	Function	RNAs are responsible for dosage compensation (DC) in Drosophila melanogaster males, directing global (but gene specific) up-regulation of transcription from the single male X-chromosome. roX1 and roX2 are essential for DC, but are functionally redundant.. The precise mechanisms by which roX RNAs direct the Dosage Compensation Complex (DCC) to specific sites in the X-chromosome are still unknown. RNAs associate with Male-specific lethal (MSL) proteins (components of the multi-protein complex DCC), directing the DCC to hundreds of sites along the X chromosome to promote histone acetylation and gene-specific activation.. Mapping of roX2 binding sites along the X-chromosome showed they were coincident with the binding sites of MSL proteins, supporting the view roX2 is part of the chromatin bound complex of MSL proteins (Simon (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22143764).
roX1 and roX2	None known	Conservation	N/A
roX1 and roX2	None known	Misc	UCSC coordinates given below are to roX1 and roX2 which are found in separate locations.
roX1 and roX2	None known	Names	roX1: RNA on the X 1. roX2: RNA on the X 2
RPS6KA2 antisense transcript	RPS6KA2AS	Features	Present in chr6q27 region, which is frequently involved in chromosomal rearrangements and associated with a wide range of human cancers and, thus, postulated to harbor tumor-suppressor genes.. Antisense RNA overlaps the 1st, 6th and 7th intron of the candidate tumor suppressor gene RPS6KA2 (so far reported as a tumor suppressor gene for sporadic epithelial ovarian carcinoma). Sense and antisense RNAs are detected in fetal brain RNA, but they show inverse expression in several breast cancer cell lines compared to normal breast tissue, with RPS6KA2 down-regulated in cancer and the antisense up-regulated.. Microarray data also showed that RPS6KA2 and its antisense RNA have a negative expression correlation (with a high confidence (p=0.0092) in 42 out of 59 patients (71%)).. Pair are proposed to be reciprocally regulated, and antisense RPS6KA2 is hypothesized to regulate RPS6KA2 expression in cancer. Over-expression of the antisense RNA in BT20 cells (a breast cancer cell line model) was associated with a decrease in the intracellular levels of the sense transcript, whereas knock-down of RPS6KA2 sense by RNAi in the BT20 cell line caused an increase in the level of RPS6KA2 antisense.. Antisense RNA is reported to map in two different genomic regions, and also to contain a potential ORF, potentially representing the FAM103A1 pseudogene.
RTL	TY1 CUT	Characteristics	Originally classified as a cryptic unstable transcript (CUT) but now classed as a Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript (XUT) (van Dijk (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21697827). Antisense to a Ty1 retrotransposon. Transcript initiates within Ty1 and is transcribed across the TY1 LTR (long terminal repeat) promoter sequence (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478). . ~400 nuc. Several initiations site, main site begins +661 nuc from the start of the LTR (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478). . Transcribed by RNA polymerase II, polyadenylated (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478). 
RTL	TY1 CUT	Expression	Unstable, degraded by a cytoplasmic 5â to 3â degradation pathway including  Xrn1, Dcp1 and Dcp2 (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478). . Reversibly up-regulated by lithium (van Dijk (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21697827)
RTL	TY1 CUT	Function	Functions in trans to silence Ty1 retrotransposon and prevent its transposition (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478).. Silencing requires histone deaceylation and Set1 histone methylation. Silencing causes a decrease in RNA polymerase II occupancy while TBP (TATA binding protein) is unchanged (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478). While silencing appears to be antagonised by H3K4me3 (van Dijk (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21697827).. Case of a CUT/XUT RNA repressing a mobile element through transcriptional gene silencing (Berretta (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18316478).. Nb: Currently unclear exactly how silencing is mediated by RTL
SAF	FAS-AS (FAS antisense RNA)	Characteristics	1556 bases; transcribed from the opposite strand of intron 1 of the human Fas gene.
SAF	FAS-AS (FAS antisense RNA)	Expression	Detected in several human tissues (such as heart, placenta, liver, muscle and pancreas, as well as kidney in lower levels). It was also detected in different cancer cell lines, including Jurkat (acute T-cell leukemia), MES-SA (uterine carcinoma) and U-937 (Histocytic Lymphoma); moderately expressed in CA46 (Burkittâs lym- phoma), Raji (Burkittâs lymphoma) and only slightly expressed in MG-63 (osteosarcoma).
SAF	FAS-AS (FAS antisense RNA)	Function	In vitro over-expression of Saf protects cells from Fas-mediated apoptosis.. Over-expression of Saf induces alternative splicing of FAS transcripts, wherein an alternative exon overlapped by the antisense RNA is retained and non-adjacent 3' exons are skipped. This results in Fas proteins that are not able to anchor to the cell membrane, therefore regulating Fas-mediated but not TNF-alpha-mediated apoptosis.
SAF	FAS-AS (FAS antisense RNA)	Conservation	Saf gene appears to be conserved among the primates and is absent in the rodents.
SatIII transcripts	None known	Characteristics	Heterogeneous sizes, up to >1.4 kb; transcribed from tandem arrays of repetitive Satellite III (SatIII) DNA in pericentromeric heterochromatin.
SatIII transcripts	None known	Expression	Induced by heat shock and a range of stresses, such as heavy metals treatment, UV-C, oxidative and hyper-osmotic stress.
SatIII transcripts	None known	Function	Can nucleate the formation of nuclear stress bodies, recruiting transcription factors and RNA processing factors (HSF1, SAF-B and SF2/ASF) to these sites (Shevtsov (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21240286).
SatIII transcripts	None known	Conservation	N/A
SatIII transcripts	None known	Misc	Genebank accessions for various RNAs: AY845690 - AY845709 
SCA8	ATXN8OS, KLHL1AS	Characteristics	~1.5kb spliced transcript. Antisense to the KLHL1 gene (homolog of the Drosophila KELCH gene) in a bidirectional transcriptional orientation (overlapping in the first exon).
SCA8	ATXN8OS, KLHL1AS	Expression	N/A
SCA8	ATXN8OS, KLHL1AS	Function	Ectopic expression in Drosophila induces late-onset, progressive neurodegeneration in the retina.. Predicted gene product underpinning the triplet repeat expansion-induced neurodegenerative disease Spinocerebellar Ataxia 8.. Associates with the RNA binding protein staufen.
SCA8	ATXN8OS, KLHL1AS	Conservation	KLHL1AS promoter is conserved between human and mouse. However, the mouse gene is not spliced.
SCA8	ATXN8OS, KLHL1AS	Name	Spinocerebellar ataxia 8 (SCA8) RNA. KLHL1AS: kelch-like 1 (Drosophila) antisense. ATXN8OS: ataxin 8 opposite strand
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Name	sfRNA: subgenomic flavivirus RNA
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Characteristics	0.3-0.6 kb. Derived from the 3' untranslated region of the RNA genome (gRNA) of Flaviviruses (Urosevic (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9010281).. Contains a 5'-proximal stable hairpin (nt 6 to 56), the conserved flavivirus 3'-cyclization motif (nt 413 to 420) and the 3'-terminal long stable hairpin structure (nt 440 to 523) (Lin (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15113895). The stable RNA structures, which include multiple pseudoknots (Olsthoorn (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11680841), located at the beginning of the 3' untranslated region render this RNA resistant to nucleases (Funk (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20719943, Silva (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20739539, Pijlman (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19064258).
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Expression	Present in infected tissues, such as the brain of mice after an intracerebral challenge with Murray Valley encephalitis (MVE) virus (Urosevic (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9010281).. In infected mammalian BHK-21 cells, the viral genome was detected as early as 24 h postinfection, and sfRNA was detected as early as 28 h postinfection, at levels 0.25 to 1.5 times as abundant as the genome RNA on a molar basis between 28 and 48 h postinfection. In mosquito C6/36 cells, the genome RNA and sfRNA were present 5 days postinfection and the small RNA was 1.25 to 5.14 times as abundant as the genome (Lin (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15113895).
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Function	Required for viral cytopathicity and pathogenicity (Pijlman (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19064258).. Transfection of sfRNA and reporter assays indicated that sfRNA modulates viral translation and replication in trans (Fan (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22040380).
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Conservation	Highly conserved among Flaviviruses, with primary sequence conservation concentrated at the loop regions of the secondary structure and at 27 nucleotides immediately adjacent to the 5' side of the structure (Brinton (1986) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3016981)
sfRNA	Flavivirus 3' structured RNA	Misc	sfRNA subgenomic fragments result from incomplete degradation of the viral genome by the host 5'-3' exonuclease XRN1 (Silva (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20739539).
Six3os	RNCR1	Characteristics	Six3os is found head to head with the Six3 gene (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823).. Six3os undergoes extensive alternative splicing, that, combined with alternative 5' start sites, creates 12 known Six3os isoforms (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823, Alfano (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15703187, Geng (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17084678).. Isoforms are up to ~7kb in length (Geng (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17084678).
Six3os	RNCR1	Expression	Human and mouse Six3os transcripts both show expression restricted to retina and brain (Alfano (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15703187).. Shows dynamic expression during mouse retinal development with an expression pattern generally concordant with, by sometimes more restricted than, Six3 (Blackshaw (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15226823, Alfano (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15703187, Geng (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17084678).. Expression was not altered in Six3 null embryos (Geng (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17084678).
Six3os	RNCR1	Conservation	Found in mouse and humans (Alfano (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15703187).
Six3os	RNCR1	Misc	The Six3 protein coding gene is an essential transcription factor involved in the development of the visual system.. One Six3os isoform has a potential ORF, however homology searching does not identify similarity to any other proteins suggesting it may not be a real ORF.
Six3os	RNCR1	Name	RNCR1: Retinal noncoding RNA 1. Six3os: Six3 opposite strand transcript
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Name	snaR: small NF90-associated RNAs
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Characteristics	~117nt. RNA polymerase III transcripts. Highly structured. snaR genes shares sequence identity with Alu RNA and two potential piRNAs. Cloned snaR sequences have a run of adenines in the 3' end followed by a run of thymidines (which presumably constitute the PolIII termination site) (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395).. snaR-A and snaR-B were originally identified associated to the Nuclear factor 90 (NF90) (a double-stranded RNA-binding protein implicated in multiple cellular functions) by in vivo cross-linking followed by immunoprecipitation.RNA species immunoprecipitated with NF90 were ~80â120 nt long (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17913627). Several related RNAs of ~104 nt were originally cloned and identified, with snaR-A being the major component, and snaR-B representing the minor subset.  snaR-A and snaR-B are ~90% identical in sequence. Human genomic sequences corresponding to snaR-A and snaR-B have occasional mismatches (suggested to be possibly due to C-to-U editing of the RNA).. snaR genes occur in multiple copies (accumulated by segmental duplication) arranged in two inverted regions of tandem repeats on human chromosome 19. Additional snaR gene copies are present, with two of them adjacent to genes encoding the beta chain of chorionic gonadotropin:. In total, 28 snaR genes have been identified in the human genome, including 14 genes for snaR-A and 2 genes for snaR-B. snaR genes identified by sequence analysis include 5 snaR-C genes and additional genes (snaR-D, -E, -F, -G1, -G2, -H, -I, -12 and -21) (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395). snaR-D to -G include 5 unique genes on chromosome 19 as well as single copies (snaR-2 and -3) on chromosomes 2 and 3. snaR-G1 and -G2 are located in a gene-rich 2.1 Mb genomic fragment between the two clusters, lying within the promoter region of two genes encoding the beta polypeptide of chorionic gonadotropin (CG-beta) (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395).
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Expression	Predominantly cytoplasmic, unstable (half-life of ~15 min in HeLa cells), expressed in diverse cell lines and human tissues. The different snaR genes have different expression levels and profiles, and, among more than 20 adult human tissues analysed, snaR transcripts are found particularly abundant in testis, with low levels detected in brain, placenta and some other organs. (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395, Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053).. Highly abundant in some cells, with snaR-A estimated in ~70,000 copies in a HEK293T cell (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395).. snaR-A and snaR-G2 are differentially expressed in discrete regions of the human brain and other tissues, such as testis (Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053). snaR-A was expression n testis was ~100-fold higher than in term placenta, lung and adipose tissue, and in brain its levels were ~10% of the testis level in three of four segments of pituitary gland, with substantial expression also observed in other brain regions (such as hypothalamus, globus pallidus and thalamus) (Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053). snaR-G2 levels in adult brain were ~55% of that in testis (highest in caudate/accumbens/putamen and globus pallidus), and several tissues displayed 5â15% of testis levels. Fetal brain contained much less snaR-G2 than adult brain (~3% of testis level), suggestive of developmental regulation. (Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053). snaR-A is up-regulated in transformed and immortalized human cells (Parrott et al. 2010).
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Function	Functions of snaR transcripts have not been identified yet.. snaR transcripts interact with NF90's double-stranded RNA-binding motifs (dsRBMs) (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395), and snaR-A is also found stably bound to ribosomes in HeLa cells (Parrott et al. 2010).. Suggested to be involved in tissue- and species-specific regulation of cell growth and translation (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395, Parrott (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20028844, Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053).
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Conservation	snaR genes are present exclusively in African Great Apes and some are unique to humans. Human snaR-A has orthologs in chimpanzee but not rhesus macaque or mouse. Chimpanzee has fewer snaR genes than humans (10 instead of 28). snaRs appear to have undergone accelerated evolution (snaR genes display a lower degree of homology within the gene than in their flanking sequence) and differential expansion in the great apes.  (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395, Parrott et al. 2010). There are ~17 nt changes between human snaR-A (121nt) and snaR-C  (119nt) species (~14% difference), compared to an average substitution rate of ~3.7?nt per 120nt (~3% difference) outside of the snaR locus (Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053).. The single snaR gene on chimpanzee chromosome 2a is 94% identical with its ortholog on human chromosome 2, and two genes on chimpanzee chromosome 19 are orthologous with snaR-G1 (a unique gene on human chromosome 19). The position of these snaR genes relative to the primate-specific CG-beta genes is conserved. (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395)
snaR	small NF90-associated RNAs	Misc	*Two families of snaR-related genetic elements were identified in primates: CAS (catarrhine ancestor of snaR), limited to Old World Monkeys and apes; and ASR  (Alu/snaR-related), present in all monkeys and apes. These two classes appear to have spread by retrotransposition.. It has been proposed that snaR genes evolved through a series of internal deletions and expansions  from the left monomer of the primate-specific Alu SINE family via ASR and CAS (Parrott (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20935053).. *Short RNAs of ~26â34 nt can be detected after long exposure of Northern blots with snaR probes (Parrott (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17855395).. *Other RNAs are also found associated with NF90, including viral RNAs, such as the VAI and VAII noncoding RNAs from human adenoviruses (Liao (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9671709).
SNHG1	UHG	Characteristics	Spliced transcript with a number of short exons (>40bp) and snoRNA containing introns (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254)..  . Transcriptional start site has characteristics of 5' TOP gene family (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254).. ~1.1kb transcript in human (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254).. Contains 8 (maybe 9) snoRNAs in human, 8 in mouse (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254).
SNHG1	UHG	Expression	Localised to the cytoplasm and associates with ribosomes (Pelczar (1998) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9671460).. RNA unstable in both human and mouse cells (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254, Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755), can be stabilised by inhibition of protein synthesis. This suggests SNHG1 may be sensitive to nonsense mediated decay and could be therefore be "translated" but perhaps only to degrade it (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254).. Up-regulated during lineage restriction of neural stem cells into bipotent neuronal/oligodendrocyte progenitors in vitro (Mercer (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20137068).
SNHG1	UHG	Conservation	Mouse SNHG1 is in a syntenic position with the human host gene. However, there is little conservation of exonic sequence compared to intronic snoRNA sequence (Tycowski (1996) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8559254, Tanaka-Fujita (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17468437).
SNHG1	UHG	Name	SNHG1: Small nucleolar RNA host gene 1. UHG: U22 host gene
SNHG3	U17HG, linc1343	Characteristics	Upstream from the RCC1 protein coding gene. Multiple SNHG3 splice isoforms exist, minority join RCC1, majority do not. Isoforms range from ~0.9kb to ~2.6kb in human.. Contain U17a and U17b snoRNAs in introns. . SNHG3 contains a number of exonic Alu elements. Transcriptional start site has characteristics of 5' TOP gene family.
SNHG3	U17HG, linc1343	Expression	Localised to cytoplasm.. Unlike SNHG1 it was not stabilised by translation inhibitors or associated with translating ribosomes and was unaffected by translation inhibitors.. Identified as expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).. Transcript found to be unstable with a half-life <2 hr in mouse N2A (neuroblastoma) cells and human B cells (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
SNHG3	U17HG, linc1343	Conservation	Not highly conserved, ~40-50% identity between mouse and human exons.
SNHG3	U17HG, linc1343	Name	SNHG3: Small nucleolar RNA host gene 3
SNHG3	U17HG, linc1343	Function	Involved in maintaining pluripotency in ESCs (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).. Knockdown in mECSs lead to down-regulation of Nanog, Sox2, Klf4 and Oct4 expression as well as changes to ESC morphology (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).. Snhg3 was found to interact with a number of chromatin binding proteins/complexes in mESCs including PRC1, PRC2, JARID1B and SUV39H1, with the general pattern being interaction with repressors of gene expression (Guttman (2011) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21874018).
SNHG4	U19H	Characteristics	Upstream from the Matrin 3 protein coding gene. A number of splice isoforms of SNHG4 exist, some of which join Matrin3 and so act as an upstream initiation site for Matrin 3. . SNHG4 specific isoforms appear to contain the first four SNHG4 exons and differ at the 3' end.. Contains U19 snoRNA in intron 3 (annotated as SNORA74A in Refseq).. Transcriptional start site has characteristics of the 5' TOP gene family.
SNHG4	U19H	Expression	Expressed in a number of adult human tissues.. Shows a nucleoplasmic localisation. In constrast to other SNHG RNA (SNHG1, SNHG3)  which are localised in the cytoplasm.. Human SNHG4 isoforms 1&2 were highly stable in B cells (half-life >8 hr), while mouse Snhg4 was highly unstable in mouse 3T3 cells, suggesting differential stability between species (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
SNHG4	U19H	Conservation	Likely present in mouse with same relationship with Matrin 3
SNHG4	U19H	Name	SNHG4: Small nucleolar RNA host gene 4
SNHG5	U50HG	Characteristics	Contains U50 and U50-like snoRNAs in introns (Tanaka (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10792466).. Alternatively spliced transcript (Tanaka (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10792466).. Refseq isoform is ~0.5kb in humans.. Transcriptional start site has characteristics of 5' TOP gene family (Tanaka (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10792466).
SNHG5	U50HG	Expression	Broadly expressed in human adult tissues.. Identified as enriched in the cytoplasm of human GM12878, HepG2, HUVEC and K562 cells bu nuclear enriched in HeLaS3 (Derrien (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22955988).. RNA is unstable with a half-life <2 hr in mouse N2A (neuroblastoma) and 3T3 cells and a half-life ~2 hr in human B cells  (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755).
SNHG5	U50HG	Conservation	Mouse has two transcripts at syntenic loci which are separated by several hundred kb and contain U50. Some sequence similarity is found between then so it is likely they share a common ancestor (Tanaka-Fujita (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17468437).. Comparing mouse and human host transcripts revealed they were "dissimilar". It was hypothesized that the host transcripts share a common ancestor but there has been little selection for maintaining the sequence the host gene exons (Tanaka-Fujita (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17468437). 
SNHG5	U50HG	Misc	SNHG5 forms a novel translocation breakpoint with Bcl6 in a diffuse large B-cell (DLB) lymphoma, although it is unclear if SNHG5 contributed to malignancy (Tanaka (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10792466).
SNHG5	U50HG	Name	SNHG5: Small nucleolar RNA host gene 5
SNHG6	U87HG	Characteristics	Spliced transcript with U87 snoRNA in second intron. . ~0.5kb transcript. Transcriptional start site has characteristics of 5' TOP gene family.
SNHG6	U87HG	Expression	Broad expression in human and mouse tissues.. Localises mostly to the cytoplasm . Human transcript found to show greater stability that SNHG1 in Hela cells (Makarova (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16226852). Also found to be quite stable in human B cells with a half-life of 7 hr, while mouse Snhg6 was significantly less stable (half-life 2.2hrs in 3T3 cells), suggesting the transcripts may have different stabilities between species (Friedel (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19561200, Clark (2012) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22406755). . Minority of SNHG6 associates with monosomes. . Blocking translation led to a very modest increase in SNHG6 levels, in contrast to SNHG1 (which showed a large increase in transcript level) suggesting it is not very sensitive to nonsense mediated decay. This may help explain its increased stability. 
SNHG6	U87HG	Function	Unknown, however the authors point out that 5' TOP family genes are important for translation and that ribosomal associated SNHGs could be involved in this process as well.
SNHG6	U87HG	Conservation	Host gene sequence shows more conservation between species than other SNHG RNAs with conservation similar to levels of mRNA 3'UTRs.. Conserved between human, mouse, rat and dog.
SNHG6	U87HG	Name	SNHG6: Small nucleolar RNA host gene 6
Sox2ot	SOX2OT, Sox2dot	Characteristics	SOX2OT holds within one of its introns the single-exon SOX2 gene, overlapping in the same transcriptional orientation (Fantes (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12612584).. Sox2ot has multiple transcription start sites, and several splicing isoforms and polyadenylation sites (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).. Mouse full-length clones range in size from 638 nt (GenBank accession no. BY721402) to ~3.5 kb (accession no. AK031919), consistent with Northern blot signals in mouse tissues, which show a major band of ~3kb, but also additional discrete bands of ~1, 4, 6, and >10 kb. In zebrafish embryos, Northern blot analysis showed a major band of ~2.5 kb, as well as less intense bands of ~1.5 and ~6 kb (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).. Alternative transcriptional start sites for Sox2ot homologs detected in different vertebrates are associated with highly conserved elements, transposon-free regions and histone modifications typical of promoters. These include a distal promoter that creates a Sox2ot isoform named Sox2dot ("Sox2 distal overlapping transcript"), located more than 0.5Mb upstream of the Sox2 gene in mouse (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420), and which also has demonstrated enhancer activity in mouse developing forebrain.
Sox2ot	SOX2OT, Sox2dot	Expression	Sox2ot is a stable transcript expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells, which, like Sox2, is down-regulated upon induction of embryoid body (EB) differentiation, but, unlike Sox2, is up-regulated during EB late differentiation. Sox2ot absolute levels are higher in cultured neurospheres, and Sox2 and Sox2ot are concordantly up-regulated in differentiated neurospheres. Sox2dot isoform is expressed at very low levels in undifferentiated neurospheres, but with a marked increase in the more differentiated neurospheres.. In situ hybridization analysis of mouse brain sections of Sox2ot and Sox2dot expression detected both transcripts in zones of adult neurogenesis, such as the subventricular zone, rostral migratory stream and olfactory bulb (where Sox2dot is most highly expressed) (Mercer (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18184812, Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).. Many Sox2ot isoforms are present in whole embryo and newborn mouse. In adult mouse, different isoforms are detected primarily in brain, but also at lower levels in tissues where Sox2 is detected, such as lung, or not detected, such as testis. In adult tissues, Sox2dot was only detected in brain.. Highly enriched binding of neuronal transcriptional repressor NRSF/REST has been found in conserved sites upstream of Sox2ot.. Sox2ot is dynamically regulated during chicken and zebrafish embryogenesis, consistently associated with central nervous system structures, including fish embryo eyes, but also mesoderm tissues. During chicken development, increasing levels ofSox2ot were observed after 2days of embryonic development, similar to the pattern observed for Sox2, although with lower absolute expression levels. Expression of both Sox2 and Sox2ot was enriched to the head of 6.5-d chicken embryos, compared to the limbs and whole body. In fish, sox2 and sox2ot presented concordant up-regulation after the sphere stage, suggesting that both are early zygotic genes, but their expression patterns diverged after the tailbud stage when sox2ot total levels decreased. Sox2dot is expressed at very low levels in early embryos, but is dramatically induced at 5 dpf.. In humans, qRT-PCR analysis showed that SOX2OT is highly enriched in the brain, where SOX2 is also predominantly expressed, but also detected in other tissues such as testis. The distribution of SOX2OT ESTs in human tissues also showed a high predominance in CNS libraries, with greatest enrichment in "lens," followed by subthalamic nucleus and Alzheimer cortex, while it is found in lowest relative abundance in cerebellum (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).
Sox2ot	SOX2OT, Sox2dot	Function	Function of Sox2ot is undetermined. SOX2OT is a candidate gene involved in myopia, as upstream or intronic regions of Sox2ot isoforms were identified as a myopia common susceptibility locus by linkage disequilibrium analysis (Andrew (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18846214).
Sox2ot	SOX2OT, Sox2dot	Conservation	Isoforms are positionally conserved in vertebrates. At primary sequence level, although not highly conserved overall, there are regions of high conservation, such as a 384nt-stretch in the exons immediately flanking Sox2 with 91.2% identity between the mouse and human genomes (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).. Some exons of SOX2OT may be species- or clade-specific (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).. Multiple SOX2OT promoters are associated with highly conserved elements in vertebrates and orthologous transcripts are detected with transcription start sites of transcripts detected in fish, amphibians, reptiles and mammals (Amaral (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19767420).
Sox2ot	SOX2OT, Sox2dot	Name	SOX2OT: SOX2 overlapping transcript
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Characteristics	Single exon ~700 nt transcript expressed in sense direction from the 2nd intron in SPRY4.. Contains a SINE at 5' end.. Secondary structure predicted to contain several long hairpins and multiple pseudoknots.  
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Expression	Expression significantly up-regulated in melanoma cell lines and patient tumour samples (both primary and metastatic) compared to melanocytes and keratinocytes. . SPRY4-IT1 showed much greater expression variation across 20 human tissue than SPRY4. Both showed positively correlated expression and depending on the tissue either could be more highly expressed than the other.. Knockdown of SPRY4-IT1 did not affect expression levels of SPRY4, validating that the two transcripts are independent.. Localized predominately in the cytoplasm. Larger punctate nuclear signal could be transcription sites. 
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Function	Knockdown of SPRY4-IT1 in melanoma cells lines decreased cell viability, increased cell apoptosis. SPRY4-IT1 impacts cell invasion and cell mobility with decreased invasion and motility in SPRY4-IT1 knockdown cells and increased mobility (faster speed of migration) in SPRY4-IT1 over-expressing cell lines.   
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Conservation	Not well conserved outside of primate, with 5' SINE element and predicted secondary structural elements only present in primates. 
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Misc	SPRY4 protein coding gene is also more highly expressed in melanoma cells and patient samples compared to melanocytes.. It is unclear if SPRY4-IT1 has a separate promoter or is transcribed as part of the SPRY4 transcript.
SPRY4-IT1	AK024556	Name	SPRY4 intronic transcript 1 (non-protein coding)
SRA	SRA1	Function	Forms ribonucleoprotein complexes with a number of nuclear receptors (including many steroid hormone receptors) generally acting to stimulate transcriptional activation (Lanz (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10199399, Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122).. Interacts either directly or through a complex with a number of other co-activator and repressor proteins, such as SRC-1, Sharp, SLIRP and p68 and p72 RNA helicases. SRA has been suggested to act as a scaffold for these complexes (reviewed in Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122).. Transgenic expression of SRA in vivo caused hyperplasia and morphological abnormalities in steroid hormone responsive tissues. Hyperplasia was accompanied by higher apoptosis however and expression of SRA did not lead to tumourigenesis (Lanz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14517287).. Associated with cardiomyopathy in humans, a role in heart development was validated in zebrafish but it's unclear if SRAP or SRA or both is responsible (Friedrichs (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19064678).. SRA activity is regulated by pseudouridylation (Zhao (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15327771, Zhao (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17170069).
SRA	SRA1	Conservation	SRA ncRNA conserved in mammals (Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122).. SRAP Protein is conserved in chordata (Chooniedass-Kothari (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15147866).
SRA	SRA1	Name	Steroid receptor RNA Activator
SRA	SRA1	Characteristics	Bifunctional gene, active as an RNA and encodes a conserved protein SRAP (reviewed in Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122).. SRA has a large number of isoforms, most of which share a central core region. Only some isoforms are also able to encode the SRAP protein, and differential splicing may be one mechanism of generating coding and noncoding isoforms of SRA (Hube (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16848684) (reviewed in Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122).. A number of functional motifs, with predicted secondary structures, are required for SRA RNA function (Lanz (2002) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12444263). 
SRA	SRA1	Expression	Expressed in a wide range of tissues, some isoforms appear to have tissue specific expression (Lanz (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10199399, Lanz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14517287).. Up-regulated in tumours of steroid hormone responsive tissues ie: breast, uterus and ovary compared to matched normal tissue (Murphy (2000) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11103781, Lanz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14517287).. Found in the nucleus and the cytoplasm (Lanz (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/14517287, Zhao (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17170069).
SRA	SRA1	Misc	Some isoforms of SRA encode a conserved protein product SRAP, which is also expressed in normal tissues and breast cancer (Emberley (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12565891, Chooniedass-Kothari (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15147866, Chooniedass-Kothari (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16152589).. Studies show SRAP can also regulate the activity of nuclear receptors and bind to promoter regions regulated by nuclear receptors, suggesting functional similarities between SRA RNA and SRAP (Chooniedass-Kothari (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20398657, Chooniedass-Kothari (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20153324).. Leygue (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17710122 provides a useful review of the literature.
SRG1	None known	Characteristics	Three transcripts: . ~400 and 500bp transcripts, start upstream of the SER3 protein coding gene and cover SER3 promoter. Differ in 3' end with longer form also covering the beginning of the SER3 coding sequence. Polyadenylated (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754, Thompson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17074811).. ~1.9kb transcript, begins at same position but runs to the end of the SER3 gene (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754, Thompson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17074811).. Could identity TATA-binding protein and RNA polymerase II binding to drive SRG1 expression (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754).
SRG1	None known	Expression	SRG1 is expressed under growth conditions where SER3 is not expressed (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754).. SRG1 expression is regulated by serine levels (Martens (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16291644).. Despite being identified as cryptic unstable transcripts (CUTs) (Davis (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16484372), SRG1 transcripts were predominately degraded in the cytoplasm not the nuclear exosome. (Thompson (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17074811).
SRG1	None known	Function	SRG1 inhibits transcription of SER3 by transcriptional interference, as the process of SRG1 transcription through the SER3 promoter prevents transcription factor binding to this locus (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754). SRG1 transcription does not appear to be sufficient for repression with proper chromatin remodeling also required (Davis (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16484372). . SER3 is an enzyme involved in serine biosynthesis, whose expression is regulated by the level of serine. Serine level controlled the expression of SRG1, with SRG1 transcribed when serine is present and repressed when it is not. This regulation depended on Cha4, a serine dependent regulator, which binds the SRG1 promoter. When serine is high Cha4 appears to recruit the SAGA and Swi/Snf complexes to SRG1 promoter to activate SRG1 expression and repress SER3 (Martens (2005) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16291644).
SRG1	None known	Conservation	SRG1 promoter/  TATA element is conserved in multiple yeast species (Martens (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15175754).
SRG1	None known	Name	SRG1: SER3 regulatory gene 1
ST7OT	ST7OT1, ST7OT2, ST7OT3, ST7OT4
<br></br>
ST7AS1, ST7AS2, ST7AS3, ST7AS4	Characteristics	Four noncoding RNAs from the RAY1/ST7 gene locus. Complex gene locus with a large number of coding and noncoding isoforms. . ST7OT1 & 2 are antisense to ST7. ST7OT3 & 4 are on the sense strand.. ST7OT1 - ~2kb unspliced antisense transcript that initiates in intron 1 of ST7, covers the first exon and terminates in the ST7 promoter region. Polyadenylated. Nb: it also overlaps exon 1 of ST7OT4.. ST7OT2 - Spliced antisense transcripts. Multiple isoforms that share either some 5' or some 3' exons. Isoforms are between 900-1300 bp, with 4-6 exons and polyadenlyated.. ST7OT3 - Spliced ~1kb transcript. Begins in intron 10 of ST7, shares exons 11-13 and sometimes 14 & 15 with ST7 plus has a number of unique exons. Some exons may also act as a alternative 3' end for ST7.. ST7OT4 - Multiple spliced transcripts within the long first intron of ST7. However, Refseq ST7OT4 transcript may be protein coding. Transcription begins just ~200bp downstream from the end of first ST7 exon.
ST7OT	ST7OT1, ST7OT2, ST7OT3, ST7OT4
<br></br>
ST7AS1, ST7AS2, ST7AS3, ST7AS4	Expression	ST7OT1 - abundantly expressed in testis, also expressed in cerebellum, skeletal muscle, uterus, cerebellum, spinal cord, fetal brain, and prostate.. ST7OT2 - testis, fetal brain, cerebellum, mammary gland, fibroblasts.. ST7OT3 - expression only detected in cerebellum.. ST7OT4 - no expression detected.
ST7OT	ST7OT1, ST7OT2, ST7OT3, ST7OT4
<br></br>
ST7AS1, ST7AS2, ST7AS3, ST7AS4	Conservation	ST7OT1 - some conserved sequence with mouse, most of this is where ST7OT1 overlaps the first exon of ST7 however.. ST7OT2 - 3' end of some isoforms shows some conservation with mouse.. ST7OT3 - some conserved sequence, most of this is shared exons with ST7 though.. ST7OT4 - sequence not conserved with mouse.
ST7OT	ST7OT1, ST7OT2, ST7OT3, ST7OT4

ST7AS1, ST7AS2, ST7AS3, ST7AS4	Misc	ST7OT1 - NCBI Gene ID: 93653. ST7OT2 - NCBI Gene ID: 93654. ST7OT3 - NCBI Gene ID: 93655. ST7OT4 - NCBI Gene ID: 338069
SUC2uxut1-3	SUC2uxut1
SUC2uxut2
SUC2uxut3	Characteristics	Three Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript (XUTs) upstream from SUC2 gene.. SUC2uxut1 (~2.3kb) in sense direction  . SUC2uxut2 (~1.2kb) and SUC2uxut3 (~1kb) in antisense direction overlapping SUC2uxut1.
SUC2uxut1-3	SUC2uxut1
SUC2uxut2
SUC2uxut3	Expression	Up-regulated in Xrn1 (5'-3' cytoplasmic exonuclease) knockout but unchanged in TRAMP nuclear degradation pathway knockout. Hence degraded by Xrn1 cytoplasmic pathway.. SUC2uxut1 reversibly upregulated by lithium. 
SUT719		Characteristics	Antisense to SUR7 coding gene. SUT719 comes from a bidirectional promoter with GAL80 where they share regulatory signals. The 3' end of SUT719 extends through and beyond the SUR7 transcription start site.  
SUT719		Expression	SUT719 and SUR7 are both expressed in standard galactose media. Upon stimulation with alpha-factor pheromone SUR7 is switched off while SUT719 continues to be expressed.. SUT719 expression is regulated by Gal4 (as is the expression of GAL80, which shares a bidirectional promoter with SUT719).
SUT719		Function	SUT719 is required for complete switching off of SUR7 expression (disruption of SUT719 expression allows SUR7 expression after stimulation with alpha-factor pheromone when it would normally not be expressed).. SUT719 acts to fine tune gene expression by impacting the on/off threshold of SUR7. When SUR7 is expressed at low levels it is inhibited by SUT719, but high level SUR7 gene expression is not affected by SUT719.
SUT719		Misc	Regulation of GAL80 gene expression also affects SUT719, as they both come from a bidirectional promoter. In turn, SUT719 can regulate the expression of SUR7. This demonstrates a model whereby neighbouring coding genes regulate each other via ncRNA expression/ regulation and also a mechanism for spreading a regulatory signal (ie: that imposed on GAL80) along a chromosome.
SUT719		Name	SUT719: Stable Uncharacterized Transcript 719
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Characteristics	TEA transcripts originate from the TEA promoter at the 5' of the array of joining (J) gene segments of the T-cell receptor alpha chain (TCRA) (de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476). Another noncoding transcript has been identified coming from a promoter within the J array (J-alpha 49).. TEA transcription extends up to ~71kb, covering the length of the J array and terminating in the C alpha region (de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476). . Full length of actual spliced TEA transcript reported as ~2kb (de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476, Shimizu (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8383995). ~4.5 and 8kb transcripts have also been reported. Transcripts generally include TEA sequence spliced to C alpha and sometimes include J segments (Villey (1997) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9247569). 
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Expression	Expressed during thymocyte development at a time recombination is occurring (Abarrategui (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16936730, Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258). Expression is highest in fetal thymocytes and is absent in mature adult T cells (de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476, Shimizu (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8383995).. TEA transcripts have been identified in the nucleus (Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258).
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Function	TEA transcription regulates V alpha-to-J alpha recombination and is necessary to generate the full complement of recombined segments (Abarrategui (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16936730, Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258).. Transcription has both activating and repressive effects on the promoters of different J segments. Segments only a small distance downstream from the TEA promoter are activated while segments more distal are repressed, with alterations in histone modifications and chromatin accessibility (Abarrategui (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16936730, Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258).. These effects target initial recombination events to the active proximal J segments. In the absence of TEA ncRNA transcription recombination occurs in more distal J segments which are normally repressed (Abarrategui (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16936730, Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258).. Repressive effects of the TEA ncRNA suggested to be due to transcriptional interference. Unknown if TEA ncRNA also has a function itself, ie: recruitment of chromatin modification complexes (Abarrategui (2006) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16936730, Abarrategui (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17882258).
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Conservation	Humans and mouse (de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476, Shimizu (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8383995).
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Misc	V(D)J recombination acts to assemble the variable regions of T cell receptors from germline variable (V), diversity (D) and joining (J) gene segments.. RNA accessions from de Villartay (1987) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/3500476 and Shimizu (1993) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/8383995 some are spliced some are not.. Human 147: GenBank: M18204.1. Human 147A1: GenBank: M18206.1. Human 147A19: GenBank: M18205.1. Mouse T early alpha (TEA) region: GenBank: D13547.1
TEA ncRNAs	None known	Name	TEA: T early alpha
TERRA	TelRNAs	Characteristics	Heterogeneous sizes (between 100 nt and 9 kb); transcribed from telomeric C-rich strand (RNAs contain UUAGGG repeats) from telomeres, initiating in subtelomeric regions.. Transcribed by RNA polymerase II. Polyadenylated. (Azzalin (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17916692, Schoeftner (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18157120)
TERRA	TelRNAs	Expression	TERRA expression is regulated by several mechanisms, especially telomere length. Measured RNA stability indicates a half-life of approximately 2.2 h (Schoeftner (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18157120).. Nuclear-restricted. Detected in different human and rodent cell lines. Levels vary according to developmental stage, cellular stress, tumour differentiation and chromatin structure: very low levels in mouse embryos between days 11.5 and 15.5 of embryonic gestation; higher levels in all adult tissues tested, with highest levels in thymus, kidney and spleen and other tissues with low or no telomerase activity; low levels in cancer cells. (Azzalin (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17916692, Schoeftner (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18157120)
TERRA	TelRNAs	Function	TERRA RNAs remain associated to telomeric chromatin, making them potential components of mammalian telomeres, and proposed involvement in shortening of telomeres.. Telomere length correlates with TERRA levels in immortal cell lines.. TERRA siRNA knock-down caused an increase in telomere dysfunction-induced foci, aberrations in metaphase telomeres, and a loss of histone H3 trimethyl K9 and origin recognition complex (ORC) binding at telomere repeat DNA.. SMG proteins (effectors of nonsense-mediated decay) are enriched at telomeres in vivo and negatively regulate TERRA association with chromatin, protecting chromosome ends from telomere loss (Azzalin (2007) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17916692).. TERRA transcripts inhibit telomerase activity in vitro, therefore suggested to negatively regulate telomere length. Consistent with this hypothesis, TERRA knock-down causes a loss of telomeric DNA repeats.. TERRA transcripts have recently been detected associated with heterochromatin marks typical of telemores (histone H3 trimethyl K9) as well as with different telomere proteins, including telomere repeat factors 1 and 2 (TRF1 and TRF2), subunits of the ORC, heterochromatin protein 1 (HP1), and members of the DNA-damage-sensing pathway. In particular, TERRA can interact directly with the TRF2 amino-terminal GAR domain and ORC1 to form a stable ternary complex, and ORC1 binding to TRF2 is RNase A sensitive (Deng (2009) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19716786).. Different lines of evidence indicate that TERRA transcripts form a parallel G-quadruplex structure localized to telomere DNA at cell nuclei, and may form an intermolecular G-quadruplex with DNA (Xu (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18776307, Xu (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20679250).
TERRA	TelRNAs	Conservation	TERRA RNAs have been described in different vertebrates (Schoeftner (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18157120) and yeast (Luke (2008) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19026778), and more recently in Arabidopsis (Vrbsky (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20548962).
TERRA	TelRNAs	Misc	Telomeric repeat-containing transcripts have been described in Arabidopsis. A portion of these TERRA transcripts are processed into small interfering RNAs, which contribute to the maintenance of telomeric chromatin through promoting methylation of asymmetric cytosines in telomeric (CCCTAAA)(n) repeats. This process relies on the RNA-dependent DNA methylation pathway  (Vrbsky (2010) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/20548962).
TERRA	TelRNAs	Names	TERRA: telomeric repeat-containing RNAs. TelRNAs: Telomeric RNAs 
tie-1as	None known	Characteristics	804 nucleotide, unspliced transcript, antisense to the 3' of tie1 in Zebrafish.. Tie-1as initiates just 3' of the tie-1 3'UTR, runs antisense through 3'UTR and into last exon.
tie-1as	None known	Expression	Tie1-as and tie-1 show similar developmental expression patterns with both being up-regulated after gastrulation but tie-1 expression is ~10x higher.. At 24 hours post fertilisation (hpf), tie-1 and tie-1as are both expressed in some tissues but tie1-as is also expressed in brain and otic vesicles where tie1 is not expressed.. Genomic DNA downstream from tie1 3'UTR was shown to have promoter activity supporting the presence of an antisense transcript.
tie-1as	None known	Function	Overlapping region of tie1 and tie-1as appear to duplex in-vivo, which appears to reduce levels of the tie-1 transcript.. Overexpression of Zebrafish tie-1as in-vivo caused vascular defects during zebrafish development, while over-expression of human tie-1as caused defects in endothelial cell junctions in human cells.
tie-1as	None known	Conservation	Identified in zebrafish, similar transcripts may also be present in human and mouse.
tie-1as	None known	Misc	Sequence and precise genome location of the transcripts have not been defined.
Tip1	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 1	Characteristics	Downstream of Utf1 coding gene.. No evidence of transcriptional connection between Utf1 and Tip1.
Tip1	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 1	Expression	Expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (mESCs), with H3K4me3 histone marks present at Tip1 loci. . Down-regulated upon mESC differentiation in neurons. H3K4me3 replaced with H3K27me3.
Tip1	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 1	Function	Insertion of Tip1 upstream of a luciferase reporter gene could silence the luciferase reporter in mESCs. Effect was strand independent, (orientation of Tip1 DNA sequence did not matter). However, Tip1 RNA was not necessary for this function.. Knockdown of endogenous Tip1 did not effect expression of the cis (Utf1) gene in mESCs. Knockdown was associated with the up-regulation of other genes, including Syn1, which is normally upregulated during ESC differentiation. Suggesting Tip1 has a trans-repressive function in mESCs.
Tip1	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 1	Misc	Exact transcription initiation and termination site of Tip3 not defined, so transcript could be larger than genomic region provided.
Tip3	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 3, AK050890, ENSMUSG00000092589	Characteristics	Downstream of Nkx2-9 coding gene. Appears to be independent transcript.
Tip3	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 3, AK050890, ENSMUSG00000092589	Expression	Expressed in mouse embryonic stem cells (mESCs) despite presence of H3K27me3 histone marks over Tip3 loci. . Tip3 expression increased upon mESCs differentiation to neural progenitors and then was switched off as the progenitor cells differentiated in neurons. Expression changes occurred alongside continued H3K27me3 marks at locus.
Tip3	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 3, AK050890, ENSMUSG00000092589	Function	Insertion of Tip3 upstream of a luciferase reporter gene could silence the luciferase reporter in mESCs. Effect was strand independent, (orientation of Tip3 DNA sequence did not matter). Tip3 RNA was required for silencing.. Knockdown of endogenous Tip3 did not effect expression of the cis (Nkx2-9) gene in mESCs. Knockdown was associated with the up-regulation of other genes, including Lzic and Stox2, which are normally upregulated during ESC differentiation. Suggesting Tip1 has a trans-repressive function in mESCs.
Tip3	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 3, AK050890, ENSMUSG00000092589	Conservation	Contains block of sequence conserved in most vertebrates.
Tip3	Transcribed intergenic polycomb 3, AK050890, ENSMUSG00000092589	Misc	Exact start and stop site of tip3 not defined but likely to be represented by Ak050890
TIR1axut	TIR1 antisense Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript 	Characteristics	Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript (XUT) antisense to TIR1 gene.. 5' of transcript begins in intergenic region downstream of TIR1 with 3' end overlapping TIR1 in antisense direction.
TIR1axut	TIR1 antisense Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript 	Expression	Up-regulated by Xrn1 knockout. Hence degraded by cytoplasmic Xrn1 degradation pathway.
TIR1axut	TIR1 antisense Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript 	Function	TIR1 is down-regulated upon Xrn1 inactivation. Interrupting TIR1axut expression restored most of TIR1 expression suggesting TIR1axut silences TIR1. Therefore antisense XUTs can repress the transcripts they overlap. . Full TIR1axut repression requires Set1 activity and appears to be antagonised by H3K4me3.. Nb: Currently unclear exactly how silencing is mediated by TIR1axut.
Tmevpg1	None known	Characteristics	Found within the Tmevpg3 genetic locus which controls Theiler's virus persistance/ load (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227).. Promoter contains binding sites for E2A and the Ets family of transcription factors. Suggesting regulation by transcription factors involved in the immune system (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227).. Spliced with 5 or 6 exons depending on isoform/ species (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227).
Tmevpg1	None known	Expression	In resistant mice Tmevpg1 is constitutively expressed in CD4+ and CD8+immune cells in the spleen and thymus and upon infection, by immune cells infiltrating into the CNS, however no Tmevpg1 expression was seen in susceptible mice (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227, Vigneau (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12719555).. Found in peripheral blood lymphocytes in humans with expression in NK+ cells, CD4+ and CD8+ T-lymphocytes (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227, Vigneau (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12719555).. In both mouse and humans Tmevpg1 was down-regulated upon immune cell activation with a reciprocal up-regulation in interferon gamma (Ifng) expression (Vigneau (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12719555). 
Tmevpg1	None known	Function	It has been speculated there may be a regulatory regulationship between Tmevpg1 and Ifng to explain their reciprocal expression (Vigneau (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12719555).
Tmevpg1	None known	Conservation	Present in mouse and human. Sequence conservation is limited to the promoter, first exons and its splice site, otherwise the transcripts are poorly conserved and can contain repeat elements (Vigneau (2001) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11735227).
Tmevpg1	None known	Misc	The Tmevpg3 genetic locus was found to control persistence of Theiler's virus in the central nervous system, along with the H-2D gene, this QTL locus was found to be near but exclude the interferon gamma (Ifng) gene (Bihl (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10224268).
Tmevpg1	None known	Name	Tmevpg1: Theiler's murine encephalomyelitis virus persistence candidate gene 1
TncRNA	TSU	Characteristics	~480 nuc (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482), independent transcript from the 3' end of the Neat1 short isoform/MEN epsilon.. Contains a number of sequence motifs that match binding sites for proteins involved in cytokine signalling which up-regulate MHC genes (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482). 
TncRNA	TSU	Expression	Expressed exclusively in the placenta and pancreas while full length Neat1 is expressed ubiquitously. Placenta was the only tissue where TncRNA predominated (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482). 
TncRNA	TSU	Function	Suppressed induction of MHC class II antigens by interferon gamma and partially blocked constitutive and interferon gamma induced expression of MHC class I antigens and ICAM-I (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482, Geirsson (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12565840). . Suppressed major histocompatibility (MHC) class II expression in-vitro through inhibition of class II transactivator (CIITA) promoters (Geirsson (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12565840, Geirsson (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12883198, Geirsson (2004) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15454174). Also bound STAT1 and reduced its nuclear translocation (Peyman (1999) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/9858482), contributing to suppression of MHCII and I in human trophoblast cells and hence preventing a deleterious maternal immune response to placental invasion of the uterine wall.. Note: While STAT1 binds the CIITA promoter, it's binding did not appear to be affected by TncRNA, which acted on an area with no known transcription factor binding sites (Geirsson (2003) - http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12883198), so the mechanism is unclear.
TncRNA	TSU	Misc	This transcript comes from the very 3' end of the Neat1 short isoform. It is therefore part of Neat1 but as described above appears to be expressed independently with a function different to that of the full length transcript.
TncRNA	TSU	Name	TncRNA: trophoblast noncoding RNA.. TSU: trophoblast STAT utron (untranslated region of an mRNA).

TPO1axut	TPO1 antisense Xrn1-sensitive unstable transcript 	Function	TPO1 is down-regulated upon Xrn1 inactivation, hence it is possible TPO1axut represses TPO1, similar to the action of other XUTs.
